| 4 — Intensity block | 4–8 wk | 1–3 reps | RIR 1–2 most work; occasional RIR 0 singles |
| 5 — Deload | 1 wk every 4–8 wk | — | Volume −30–50 %, intensity −10–20 % |

Cycle phases 3 → 4 → 5 to advance toward +50 kg → +75 kg → +100 kg milestones.

**Rules:**
- IF two anchor lifts per session → avoid; one anchor per session only.
- IF anchor quality is compromised → reduce secondary work first; never compromise anchor.
- IF microloading: 0.5–2.5 kg increments; at +50+ kg, even 1 kg jump ≈1.5 % — right scale.
- IF step loading: 2–3 weeks at the same load before adding weight.
- IF anterior shoulder soreness on dip descent >7–10 days → PAUSE, clinician review.
- IF elbow flexor/extensor soreness limits load >2 weeks → PAUSE, clinician review.
- IF sharp wrist or AC joint pain → PAUSE, review.
- IF strength regresses across 2 consecutive sessions despite sleep/nutrition → review.

**Practical programming numbers:**
- Sessions/lift/week: 2 (specialization), 1–2 (peaking)
- Hard sets/lift/week: 6–12 (upper end for strong recovery + clean joint history)
- Anchor working set structure: 1 top set + 1–2 back-off sets at −5–10 % load
- RIR targets: 2–3 (hypertrophy blocks), 1–2 (strength blocks), 0–1 on occasional singles (intensity blocks)
- Descent tempo: 2–3 sec controlled; no bounce on dips; no kip on pull-ups
- Return from layoff: restart at 50–60 % of prior load; add hypertrophy block before strength work; deload cycle every 4–6 wk (not 8 wk)

**Template (4-wk strength block, +60–70 kg pull / +50–60 kg dip):**
- Day 1: Weighted pull-up 1×3 at RIR 1 + 2 back-off ×4 at −10 % → Weighted dip support 3×6 at RIR 2–3 → Row 3×8 → Elbow flexor isolation 2×10
- Day 2: Weighted dip 1×3 at RIR 1 + 2 back-off ×4 at −10 % → Weighted pull-up support 3×6 at RIR 2–3 → OH press 3×6 → Triceps isolation 2×10

**Goal-agnostic note:** Phase structure and microloading logic apply to any progressive bilateral compound movement (barbell lift, ring work, etc.). Weighted pull-up/dip are illustrations of anchor-lift periodization, not defaults for all clients.

---

## Weighted Muscle-Up Programming

**PRINCIPLE:** Weighted muscle-up is a high-skill explosive compound requiring a strength surplus over the loaded version; ring and bar versions are programmed separately. (Art. 28)

**Definitions (internal):** Strength surplus principle = weighted MU requires comfortably more pulling AND pressing strength than the load on the MU itself; transition = primary technical limiter.

**Prerequisite gates:**
- Bar MU: ≥3 strict, no kip
- Ring MU: ≥3 strict false-grip reps before adding ring weight
- Weighted pull-up: +30–40 % BW × 3–5 strict reps
- Weighted dip: +40–50 % BW × 3–5 strict reps
- Transition control: slow MU transition (eccentric or paused) under control
- No anterior shoulder, biceps tendon, or wrist symptoms → IF present, PAUSE, clinician review

**Phase structure:**
| Phase | Duration | Focus |
|---|---|---|
| 1 — Strict MU consolidation | 4–8 wk | 3–5 strict reps; clean transition |
| 2 — Light weighted MU | 6–12 wk | 2.5–10 kg; 1–3 reps/set |
| 3 — Strength surplus block | 8–12 wk | Reduce MU vol; push weighted pull-up + dip; return to MU after support lifts grow |
| 4 — Heavier weighted MU | 8–12 wk | Singles and doubles; microload |
| 5 — Deload / peak | — | — |

Cycle phases 3 ↔ 4 to continually build strength surplus over loaded MU.

**Rules:**
- IF athlete cannot perform strict unloaded MU cleanly → do NOT load it.
- IF adding weighted MU to program → substitute for one weighted pull-up day, NOT added on top.
- IF DE days: separate explosive MU days from heavy dip days by ≥48 h when anterior shoulder sensitivity is a concern.
- IF anterior shoulder pain on transition >7–10 days → PAUSE, review.
- IF bar speed or technique clearly deteriorate → end set, do not push to rep target.
- Bar MU vs. ring MU: program separately; they are NOT interchangeable.

**Practical programming numbers:**
- Frequency: 1–2 sessions/week (2 only with disciplined recovery and reduced anchor lift volume)
- Sets/session: 3–6 quality sets
- Reps/set: 1–3 strict; avoid technical grinding
- RIR: 1–2 on most work; RIR 0 only on planned attempts
- Rest: 3–5 min between sets (explosive work undermined by short rest)
- Microloading: 0.5–2.5 kg jumps
- High pull specifics: pull to sternum/lower chest before initiating transition; slow transition 3–6 sec

**Template A (bar specialization):**
- Day 1: Bar MU explosive 5 singles at light–moderate load, RIR 1 → Weighted pull-up 3×4 at RIR 2 → Triceps/elbow extensor isolation 2×10
- Day 2: Slow MU transition 3×1 light → Weighted dip 3×4 at RIR 2 → High pull to sternum 3×3

**Goal-agnostic note:** Strength surplus principle and phase-gating logic apply to any complex compound skill (barbell complex, gymnastic transition). Muscle-up is an illustration only.

---

## Handstand Push-Up (HSPU) Programming

**PRINCIPLE:** HSPU is a maximal overhead press in an inverted balance-demanding position; balance, scapular upward rotation, and wrist tolerance must be built before high-rep strength work. (Art. 29)

**Definitions (internal):** Pressing frequency cap = total hard pressing sessions/week across ALL pressing patterns combined.

**Prerequisite gates:**
- Strict push-up: 20 controlled reps
- Wall handstand hold: 30–60 sec, ribs stacked, shoulders fully elevated
- Freestanding HS hold (for freestanding HSPU): 20–30 sec consistent
- Scapular upward rotation: clean overhead arm raise without anterior tilt or rib flare
- Wrist tolerance: no symptoms in deep wrist extension for 30+ sec under load
- No anterior shoulder, AC joint, or wrist symptoms → IF present, PAUSE, clinician review

**Phase structure:**
| Phase | Duration | Key variation |
|---|---|---|
| 1 — Vertical press foundations | 4–8 wk | Pike push-up, elevated pike, strict OH press |
| 2 — Wall HSPU | 4–12 wk | Build to 5–8 strict reps on wall |
| 3 — Deficit wall HSPU | 8–12 wk | Add 2–6 cm deficit; progress in 1–2 cm steps only |
| 4 — Freestanding HSPU | Variable | Requires consolidated freestanding HS |
| 5 — Loaded / higher deficit | Optional/elite | — |

**Skill progression ladder:** Pike push-up → elevated pike → wall pike → wall HSPU → deficit wall HSPU → freestanding HSPU → deficit freestanding HSPU. Add negatives at each stage.

**Rules:**
- IF stacking HSPU with planche + front-loaded carries on same day → avoid; wrist extension overload.
- IF total pressing sessions/week > 3 → reconfigure before adding HSPU.
- IF anterior shoulder pain in bottom position >7–10 days → PAUSE, clinician review.
- IF sharp wrist pain on weight-bearing → PAUSE, review.
- IF numbness/tingling in hands during/after sets → PAUSE, clinician review.
- IF wrists/shoulders feel cranky on a given day → substitute seated DB press or landmine press.
- Deficit progression: 1–2 cm steps maximum.

**Practical programming numbers:**
- Pressing frequency: 2–3 sessions/week across ALL pressing patterns combined
- HSPU hard sets/week: 6–12 (upper end only for strong shoulder tolerance)
- Sets/session: 3–5
- Reps/set: wall 3–8; deficit 3–6; freestanding 1–5
- RIR: 1–3 on most work
- Descent tempo: controlled 2–3 sec; no bouncing off head

**Template A (wall HSPU specialization):**
- Day 1: Wall HSPU 4×5 at RIR 2 → Pike push-up 3×10 → Scapular work 3×10
- Day 2: Wall HSPU negative 3×3, 4–5 sec → Strict OH press 3×5 → Wrist conditioning 2×10

**Goal-agnostic note:** Pressing frequency caps and phase structure apply to any overhead pressing goal. HSPU is an illustration; the same logic governs barbell OH press, ring pressing, etc.

---

## Front Lever and Planche Progressions

**PRINCIPLE:** Straight-arm strength scales slowly via lever-length progression; overuse is the dominant risk; short, frequent doses are superior to long, low-frequency sessions. (Art. 30)

**Definitions (internal):** Lever length progression = tuck → advanced tuck → straddle → full; microprogression gate = 3×10 sec clean holds at current lever before advancing; dose cap = 30–60 sec total quality hold time per session divided into 5–15 sec sets.

**Prerequisite gates:**
- Front lever route: strict pull-up 10 reps
- Planche route: weighted dip +25–40 % BW × 3–5 reps
- Scapular + shoulder baseline: clean scapular pulls, prone Y/T/W endurance, planche lean 30+ sec
- Wrist baseline (planche): wrist extension under load tolerated without symptoms
- No active medial or anterior elbow symptoms → IF present, PAUSE, clinician review

**Phase structure:**
| Phase | Duration | Key focus |
|---|---|---|
| 1 — Scapular/joint prep | 4–8 wk | Scapular pulls, German hangs (careful), planche leans, support holds |
| 2 — Tuck variations | 8–16 wk | Tuck FL/tuck planche holds + first dynamic reps |
| 3 — Advanced tuck + straddle | 12–24 wk | Lever length advances; volume cap maintained |
| 4 — Full position | Years | Often 2–4 yr from starting point for planche |

**Rules:**
- IF elbow or biceps tendon feels even mildly cranky → REDUCE volume 30–50 % and hold 1–2 weeks.
- IF front lever AND planche trained in same block → cap total straight-arm exposures to 2–4/week; cap session length to 15–25 min.
- IF biceps tendon discomfort persists >10–14 days → PAUSE, clinician review.
- IF OAP also in program → both share elbow flexor / biceps tendon tolerance; manage as combined exposure.
- IF heavy planche + heavy bench/dip on same day → avoid (anterior shoulder / wrist overload).
- IF heavy front lever + heavy weighted pull-up on same day → avoid (elbow flexor overload).
- IF advance lever length: gate = 3 sets × 10 sec clean holds at current lever.

**Practical programming numbers:**
- Frequency: 3–5 short sessions/week (one primary skill); 2–4 total straight-arm exposures (both skills combined)
- Hold time/session: 30–60 sec total quality holds (working lever), sets of 5–15 sec
- Dynamic work: 3–6 quality reps/session (Phase 2+); cap eccentric volume
- Recovery spacing: 24–48 h between hard straight-arm sessions per skill
- Combined planche path: tuck planche 2–4 yr to full for advanced athletes (longer for heavier athletes or elbow history)

**Template (combined, intermediate progression):**
- Mon: FL scapular pulls 3×6 → Tuck FL hold 4×10 sec → Tuck FL raise 3×5
- Tue: Planche lean 3×20 sec → Tuck planche hold 4×10 sec → Pseudo planche push-up 3×6
- Wed: Recovery
- Thu: Adv tuck FL holds 3×6 sec → Ice cream maker tuck 3×5
- Fri: Adv tuck planche holds 3×6 sec → Tuck planche push-up 3×4
- Sat: Optional light skill or rest; Sun: Rest

**Goal-agnostic note:** Lever-length progression and dose-cap logic apply to any isometric skill with increasing moment arm (flags, L-sits, ring support positions). FL/planche are illustrations only.

---

## Tendon Loading for Calisthenics (Elbows, Shoulders, Wrists)

**PRINCIPLE:** Tendons adapt over weeks to months; the correct dose is fewer hard exposures, more time, with deliberate mode sequencing: isometrics first, then HSR, then eccentrics, then progressive exposure. (Art. 31)

**Definitions (internal):** HSR (heavy slow resistance) = 3–5 sec concentric, 3–5 sec eccentric; pain monitoring threshold = 0–3/10 ache during loading that resolves within 24 h; 48–72 h spacing = minimum between hard tendon sessions per tissue.

**Tissues most exposed in advanced calisthenics:**
| Tissue | Exposed by |
|---|---|
| Common flexor tendon (medial elbow) | Pull-ups, OAP, false grip, gi grip |
| Distal biceps / biceps tendon | Front lever, OAP, supinated chin-ups, false grip |
| Common extensor tendon (lateral elbow) | Straight-arm pressing, handstand, planche |
| Anterior shoulder structures | Dips, ring dips, MU, planche |
| Supraspinatus / rotator cuff | Handstand, overhead pressing |
| Wrist flexor + extensor tendons | Handstand, planche, ring work |

**Loading mode toolkit:**
| Mode | Parameters | Use case |
|---|---|---|
| Isometrics | 20–45 sec at moderate–high intensity; 3–5 sets | Early and acute tolerance work; often more tolerable when symptoms are present |
| HSR | 3–5 sec concentric + 3–5 sec eccentric; 3–4 sets × 6–15 reps; 2–3×/wk per tissue; 48–72 h spacing | Capacity building |
| Eccentrics | 3–6 sec descent; often higher load than concentric capacity; 72–96 h spacing | High-load tolerance |
| Progressive exposure | Integration of loaded patterns at increasing intensities into skill/sport | Endpoint of tendon program |

**Rules:**
- IF initiating a tendon rebuild → start with isometrics; add HSR only after isometrics are tolerated; add eccentrics last.
- IF pain during loading is 0–3/10 and resolves within 24 h → often acceptable to continue at current dose.
- IF pain >3/10 OR does not resolve within 24 h → REDUCE load or PAUSE loading for that pattern, clinician review.
- IF pain persists at night → PAUSE, clinician review.
- IF visible swelling → PAUSE, clinician review.
- IF loss of strength in affected pattern across multiple sessions → PAUSE, clinician review.
- Tendons remember overuse: errors show up 2–4 weeks later; be conservative on load jumps.
- Each tendon mode needs 4–8 weeks to express; do NOT switch modes weekly.
- One hard tendon session per tissue per 48–72 h; two soft sessions/week may be added if tissue is tolerating well.
- Hold a load for 2–3 sessions before increasing.
- Each high-tendon-load skill (planche, FL, OAP, ring dip, false-grip) requires dedicated tendon loading either inside or alongside the skill block.
- A 1-week deload every block allows accumulated tendon load to settle.
- Rebuild timeline: 8–16 weeks for meaningful change; chronic patterns longer.
- Adaptive/return from layoff: Phase 1 isometric work extended to 12–20 wk; microload in 1–2 kg steps; coordinate with clinician.

**Template — common flexor (medial elbow) rebuild during OAP block:**
- Mon: Long-lever isometric pull 90° lockoff 3×20 sec/arm → HSR pull-up 3×8 (3 sec down, 3 sec up)
- Wed: Slow eccentric pull-up 3×4, 5 sec down → Wrist flexion HSR 3×10
- Fri: Long-lever isometric 3×20 sec/arm → Light archer pull-up 3×4/arm
- Reassess at 4–6 weeks; reduce OAP-specific work during rebuild

**Template — biceps tendon support during front lever block:**
- 2 short sessions/wk:
  - Session 1: Long-lever isometric tuck hold 3×15 sec → Supinated chin-up HSR 3×8 moderate
  - Session 2: FL raise tuck 3×5 slow → German hang 3×10 sec (if tolerated)

**Goal-agnostic note:** Tendon-loading mode sequencing and dose rules apply to ANY connective tissue bottleneck (patellar tendon, Achilles, rotator cuff). Calisthenics examples are illustrations; principles apply across goal classes.

---

## Advanced Ring Skills: Iron Cross, Hefesto, Impossible Dips

**PRINCIPLE:** Iron cross, hefesto, and impossible dips demand multi-year rings-specific foundations, conservative eccentric dosing, and assisted-route-first progression; stop rules are non-negotiable. (Art. 32)

**Definitions (internal):** Assisted route = band, pulley, or spotter assistance with measurable, progressively reduced counterweight; stop rules = absolute triggers that terminate the session regardless of plan.

**Prerequisite gates — iron cross:**
- Ring MU: 5+ clean reps
- Weighted dip: +50 % BW × 3–5 reps
- Ring support hold: 30+ sec, rings turned out, clean shape
- Straight-arm foundation: controlled back lever route, mature ring support work
- No anterior shoulder, biceps tendon, or elbow symptoms → IF present, PAUSE, clinician review

**Prerequisite gates — hefesto:**
- Equivalent to iron cross prerequisites PLUS
- Shoulder extension range with control
- Biceps tendon tolerance in extended-shoulder positions (German hang, ring skin-the-cat)
- Eccentric tolerance in pull-up patterns at high loads

**Prerequisite gates — impossible dip:**
- Strict deep ring dip, rings turned out, multiple sets of 6+
- Iron cross or near-cross hold capacity
- Pressing strength surplus over working ring dip load

**Phase structure (all three skills):**
| Phase | Duration | Focus |
|---|---|---|
| 1 — Ring strength foundation | 12+ months | MU, ring dip, support hold, back lever, FL, planche progressions |
| 2 — Straight-arm specific prep | 6–12 months | Back lever holds, cable cross exposure, partial cross eccentrics with heavy assistance |
| 3 — Assisted skill | 6–18 months | Band/pulley/spotter; progressively reduced support; eccentrics from lockout to deepest tolerated angle |
| 4 — Limited unassisted holds | Variable | Brief, supervised, spotter present |

**Skill progression ladders:**
- Iron cross: Ring support, rings turned out → straps-assist cross hold → cable cross machine → band-assisted cross hold → pulley-assisted cross (measurable counterweight) → eccentrics from support to cross → brief unassisted holds (spotter)
- Hefesto: German hang holds → skin-the-cat slow → heavily assisted hefesto eccentric → reduced assistance → assisted hefesto concentric → unassisted attempts (spotter only)
- Impossible dip: Ring dip turned out → deep ring dip → near-cross angle with band → eccentrics from support to deepest tolerated → assisted impossible dip → unassisted (supervised)

**Rules:**
- IF assistance is so low that shape breaks → exposure is too heavy; increase assistance.
- IF microloading: reduce counterweight in 1–2 kg steps; band tension reduction in small measurable increments.
- IF any stop-rule trigger occurs → terminate session immediately, clinician review.
- Iron cross iron rule: do NOT attempt without secure rings, sufficient clearance, controlled exit strategy.
- These skills are generally NOT recommended for BJJ/hybrid athletes (risk-to-transfer ratio unfavorable); only in dedicated off-season blocks if athlete insists.

**Practical programming numbers:**
- Frequency: 2–3 short sessions/week
- Working dose/session: 30–90 sec total working time at working position, divided into small sets
- Eccentric reps/session: 1–3 (with significant rest between)
- Rest: 3–5 min between sets (longer if needed)
- Spacing: 48–72 h between hard ring-specific tendon sessions

**STOP RULES (non-negotiable):**
- Sharp anterior shoulder pain on hold or descent
- Biceps tendon pain that persists >5–7 days
- Audible pop or sudden loss of strength
- Persistent pain limiting daily tasks
- Numbness, tingling, or grip weakness in the involved arm
- Any feeling of joint instability during hold

**Template — iron cross mid-progression:**
- Day 1: Ring support hold 3×15 sec turned out → Pulley-assisted cross 3×5 sec at working counterweight → Cross eccentric assisted 2×1, 4 sec descent
- Day 2: Ring strength support → Weighted dip 3×4 RIR 2 (light by athlete standard) → Back lever 3×8 sec
- Day 3: Pulley-assisted cross 3×5 sec lighter counterweight → Light skill maintenance

**Goal-agnostic note:** Assisted-route-first principle and stop rules apply to any extreme-load isometric or eccentric skill across goal classes (gymnastics, ring sport, adaptive). Iron cross/hefesto are elite-tier illustrations; most athletes will not pursue these.

---

## Conjugate Method (ME / DE / RE)

**PRINCIPLE:** Conjugate is a concurrent programming logic that rotates exercise variations to prevent accommodation while simultaneously developing maximal strength (ME), rate of force development (DE), and hypertrophy (RE). (Art. 33)

**Definitions (internal):** ME = maximum effort, RPE 8.5–10 on rotating variation; DE = dynamic effort, submaximal load moved with maximal intent (bar speed is the variable); RE = repetition effort, 6–15 reps at RIR 1–3; accommodation = plateau against a fixed variation, typically after 3–4 weeks.

**Prerequisite gates:**
- ≥12 months consistent intermediate-level loading, clean technical model on competition lifts
- Demonstrated ability to autoregulate by RPE/RIR within one notch
- GPP and structural balance floor: full-range pressing, rowing, hinging, squatting; baseline conditioning (≥15–20 min zone-2 tolerable)
- No active symptom flare limiting ROM or load in primary pattern → IF present, PAUSE ME on that pattern, clinician review

**Programming numbers:**
| Day type | Main lift | Load/intensity | Sets/reps | Rest |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| ME lower | Rotating variation (box squat, SSB, GM, rack pull, deficit DL, pin squat) | RPE 8.5–9.5, top single/double/triple | 1 top set; optional 1 back-off at 90 % of top | Full |
| ME upper | Rotating variation (CGB, board, floor, incline, football bar) | RPE 8.5–9.5 | Same as ME lower | Full |
| DE lower squat | ~50–60 % competition 1RM + 20–30 % accommodating resistance at top | 6–10×2, bar speed primary | Short (45–90 sec) | — |
| DE lower DL | 70–80 % for speed singles | 6–10×1 | Short (45–90 sec) | — |
| DE upper bench | ~45–55 % + chains/bands, rotating grips | 8–12×3 | Short (45–90 sec) | — |
| RE accessories | 4–6 movements | RIR 1–3, 3–5 sets × 6–15 reps | — | — |

**Variation rotation:** every 1–3 weeks (faster accommodators = weekly; slower = 2–3 weeks). After 3 weeks and no load progress or technical degradation → rotate.

**Wave logic for DE:** 3-week waves stepping up DE percentages from baseline to peak; reset with deload or new variation.

**If/then routing:**
- IF athlete = advanced powerlifter, low sport stress, GPP met → full conjugate, 4 days/wk (ME upper/lower + DE upper/lower)
- IF athlete = advanced strength + moderate sport stress → reduce DE set count 30–50 %; rotate ME variations every 1 week
- IF athlete = BJJ/grappling with strength goals → modified conjugate, 2 strength days/wk (ME bias + DE/RE bias); ME sessions ≥24–36 h from hard sparring
- IF athlete = hybrid with endurance demand → reduce ME to 1×/week per lower/upper; keep DE short; accept slower strength gains
- IF autoregulation degraded 2 consecutive sessions → drop ME to RPE 7 top set; hold DE percentages; do NOT introduce new variations
- IF variation used 3 weeks and top-set load stagnating or technique degrading → rotate
- IF sleep/HRV degraded 5–7 days → insert deload week before continuing
- IF weak point identified in prior testing and still the primary sticking point → bias 30–50 % of accessory volume to that pattern for next 4–8 weeks
- IF sport competition within 2–3 weeks → suspend DE squat with heaviest bands and ME DL variants with highest systemic cost
- DE bar speed drop rule: IF speed drops >10–15 % across working sets → end DE work early

**Accessory pool:** 40–60 % of weekly volume; 3–5 sets × 6–15 reps; RIR 1–3; biased to identified weak points and structural balance.

**Accommodating resistance for DE:** bands/chains should add 20–30 % of bar weight at lockout; NOT more (excessive band tension turns DE into a different lift).

**Goal-agnostic note:** Variation rotation and concurrent quality development apply across all advanced training goals (calisthenics, weighted skills, sport S&C). Powerlifting examples are illustrations only.

---

## Daily Undulating Periodization (DUP)

**PRINCIPLE:** DUP rotates the primary training quality (strength/hypertrophy/power/skill) session-to-session within the week; maintains all qualities simultaneously rather than cycling them in blocks. (Art. 34)

**Definitions (internal):** Undulating = session-to-session rotation within a week (NOT week-to-week); bracket integrity = each quality zone must remain distinct across sessions.

**Prerequisite gates:**
- ≥6–12 months consistent intermediate-level training, clean technical model
- Reliable RPE/RIR autoregulation within one notch
- GPP floor: complete planned week without symptom flare or persistent recovery debt
- No active flare in main movement pattern → IF present, route affected lift to lighter brackets, reduce volume
- Athlete tolerates 3–4 different intensity zones/week without crashing (athletes who respond poorly to variety are not DUP candidates)

**Core DUP brackets:**
| Day type | Sets × Reps | Intensity | RIR |
|---|---|---|---|
| Heavy | 3–5 × 1–5 | High (RPE 8–9 on top sets) | 0–2 top set |
| Moderate (Hypertrophy) | 3–5 × 6–10 | Moderate (RPE 7–8) | 1–3 |
| Light/Speed or Technique | 3–6 × 2–3 maximal intent, OR 3–5 × 10–15 | Submaximal, 60–75 % | 2–3 |
| Skill/Technique (optional) | — | Very low neural cost | Submaximal |

**If/then routing:**
- IF athlete = advanced strength, no sport stress → full 4-day DUP (heavy, hypertrophy, power, hypertrophy)
- IF athlete = strength + 2 sport sessions/week → 3-day DUP (heavy, hypertrophy, power)
- IF athlete = strength + 3–4 sport sessions/week → 2-day DUP (heavy, hypertrophy/power blend)
- IF athlete = hybrid with endurance → 3-day DUP; heavy day far from key endurance session; power day on active recovery slot
- IF autoregulation flags 2 sessions in a row → reduce all top sets by 1 RPE notch; keep brackets and variation
- IF specific lift stalls 2–3 weeks → vary the lift (variation rotation) but keep DUP brackets
- IF sport competition within 2–3 weeks → drop hypertrophy day to short maintenance; keep heavy and power exposures lighter
- IF sleep/HRV/readiness markers degrade 5–7 days → insert deload
- Power day bar speed drop rule: IF bar speed drops >10–15 % → end set early, reduce load next set; if persistent across deload → clinician review
- DUP block duration: 6–12 weeks typical before deload or pivot; long-term DUP continues with variation rotation + periodic deloads

**Critical integrity rule:** Heavy day ≠ hypertrophy day in disguise. Brackets must remain distinct. Do NOT let hypertrophy day creep to equal the heavy day.

**Weighted calisthenics DUP example (anchor lift = weighted pull-up):**
- Heavy: 3×3 RPE 9
- Hypertrophy: 4×8 RIR 2
- Power: banded explosive pull-up or MU technique session

**Goal-agnostic note:** DUP's bracket structure applies across all training modalities (calisthenics, powerlifting, rings, hybrid). The quality rotation principle is modality-agnostic; examples are illustrations only.

---

## Pivot Blocks and Training Stress Reorientation

**PRINCIPLE:** A pivot block is a productive 2–4 week phase that changes the dominant training stimulus when accommodation (not mere fatigue) is the limiter; deloads restore readiness against the same stimulus; pivots change the stimulus. (Art. 35)

**Definitions (internal):** Pivot = 2–4 week phase at RPE 6–8, productive intensity, different dominant variable; deload = 4–10 day reduction; accommodation = stimulus producing no new adaptation even when fresh.

**Pivot directions and trigger conditions:**
| Direction | Trigger | Mechanism |
|---|---|---|
| Intensity → volume | High recent intensity, low recent volume | Move to 6–10 reps at RIR 1–3 for 2–3 wk |
| Competition lift → variation | Grind on same pattern | Redistribute pattern-specific stress |
| Concentric → eccentric/tempo | Connective tissue fatigue | Tempo, slow eccentrics, pause variants |
| Strength → hypertrophy | Block at >80 % producing accommodation | 65–75 % for 2–3 wk, higher set volume |
| Bilateral → unilateral | Asymmetry surfaced | Redistribute to single-leg/single-arm patterns |
| Sport-stress → strength-restoration | Post-high sport load | Restore strength volume before next sport peak |

**Pivot block parameters:**
- Duration: 2–4 weeks (shorter than development block, longer than deload)
- Intensity: RPE 6–8 on most working sets; AVOID RPE 9–10
- Volume: comparable to or slightly higher than previous block, in NEW modality
- Exercise selection: variations, NOT competition lifts at competition intensities
- Exit criteria must be defined before starting: symptoms resolved + tolerance reestablished + planned duration complete

**If/then routing:**
- IF block produced no progress for 2–3 weeks AND 7-day deload did NOT restart progress → pivot block 2–3 wk
- IF athlete just completed competition or major sport event → pivot block 2–4 wk before next development block
- IF pattern-specific symptom flare in ONE lift but otherwise progressing → pivot affected lift only (variation pivot); keep other lifts in development block
- IF autoregulation reliability degraded across 2 weeks → pivot before continuing
- IF clear weak point surfaced during development block → pivot toward that weak point with biased accessory volume
- IF sleep/mood/appetite degraded 7–10 days despite normal training intensity → deload FIRST; if deload doesn't resolve → pivot
- IF approaching known sport peak in 4–6 weeks → pivot NOW toward sport-aligned stimulus; do NOT start new heavy development block
- IF no progress 2–3 wk + NOT accommodated → deload, not pivot
- Distinguish: fatigue (→ deload) vs. accommodation (→ pivot): if stimulus still working when fresh → deload; if stimulus stopped working even when fresh → pivot

**Selecting pivot direction:**
- High recent intensity, low recent volume → volume pivot
- High recent volume, decaying intensity → intensity pivot at variation lifts
- Pattern-specific symptom or asymmetry → variation or unilateral pivot
- Decaying RFD → speed/power pivot
- Tendon irritation → tempo/eccentric or isometric pivot
- General accommodation → hypertrophy pivot

**Template D (elbow flexor irritation from weighted pull-up block):**
- Duration: 3 weeks
- Replace heavy weighted pull-up → tempo strict pull-up 4×5, 3-sec eccentric, RIR 2
- Replace weighted dip → paused dip 3×6 RIR 2
- Add isometric scapular + elbow flexor holds 2–3×/wk
- Return to weighted pull-up at moderate intensity (RIR 2–3) after pivot; build back to heavy
- IF symptoms persist → clinician review

**Goal-agnostic note:** Pivot logic is universal across any training modality. The distinction between deload (readiness restoration) and pivot (stimulus change) applies equally to calisthenics, powerlifting, running, and hybrid contexts.

---

## Block Periodization — Accumulation / Intensification / Realization

**PRINCIPLE:** Block periodization sequences distinct 2–4 week phases with one dominant quality developing while others are maintained at minimum effective dose; requires honest acknowledgment of what is being de-prioritized each block. (Art. 36)

**Definitions (internal):** MEV (minimum effective dose) for maintained qualities = 1–2 short sessions/week; mesocycle = A → I → R → transition, typically 8–12 weeks.

**Block parameters:**
| Block | Duration | Intensity zone | Volume | Accessory |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Accumulation (A) | 2–4 wk | 60–75 % | High | High |
| Intensification (I) | 2–4 wk | 80–92 % | Moderate (−20–30 % vs A) | Reduced |
| Realization (R) | 1–3 wk | 90–100 % | Low, high specificity | Minimal |
| Transition (deload/pivot) | 1–2 wk | Reduced | Reduced | Structural balance |

**Sequencing rules (non-negotiable):**
1. Accumulation MUST precede intensification. Going straight to intensification from low-volume base = neural exposure without tissue tolerance.
2. Realization works ONLY after successful intensification block. Realization without intensification = deloading.
3. Transition blocks MUST follow realization. New mesocycle immediately after realization → compounding fatigue.

**12-week mesocycle for powerlifting (weeks 1–4 / 5–8 / 9–11 + wk 12 taper):**
- Wks 1–4 (A): Squat 4×8 at 70 % RIR 2; Bench 4×8 at 70 %; DL 3×6 at 70 %. Heavy accessory volume. Specialty bars dominant.
- Wks 5–8 (I): Squat 4×4 at 80–87 % RPE 8–9; Bench 4×4; DL 3×3 at 85–90 %. Accessories −20–30 %. Competition lifts dominant.
- Wks 9–11 (R): Squat 3×2 at 90–95 %; Bench similar; DL 2×1 at 90–95 %. Accessories minimal. Opener at end of wk 10 or 11.
- Wk 12: Taper + meet.
- Wks 13–14: Volume pivot.

**If/then routing:**
- IF 8–12 wk to major event → standard mesocycle (A → I → R)
- IF 4–6 wk to event → compressed mesocycle (short A → I → taper); hypertrophy gains minimal
- IF 16+ wk → two stacked mesocycles; first R phase = strength test; second R = event
- IF sport competition mid-mesocycle → adjust in-progress block to maintenance; resume with transition pivot after comp
- IF athlete in-season (regular weekly competition) → NO R blocks, NO full A blocks; 3-week mini-blocks alternating hypertrophy and strength bias at reduced volume
- IF A block producing symptom flare → reduce volume 20–30 % before reducing block duration
- IF I block top-set RPE drifts from RPE 8 → RPE 9.5 within 2 wk → extend block 1 wk at reduced loads OR pivot to different variation
- IF R block shows declining performance week-over-week → end R block early, pivot

**Hybrid grappler 12-week example:**
- Wks 1–4 (A): 2 strength sessions/wk; front squat 4×8 RIR 2, RDL 4×8, weighted pull-up 4×8; mat at base level; conditioning 2×/wk zone 2
- Wks 5–8 (I): 2 strength sessions; front squat 5×4 RPE 8.5, weighted pull-up 4×4 RPE 8; mat volume increases; conditioning adds intervals
- Wks 9–11 (R): strength reduced to 1 session/wk maintenance; sport volume peaks
- Wk 12: Taper; Wks 13–14: transition pivot

**Goal-agnostic note:** Block sequencing and quality prioritization apply across all athletic goals. The specific %1RM numbers and sport-load examples are illustrations; principles generalize to any training context requiring a competition peak.

---

## Autoregulated Load Selection (RPE / RIR / Velocity)

**PRINCIPLE:** Autoregulation adjusts daily training load to match actual athlete readiness rather than a fixed percentage chart; daily 1RM variance of 5–15 %+ is the norm, not the exception. (Art. 37)

**Definitions (internal):** RPE 10 = could not have done another rep; RPE 8 = could have done 2 more with good form; RIR 0 = RPE 10, RIR 2 = RPE 8; VBT = velocity-based training; readiness markers = sleep, HRV trend, subjective recovery, soreness, warm-up bar feel.

**RPE / RIR anchors:**
| RPE | RIR | Common use |
|---|---|---|
| 10 | 0 | Competition, max testing only |
| 9–9.5 | 0–1 | Planned heavy singles in intensity blocks |
| 8–9 | 1–2 | Top working sets, strength blocks |
| 7–8 | 2–3 | Hypertrophy blocks, back-off sets |
| 6–7 | 3+ | Deload, pivot, technique work |

**Velocity targets (general ranges; athlete-calibrate individually):**
| Lift | Power/Speed | Strength-Speed | Strength | Maximal Strength |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Squat | 0.75–1.00 m/s | 0.55–0.75 m/s | 0.35–0.55 m/s | <0.35 m/s |
| Bench | 0.75–1.00 m/s | 0.50–0.75 m/s | 0.30–0.50 m/s | <0.30 m/s |
| Deadlift | >0.50 m/s (submaximal) | — | — | <0.30 m/s (approaches maximal) |

**Readiness gating rules:**
- IF sleep <target duration by ≥90 min AND warm-up feels heavy → reduce top set by 1 RPE notch (e.g., RPE 8 → RPE 7)
- IF sleep good AND warm-up crisp → keep planned targets; optionally add top single at +1 RPE notch ONLY if planned
- IF 2 consecutive sessions show low readiness → insert deload mid-block
- IF day after hard sparring → reduce all top-set targets by 1 RPE notch
- IF within 48 h of tournament → no RPE >7 work; no new variations
- IF travel/competition stress disrupts sleep → reduce volume AND intensity proportionally

**Calibration / accuracy rules:**
- Calibration period: 4–8 weeks comparing RPE estimates to actual bar speed and AMRAP verifications
- Periodic verification: at least once per block via AMRAP at submaximal load; IF athlete predicts RIR 2 and hits 5 more reps → accuracy is off
- Cross-check: IF RPE feel decouples from bar speed → investigate fatigue, technique, or psychological state
- RPE on top set (not warm-ups); log immediately after set, not at session end
- RIR estimation cue: "If you stopped right now and rested 10 sec, how many more reps with good form?"
- Technical RPE vs. systemic RPE: grinding RPE 8 (bracing failure) ≠ clean RPE 8; only clean reps are usable training stimuli

**Programming rules:**
- Working sets prescribed as effort targets, not fixed loads: "Squat top set at RPE 8 for 3 reps"
- Load ranges provided as guides: "Expect RPE 8 ≈ 80–85 % of 1RM; adjust on the day"
- IF top set hits target reps at lower RPE than planned → optionally add weight on next set within planned ceiling, OR proceed as planned
- IF top set hits target RPE before target reps → END the set; log actual reps; do NOT push to target
- IF 2 sessions in a row show low readiness → reduce volume + intensity rest of week; plan deload
- IF readiness high but planned intensity conservative → do NOT exceed planned ceiling; ceiling protects against overshoot
- Back-off sets: prescribed as % of top set load (e.g., 90 % of top for next set)
- RIR cap: most accessory and submaximal work = RIR 1–3; top sets = RPE 8–9; singles = RPE 9–9.5; RPE 10 reserved for testing/competition
- VBT DE rule: IF velocity drops below velocity target on any set → end set early; IF consistently above target → add 2.5 kg within planned ceiling

**Goal-agnostic note:** Autoregulation applies equally to calisthenics, powerlifting, hybrid, and sport athletes. Specific velocity profiles are movement-and-athlete-specific; the RPE/RIR anchors and readiness gating logic are universal.

---

## Deloads, Resensitization, and Fatigue Dissipation

**PRINCIPLE:** Deloads are planned 4–10 day stress reductions to dissipate fatigue and restore readiness against the CURRENT stimulus; they differ from pivot blocks (which change the stimulus). (Art. 38)

**Definitions (internal):** Resensitization = restoration of adaptive response to a given stimulus after accumulated exposure; volume deload = sets reduced 40–60 %, intensity maintained; intensity deload = top sets reduced 10–20 %, volume maintained; combined deload = default for general fatigue.

**Deload types and indications:**
| Type | Volume change | Intensity change | Indication |
|---|---|---|---|
| Volume deload | −40–60 % sets | Unchanged | Connective tissue + metabolic fatigue |
| Intensity deload | Unchanged | −10–20 % (e.g., RPE 9 → RPE 7) | Neural fatigue |
| Combined | −40–60 % | −10–20 % | General fatigue (default) |
| Frequency deload | Sessions/week reduced | Unchanged | High life-stress weeks |
| Active recovery | Replace strength with light movement, mobility, low-intensity conditioning | — | High-fatigue states, transition periods |

**Deload structure (combined, default):**
- Days 1–3: Volume 50 % of normal; RPE 6–7; same movement frequency
- Days 4–7: Maintain reductions; light technical work allowed; one moderate session at end of week for athletes who decondition quickly
- Avoid: max-effort singles, AMRAPs, new variations, novel exercises causing DOMS
- Allow: light mobility, low-intensity conditioning, technique refinement at submaximal loads

**Deload frequency (standard cadence):**
- High-intensity blocks: every 3–4 weeks
- General strength blocks: every 4–6 weeks
- Hypertrophy / accumulation blocks: every 5–6 weeks
- Pre-competition: 1 deload in final week or week-before-last
- Post-competition: default 1-week deload, often extended to pivot

**If/then routing:**
- IF 4–6 weeks since last deload → schedule deload now or upcoming week
- IF readiness markers (sleep, mood, warm-up feel, bar speed) degraded 5–7 days → deload this week
- IF autoregulation accuracy degraded (RPE estimates decouple from bar speed) → deload
- IF RPE on previously-easy loads has crept upward by 1–2 notches across 2 weeks → deload
- IF pattern-specific symptom flare → PIVOT, not deload
- IF high life stress (travel, work, sleep loss) but normal training stress → preemptive deload
- IF approaching competition in 1–3 weeks → integrate deload into peaking taper
- IF returning from illness or extended layoff (>7–10 days) → first week back = deload-equivalent even if athlete feels eager
- IF 7-day deload does NOT restore readiness markers → extend 3–7 more days at same reduced loads
- IF extended deload still does not restore readiness → pivot to different stimulus; investigate sleep, nutrition, life stress
- IF 2 deloads in a row needed without development between them → coach review on program sustainability

**Deload exit criteria:**
- Readiness markers (sleep, mood, warm-up feel, bar speed) normalized → resume at planned loads
- IF not normalized after 7 days → extend or pivot

**Deload vs. pivot decision:**
| Deload when... | Pivot when... |
|---|---|
| Fatigue is general, not pattern-specific | Stimulus produced no progress for 2+ wk even when fresh |
| Current stimulus WAS producing progress until recently | Pattern-specific symptom flare requiring stimulus change |
| Sport calendar permits 4–10 day reduction | Planned transition between mesocycles |

**BJJ/grappling deload rules:**
- Schedule deload weeks to coincide with reduced SPORT volume where possible
- IF sport volume cannot be reduced → strength deload still helps but is partial
- During high-intensity sport phases → increase deload frequency for strength (every 3–4 wk vs 4–6)
- After tournament / training camp peak → default 1–2 week deload, often extending to pivot block
- Hybrid athletes: deload across BOTH modalities together when possible

**Adaptive athletes:** deload duration 7–10 days common (vs 4–7 days); frequency every 3–4 weeks; coordinate with clinicians.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Deload principles (volume, intensity, combined, frequency, active recovery categories) and routing rules apply universally across all goal classes and training modalities.

---

## Deadlift Specialization and Block Architecture

**PRINCIPLE:** Deadlift specialization is a 4–8 week block where the pull gets first priority in fatigue allocation; not a default mode — justified only when gap is large, timeline long, recovery available, pain not limiting, and technical limiter is stable. (Art. 33/Cluster C)

**Definitions (internal):** Hard top sets = work above ~80 % or RPE ≥8; junk volume = mid-% sets with no clear position, tempo, or pause intent.

**Hinge selection routing:**
- IF bar slows in first 6 inches + early back rounding → prioritize deficit pulls + lat-driven start cues
- IF bar clears knees then stalls → prioritize block pulls, glute lockouts, tempo pulls to knee
- Conventional: best for long arms relative to torso, good lumbar tolerance, symmetric hip extension
- Sumo: best for strong hip abduction/external rotation, shorter torso
- Trap bar: preferred for hybrid/grappling athletes; reduces lumbar shear; also useful secondary for competition pullers

**Volume framework:**
- Hard top sets/week (above ~80 % or RPE 8+): 2–6 for advanced lifter (varies by phase/recovery)
- Supplemental hinge volume: 65–80 % zone, position/bar path/bracing intent
- Accessory hinge (RDL, good mornings, back extensions): tracked separately; NOT counted as deadlift volume

**Intensity rotation within a mesocycle:**
| Type | Zone | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| Heavy exposure | 87–95 % | Confidence, position test |
| Speed/position | 65–80 %, strict bar speed | Bar path, eccentric tempo, or pauses |
| Capacity | 70–82 %, repeats, longer rest | Tendon + connective tolerance |

One intensity type = priority per session; stacking two = quiet fatigue accumulation.

**Specialization block structure (4–6 weeks):**
- Wks 1–2 (re-entry/position): 1 heavy day RPE 7–8 (technique); 1 supplemental hinge day (paused/tempo moderate); posterior chain accessories 2×/wk
- Wks 3–4 (load): heavy day RPE 8–9; supplemental slightly heavier (position priority); squat held at maintenance (1 day, lower volume)
- Wk 5 (load test): 1 heavy single RPE 9 (checkpoint); reduced supplemental; optional second moderate hinge if recovery permits
- Wk 6 (deload/transition): reduce hinge volume ~50 %; 1 moderate exposure; reassess

**When to specialize (multiple conditions should hold):**
- Deadlift has largest gap between current and goal
- Deadlift stalled while squat and bench progressed
- Meet/test far enough out (absorb block + normal peak)
- Recovery bandwidth available
- Technical limiter stable at heavy loads (if technique breaks down >85 % repeatably → build AROUND pull first)

**When to build around the pull instead:**
- Technical limiter unresolved at heavy loads
- Lower back, hips, or grip cannot tolerate higher hinge volume
- Squat also priority and progressing
- Meet window too short for full specialization before peaking
- Recovery compromised

**Fatigue triggers inside block:**
- Bar speed drops 2 RPE points week-over-week at same load → pull brakes (cut supplemental, not main)
- Sleep below usual floor >2 nights/week
- Grip endurance collapses on previously-easy supplemental work
- Morning posterior chain stiffness persists past warm-up 2 sessions in a row

**Substitution rules:**
- IF conventional breaks down → route to trap bar or block pulls for 2 wk; keep supplemental on competition-style hinge at lighter loads
- IF grip is limiter → straps on supplemental; protect hook grip for top sets
- IF lumbar tolerance drops mid-block → elevated pulls 1 wk; position-focused supplemental; review before reloading

**Goal-agnostic note:** Block architecture, intensity rotation, and fatigue trigger logic apply to any primary pattern specialization. Deadlift is the illustration; same rules apply to squat, bench, ring skill, etc.

---

## Squat Specialization for Advanced Lifters

**PRINCIPLE:** Squat responds to frequency (2–4×/wk) before volume; structured frequency with distinct session hierarchy (primary/secondary/technique) outperforms same volume in 1–2 sessions. (Art. 34/Cluster C)

**Frequency design:**
- Day A (primary): main squat variation, top sets RPE 8–9; 1–2 back-off sets, strict tempo or pause
- Day B (secondary): variation biasing weak point (pause, tempo, different bar); top sets RPE 7–8, more total reps
- Day C (technique/capacity): lighter variation RPE 6–7, position + bar speed + brace; higher set count, lower per-set intensity
- Optional Day D: <65 % for 3–5 rep pattern work only

**Hard squat sets/week above ~80 % or RPE 8:** 4–10 for advanced lifter (main + secondary days carry most); rest distributed as supplemental + capacity.

**Variation selection (hold 2–3 per block):**
| Variation | Targets |
|---|---|
| Pause squat | Brace + control out of hole |
| Tempo squat | Eccentric control, hypertrophy |
| High bar | Knee/quad emphasis (quad is limiter) |
| Low bar | Hip/posterior chain (back angle limiter) |
| Front squat | Upper back, brace, quad position |
| Safety bar | Upper back load reduced (shoulder/elbow constraint) |
| Box squat | Reduce range; hip emphasis |

**Fatigue signals (2+ in same week → cut supplemental or reduce Day B intensity):**
- Warm-ups feel heavier than usual at same load
- Knee/hip stiffness persists longer into session
- Bar speed drops at top set without load change
- Sleep quality slips after main squat day

**Substitutions:**
- Knee tolerance drops → box squats or tempo to higher box 1–2 wk; review before reloading
- Hip tolerance drops → narrow stance or front squat for defined window
- Upper back limiter → safety bar or front squat to maintain frequency without barbell across upper back

---

## Bench Press Specialization

**PRINCIPLE:** Bench specialization raises frequency (3–4 pressing days/week), structures volume by purpose, and manages shoulder tolerance — which is the true ceiling, not pec strength. (Art. 35/Cluster C)

**Frequency design:**
- Day A (primary): competition-style bench, top sets RPE 8–9; back-off sets strict tempo/pause
- Day B (secondary): variation biasing weak point (CGB, paused, spoto, board); top sets RPE 7–8, more total reps
- Day C (volume): lighter pressing RPE 6–7, different grip/bar, higher set count, bar path focus
- Day D (optional): DB pressing or incline at moderate load (when shoulder tolerance is high)

**Hard pressing sets/week above ~80 % or RPE 8:** 6–12 (distributed across primary and secondary days; volume day adds capacity but must not push primary/secondary into debt).

**Variation menu:**
| Variation | Function |
|---|---|
| Paused bench | Bar control, tightness off chest, leg drive timing |
| Spoto press | Position at hardest point of bar path (brief pause above chest) |
| Close-grip bench | Triceps + lockout; reduces shoulder load for some lifters |
| Board press | Lockout + overload above sticking point |
| Larsen press (feet up) | Removes leg drive; upper back stability + pec contribution |
| DB bench | Shoulder-friendly volume, ROM, stabilizer work |

**Lockout failure diagnosis (not "add triceps volume" by default):**
- Bar drifts forward at top → upper back gave up
- Bar drifts back → leg drive timed late
- Genuine triceps gap → close grip + board work

**Shoulder tolerance rules:**
- Upper back volume: 2–3×/wk horizontal pulling + external rotation work
- Grip width + elbow flare: adjusted to keep shoulder in tolerable arc
- IF shoulder talks during warm-ups → change variation that day OR shorten session
- Pulling volume should rise proportionally with pressing volume

---

## Overhead Press Development

**PRINCIPLE:** Strict press, push press, and shoulder capacity work are three separate jobs; horizontal pulling volume must match or exceed pressing volume across the week. (Art. 36/Cluster C)

**Programming numbers:**
- Strict press (priority): top sets 3–6 reps at RPE 7–9, 2–3×/wk
- Push press: top sets 2–5 reps at RPE 7–9; use when overhead strength needed above strict press capacity
- Hard overhead sets/week above ~80 % or RPE 8 (overhead as priority): 3–8

**Capacity work (non-negotiable, not a warm-up):**
- Vertical pressing accessories: half-kneeling press, single-arm DB press, Z-press
- Horizontal pulling: volume ≥ pressing volume across week
- External rotation: band/cable/DB, 2–3 exposures/wk
- Scapular work: serratus push-ups, prone Y/T, scapular pull-ups

**Decision rules:**
- IF goal = competition powerlifting, bench is priority → overhead is supplemental, 1–2×/wk moderate
- IF goal = hybrid performance → overhead can equal bench, 2–3×/wk
- IF shoulder sensitive → drop overhead frequency FIRST (before bench frequency)

---

## Heavy Singles in Training

**PRINCIPLE:** A heavy single is a training tool confirming that a load is movable at a known RPE on a given day; NOT a PR attempt; NOT the most efficient strength-building tool. (Art. 37/Cluster C)

**Frequency and dosing:**
- 1 heavy single/week on ONE lift, rotated across a block = sustainable for most advanced lifters
- 2 heavy singles/week on DIFFERENT lifts = upper limit; only with good sleep and low life stress
- 3 lifts heavy single same week = reserved for peaking; rare outside that context

**RPE targets for training singles:** RPE 8–9 (NOT RPE 10 in regular training; RPE 10 reserved for testing/competition).

**If/then routing on the day:**
- IF planned single misses, technique CLEAN, bar speed too slow → drop load 5–10 %, complete working single; block continues normally next week
- IF technique BROKE DOWN at the single → end heavy work; review video; do NOT retry at same load
- IF something feels off not matching recent training → pause heavy work; complete moderate supplemental or end session; reassess

**Fatigue triggers (pull singles from the week):**
- Bar speed on warm-up sets noticeably slower than baseline
- Heart rate/perceived exertion at warm-up loads higher than usual
- Sleep below athlete's floor in last 2 nights
- Mood + focus flat (recognized fatigue signal)
- Substitute: doubles or triples at planned single's RPE −1

**BJJ/hybrid rules:**
- Max 1 heavy single/week during in-season
- Avoid within 48 h before hard rolling day or competition simulation
- Serve mostly as readiness checks, not progression drivers, during hard mat blocks

---

## Weak Point Training for Powerlifting

**PRINCIPLE:** Weak point = specific position, range, or pattern where bar consistently slows or fails on HEAVIEST sets; identified from 3 evidence sources (video + bar speed + failure pattern), NOT from next-day soreness. (Art. 38/Cluster C)

**Identification method (requires 3 sources to agree):**
1. Video on top sets (NOT working sets — working sets hide the limiter)
2. Bar speed on top sets (deceleration timing identifies range)
3. Failure pattern (where missed reps actually fail: off chest / mid-range / lockout for bench; hole / mid-range / top for squat; floor / knee / lockout for deadlift)

**Weak point → standard response matrix:**
| Lift | Failure range | First response |
|---|---|---|
| Bench — off chest | Paused bench, spoto press, upper back + pec mass | — |
| Bench — mid-range | Paused bench heavier, CGB, upper back tightness | — |
| Bench — lockout | CGB, board press, triceps accessories, bar path review | — |
| Squat — hole | Pause squat, tempo squat, quad/hip mass | — |
| Squat — mid-range | Tempo squat, posterior chain, brace under heavier loads | — |
| Squat — lockout | Good mornings, hip thrust (usually a back angle / hip extension issue) | — |
| DL — off floor | Deficit pulls, lat tension cues, slow eccentric RDL, glute/quad development | — |
| DL — at knee | Tempo pulls to knee, paused pulls below knee, posterior chain hypertrophy | — |
| DL — lockout | Block pulls, glute bridges, hip thrusts, upper back, lockout accessories | — |

**Hidden limiter check:** IF obvious strength interventions not changing bar speed at top sets → consider TOLERANCE as limiter (athlete subconsciously protecting a historically sensitive region); route accordingly.

**Programming rules:**
- Weak point work: ADDED to program, NOT substituted for main lift
- Volume: 2–4 hard sets/wk, moderate intensity with constraint (pause/tempo/partial range)
- Minimum hold time: ≥4 weeks before judging; remove when bar speed/position evidence confirms change
- IF weak point variation triggers NEW pain → pause, reassess limiter, clinician review

---

## Powerlifting Peak Week

**PRINCIPLE:** Peak week is the controlled removal of fatigue at a rate exceeding fitness loss; goal = express developed capacity, not build more strength. (Art. 39/Cluster C+D)

**Prerequisites before committing to taper:**
- Top sets hit prescribed RPE ≤8 in last 2 heavy sessions of block
- Bar speed at opener weight unambiguous and crisp (not grinding)
- Sleep/bodyweight/resting HR inside normal band
- No new joint pain altering technique in last 14 days
- Competition technique (commands, pause length, depth standard) rehearsed under load

**7-day peak week template (Saturday meet):**
| Day | Session content |
|---|---|
| Monday (8 days out) | Squat opener single @ RPE 7 + Bench opener −5–10 kg single @ RPE 7; light 1 upper back + 1 triceps movement; total session <75 min |
| Tue or Wed | DL: opener −10–15 kg single, stop; optional light bench technique 3×3 @ 60 %, leg drive + bar path; no back-off sets; no top sets >RPE 7 |
| Thursday | Squat 2–3 singles @ 60–70 %, slow eccentric + fast concentric, command timing practice; Bench 2–3 singles @ 60–70 %, pause practice |
| Friday | Optional empty bar to mid-50 %, 5–10 min movement then stop; OR full rest |
| Saturday | Compete |

**Volume tapering (final 2 weeks):**
- 2 weeks out: volume −30–50 % vs previous high week; intensity preserved on top sets
- 1 week out: volume −50 % of 2-weeks-out level; top sets backed off in intensity
- Peak week: openers serve as main intensity exposure

**Bar speed decision rules during peak week:**
- IF opener speed Monday is FASTER than block average → hold plan
- IF opener speed EQUAL to block average → hold plan but drop 1 accessory
- IF opener speed VISIBLY SLOWER → cut Tue/Wed DL single to 70 % double @ RPE 6; skip mid-week back work entirely
- "Heavy feel" with normal speed on video → trust video, not feel (peak-week perception of heaviness is normal)

**Fatigue triggers (changes the plan if 2+ appear within 7 days of meet):**
- 2+ nights sub-baseline sleep
- Resting HR elevated ≥8 % over 3-day rolling mean
- New low-back stiffness on first morning movement not clearing after warm-up by Wednesday
- Bar path drift on bench at sub-maximal loads
- Loss of appetite or unintended weight drop beyond planned cut
- Action: drop second heavy session; keep skill work only; reassess Thursday

**Powerlifting-specific timing:**
- Squat: earlier volume reduction (~10 days out); skill singles held longer
- Bench: holds small dose of frequency deeper into peak week (bench tolerates volume better)
- Deadlift: last heavy touch 10–12 days out; peak week ≤1 moderate single
- Sumo: often needs extra recovery day → move DL single to Monday (not Tuesday)

**BJJ/hybrid during peak week:**
- Drop live rolling 10 days out
- Technical drilling (no resistance) through Wednesday
- Stop ALL mat work by Thursday
- Resume rolling ≥5–7 days post-meet; restore intensity gradually

---

## Attempt Selection (Powerlifting)

**PRINCIPLE:** Attempt selection is risk management under partial information; primary rule = avoid bombing out; conservative opener is non-negotiable. (Art. 40/Cluster C+D)

**Opener anchors:**
| Lift | Opener as % of realistic 3rd attempt |
|---|---|
| Squat | 90–93 % |
| Bench | 91–94 % |
| Deadlift (conventional) | 88–92 % |
| Deadlift (sumo) | 89–91 % |

Opener = confident gym triple converted to single OR these %s of planned 3rd. Speed should look FAST on warm-up video. Feel = "moderate single."

**Second attempt logic:**
- Planned jump: 4–7 % above opener (squat/bench); 3–5 % above opener (deadlift)
- Target feel: RPE 8.5–9 at most
- IF opener moved expected/better speed → second = planned number
- IF opener noticeably slower → second = planned jump halved (e.g., 10 kg → 5 kg jump)
- IF opener was a grind → smallest legal jump; protect the lift; decide third on second performance
- IF opener missed → re-take opener (do NOT lower unless the miss was strength not technique)

**Third attempt logic:**
- Total builder: 2–4 % above second; high but not guaranteed probability; default choice
- PR attempt: only when total is SECURE + meet position justifies risk; coach decision (not athlete decision)
- IF second missed on strength → third = opener + smallest meaningful jump (total preservation priority)
- IF second missed on technique → re-take second
- IF second moved unexpectedly well → increase third by ≤2–3 % over originally planned third; do NOT invent a new PR number

**Hybrid/BJJ modifications:**
- Openers: more conservative, near 92–94 % of recent best gym single
- Seconds: match recent confident gym single (not stretch target)
- Thirds: total-builder style by default; save PR chasing for strength-only block

---

## 1RM Testing Protocol

**PRINCIPLE:** 1RM testing is expensive; default to the lowest-cost modality that answers the actual programming question; never test inside 8 weeks of a planned meet. (Art. 41/Cluster D)

**Testing modalities ranked by recovery cost:**
| Modality | Recovery time | Best use |
|---|---|---|
| True 1RM single | 7–10 days (DL longer) | Highest validity for meet prediction |
| Top single @ RPE 9 | 5–7 days | Calibrating peaking block within 12–16 wk of meet |
| Heavy triple/double @ RPE 8–9 + estimation | 3–5 days | Most programming decisions (lower accuracy at extreme top end) |

**Testing day protocol (one lift):**
- General warm-up: 8–12 min
- Empty bar: 2×5 technique
- 40 %: 5 reps → 55 %: 3 reps → 70 %: 2 reps → 80 %: 1 rep → 88 %: 1 rep → 93 %: 1 rep → 97–100 %: planned top single → Optional 101–103 %: only if prior single moved with CLEAR bar speed + NO technical breakdown
- STOP on first missed lift, slow grind, or technical breakdown; do NOT chase

**Decision rules during test:**
- IF 93 % single grinds → planned top = final single; no jump above it
- IF 88 % single moves slowly → drop planned top to 95 %
- IF bar speed at top single unexpectedly fast → 2–3 % jump allowed IF athlete in good state AND lift technically clean
- IF technique breaks at any point → prior lift before breakdown = test result

**Post-test window (5–7 days after true 1RM):**
- No top sets above RPE 7 on tested lift
- Volume on tested lift: 60–70 %, technique focus
- Other lifts: normal intensity; systemic carryover expected 48–72 h
- IF two lifts tested in same week → reduced-intensity full week behind both
- Triple-lift testing in one week: rarely justified; routinely costs more than it informs

**If/then routing after the test:**
- IF confirmed expected numbers → program next block off new training max
- IF exceeded expectations → program off original projected number (NOT new number); banked progress more durable than chased
- IF underperformed → do NOT raise volume to compensate; examine sleep, stress, technical pattern, block design
- IF technical miss but load was completable → re-test with technique fix in 7–10 days at SAME load (not above)

---

## Post-Meet Recovery: 3-Phase Rebuild

**PRINCIPLE:** Post-meet recovery has 3 phases (decompression → re-introduction → rebuild); athlete will feel better at day 3 than they actually are; premature intensity restoration costs the next block. (Art. 43/Cluster D)

**Phase structure:**
| Phase | Days | Load / Content |
|---|---|---|
| 1 — Decompression | 0–7 | Days 0–2: no barbell; walking, light cycling, mobility. Days 3–5: empty bar to 40 % on competition lifts (optional). Days 5–7: optional light upper/lower accessory at low RPE. |
| 2 — Re-introduction | 7–14 | 3–4 sessions; competition lifts 60–70 % × 3–5 at RPE 6; 1 accessory/muscle group moderate volume; NO top singles, NO max effort, NO grinders. |
| 3 — Rebuild | 14–28 | Wk 1: top sets RPE 7 × 3–5; Wk 2: top sets RPE 7.5–8 × 1–3; End: confident heavy single RPE 8 on one lift to confirm training max |

**End-of-Phase-2 check:** athlete moving cleanly at 70 % on ALL three lifts → enter Phase 3. IF not → hold Phase 2 one more week.

**If/then routing:**
- IF persistent low-back stiffness past day 5 → keep Phase 1 longer; add walking + breath-driven mobility; no barbell pulling until clear
- IF joint pattern that bothered athlete during block RETURNS in Phase 2 → pause + clinician review; do NOT push to Phase 3
- IF athlete flat through Phase 2 into Phase 3 → extend Phase 2 by 1 week (premature Phase 3 makes next block harder)

**Deadlift-specific:** re-introduce DL after squat in Phase 2; first DL session = paused DL at 50–60 %, focused on setup/break, NOT load.

**BJJ/hybrid post-meet:**
- No live rolling for ≥5–7 days
- Technical drilling (low intensity) resumes Phase 1 days 4–5
- Light rolling (controlled pace) in Phase 2 days 8–14
- Full-intensity rolling ≥Phase 3 only

---

## Strength Building vs. Strength Expression (Block Type Decision)

**PRINCIPLE:** Build blocks and expression blocks have different inputs, volume distributions, and success criteria; treating a peak block like a build block → flat meet day; treating a build block like a peak → stalled cycle. (Art. 44/Cluster D)

**Characteristic comparison:**
| Dimension | Build block | Expression block |
|---|---|---|
| Total volume | Higher | Lower |
| Intensity zone | 70–85 % | 85–95 % |
| Top-set RPE | 7–9 | 7–8.5 |
| Accessory work | High, weak-point targeting | Reduced; minimize eccentric load accessories |
| Primary signal | Top-set RPE vs. plan; volume tolerance | Bar speed at sub-maximal loads; single-rep technique; subjective sharpness |
| Accumulated fatigue | Intentional, managed | Actively shed week-over-week |
| Grinders | Normal | Red flag |

**Block type decision rules:**
- IF competition within 12 weeks → block within 4–6 weeks of meet = expression block; prior block = build transitioning to expression
- IF returning from layoff or missed cycle → next block = BUILD regardless of calendar pressure
- IF plateau >2 consecutive cycles → next block = BUILD with significant changes (volume, frequency, exercise selection, rest)
- IF within 2 weeks of meet → PEAK WEEK; nothing should resemble a build block

**If/then routing inside a block:**
- IF build block produces sharp readiness early → hold the build; time is not right to collapse into expression
- IF build block produces persistent fatigue late → shorten by 1 week; brief expression block before next build
- IF expression block produces grinders → cut second heavy session; re-evaluate opener; do NOT chase planned numbers
- IF expression block produces unexpectedly fast singles → do NOT raise meet numbers beyond planned 3rd attempt

**Powerlifting long-term ratio:** ~70–80 % of year in build blocks; 2–3 expression blocks/year culminating in meets.

**Hybrid athletes:**
- Use shorter build blocks (3–5 weeks) + brief reset week vs. longer build blocks
- Time expression blocks with REDUCED mat volume
- Avoid full expression blocks during tournament prep (that block belongs to the mat)

---

## GPP for Advanced Strength Athletes

**PRINCIPLE:** GPP is the minimum dose of targeted support work that raises the athlete's absorptive, recovery, and repeatability capacity without cannibalizing the priority session. (Art. 45)

**GPP vs. SPP:** IF exercise looks like the sport → SPP. IF shares energy system or tissue demand but NOT the pattern → GPP. IF shares neither → restoration or play.

**Junk GPP criteria (avoid if ANY of these is true):**
- Does not address a real limiter
- Costs more recovery than gain returned
- Cannibalizes the priority session that follows

**Dosing rules:**
- Place GPP after priority session, on a lower CNS day, OR as a short separate session
- Do NOT pile loaded carries onto a max-effort squat day if athlete is already cooked
- Cap sled/carry volume so the next priority session remains intact
- Use unilateral and trunk-stiffness work as low-cost, high-yield GPP

**If/then routing:**
- IF athlete in peak block → strip GPP to short alactic taps + easy aerobic flushes only
- IF athlete in accumulation block → expand GPP to loaded carries, sled work, zone-2
- IF grip is the limiter → move grip GPP off lifting days to separate short blocks
- IF athlete reports stacked fatigue across 2 sessions → cut GPP volume BEFORE cutting SPP

**Templates (scalable):**
- After-lift tail: 8–12 min; sled push + easy carry + trunk anti-rotation; moderate HR
- Separate aerobic session: 30–45 min zone-2 bike or rower; nasal breathing if tolerated
- Capacity circuit: 3 rounds; loaded carry + sandbag pickup to shoulder + controlled step-ups; long rests, clean reps

---

## Conditioning for Strength Athletes — Energy System Taxonomy

**PRINCIPLE:** Aerobic base is the most commonly missing layer in advanced strength programs; it raises between-set recovery and overall work tolerance; threshold work is only for hybrid/sport athletes, not classical powerlifters. (Art. 46)

**Conditioning taxonomy:**
| Layer | Work:Rest | Duration | Primary benefit for strength athletes |
|---|---|---|---|
| Alactic power | 5–10 sec work : 2–4 min rest | Short | Supports peak-effort lifts and short bursts; cheap on recovery if dosed correctly |
| Alactic capacity | 10–20 sec work : 60–90 sec rest | Short blocks | Helpful for strongman repeated-effort events |
| Aerobic base (Zone 2) | Continuous | 20–60 min | Missing layer in most programs; raises between-set recovery and work tolerance |
| Tempo/extensive intervals | Moderate sub-threshold | — | Cleans up between-session recovery; body composition support |
| Threshold | — | — | Only for hybrid/sport; skip for pure strength athletes |
| Restoration | Easy | 20+ min | Recovery flush |

**Dosing templates for advanced strength athlete neglecting conditioning:**
- Zone 2: 2 sessions/week × 30–45 min; low-impact tool
- Alactic: 1 session every 7–14 days during off-season; 6–8 efforts × 5–8 sec; full recovery
- Tempo/extensive intervals: 1×/week if work capacity is clear bottleneck; pull back as meet approaches

**If/then routing:**
- IF ≥12 wk from meet → aerobic base is priority
- IF 4–8 wk out → taper conditioning to maintenance
- IF peak week → strip to walks and very easy spins
- IF cold hands/feet, slow warm-ups, slow between-set recovery → aerobic base is limiter
- IF sport is strongman → add alactic capacity work mirroring event timing

**Fatigue triggers:**
- Morning resting HR elevated >5–7 beats over baseline for several days → reduce conditioning intensity
- Lift performance dropping with high subjective fatigue → check conditioning overlap
- Sleep onset delayed after evening intervals → move conditioning earlier

---

## Conditioning for Grappling and MMA

**PRINCIPLE:** Grappling/MMA are repeated near-maximal efforts over rounds; aerobic base is the foundation for round recovery; alactic capacity addresses repeated scramble quality; sport-specific intervals mirror actual round structure. (Art. 47)

**Combat conditioning taxonomy:**
| Layer | Tool / Protocol | Primary role |
|---|---|---|
| Aerobic base | Easy bike/ski erg/swim/sled walks; long duration | Foundation; recovery between rounds and sessions |
| Tempo/extensive intervals | Bike, rower, ski erg; moderate sub-threshold | Bridge base to sport |
| Alactic power | 10 sec hard : 20 sec easy × 8–12 rounds (bike/ski erg) | Scramble bursts, entries |
| Alactic capacity | 30 sec hard : 30 sec easy × 6–10 rounds | Repeated effort within a round |
| Sport-specific intervals | 5-min mixed-effort round × 2–5, 1 min rest; sandbag medleys | Round-specific conditioning transfer |
| Restoration | Easy bike, walking, mobility, pool flush | Critical given high mat volume |

**Hard sparring cap:** ≤2 sessions/week in most blocks. Hard sparring IS conditioning whether the athlete counts it or not.

**If/then routing:**
- IF sparring day is heavy → no additional hard conditioning same day
- IF comp >8 wk out → aerobic base in foreground
- IF comp 4 wk out → sport-specific round intervals dominate
- IF comp 1–2 wk out → taper; short alactic taps + easy aerobic flushes only
- IF grip + neck fried → move grip-heavy GPP off schedule; use bike or ski erg instead of ropes + carries

**Scheduling rules:**
- Same-day consolidation: pair conditioning WITH mat work to protect off days
- Lower CNS days carry aerobic base
- Strength sessions on highest-energy day available
- ≥1 genuine rest day non-negotiable

---

## Conditioning for Hybrid Athletes (Concurrent Training)

**PRINCIPLE:** Hybrid athletes risk doing every quality enough to be tired, not enough to improve; the coach must defend each quality with the smallest cost to others; interference is real and manageable, not deniable. (Art. 48)

**Interference management rules:**
- Separate sessions by ≥6 hours where possible
- Strength BEFORE endurance when both in one day (unless skill is priority)
- Avoid hard running the day after heavy squat day → use bike/ski erg/pool instead
- Trunk fatigue + grip fatigue limit subsequent sessions; plan around them

**If/then routing:**
- IF next event = endurance event → endurance is priority; strength shifts to 2 short maintenance sessions/week
- IF next event = strength event → strength is priority; endurance shifts to 2 zone-2 sessions + short tempo/interval
- IF both seasons overlap → alternate which quality leads each microcycle
- IF persistent stiffness/pain after high running week → switch to low-impact aerobic tools; review form

**Taper for hybrid athletes:**
- Cut interval + threshold volume FIRST
- Keep alactic and easy aerobic for sharpness

---

## Loaded Carries, Sleds, and Medleys

**PRINCIPLE:** Loaded carries/sleds/medleys simultaneously build trunk stiffness, work capacity, and joint-friendly conditioning; select tool by the athlete's limiting structure, not by preference. (Art. 49)

**Tool selection by limiting structure:**
| Limiting structure | Preferred tools |
|---|---|
| Trunk stiffness | Suitcase carry, yoke (if tolerated), sled push |
| Scapular control | Unilateral carries, controlled rowing, throw progressions |
| Hip capacity | Sled push, low box step-ups, A/B skips |
| Knee tolerance | Backward sled drag, bike, pool, low box work |
| Foot/ankle limited | Pool, bike, controlled pogos only when tolerated |
| Neck + grip limited (grapplers) | Bike or rower over rope + carry; reduce grip GPP |

**Dosing rules:**
- Place after priority lift or on separate lower CNS day
- 1–2 tools per session; avoid medley buffet
- Trunk emphasis: heavier load, shorter distance, slower walk
- Capacity emphasis: moderate load, longer distance/time, controlled pace
- Event prep: match event time and load

**Templates:**
- Trunk biased: 3 rounds; heavy suitcase carry 20 m/side, walk back, 60–90 sec rest
- Capacity biased: 4–6 rounds; sled push 20 m + walk back; moderate load, low rest
- Event biased: 2–4 sets at competition distance/load/cadence

---

## Plyometrics and Medicine Ball Power

**PRINCIPLE:** Plyometrics maintain rate of force development and bridge slow strength to fast sport expression; they are NOT conditioning; dosed as conditioning, they fail at both jobs. (Art. 50)

**Progression ladder:**
1. Landing mechanics (step off low box, soft landing, freeze)
2. Pogo hops (stiff ankle, short ground contact)
3. Skips (A skip, B skip)
4. Broad jump + box jump (concentric biased, cheap on CNS)
5. Bounds (single-leg power, higher demand)
6. Depth + drop jumps (reactive; earn this; higher CNS cost)
7. Med ball throws (linear + rotational)
8. Contrast pairs (heavy lift + short plyo; 3–5 min rest between pairs)

**Med ball work:**
- Chest pass: upper body horizontal power
- Overhead slam: trunk-to-floor power
- Rotational throw: hip-to-shoulder transfer (critical for grapplers, strikers, throwers)
- Scoop throw: posterior chain to anterior chain transfer
- Sets: 2–5 reps, full intent, full recovery

**Dosing rules:**
- Non-impact plyos: 20–50 contacts/session for advanced athletes who lift heavy
- Depth + drop jumps: 10–20 contacts/session, rarely more
- Place plyos EARLY in session (fresh, not fatigued)
- Contrast pairs: 3–5 min rest between pairs

**If/then routing:**
- IF landing mechanics not clean → NO depth or drop jumps; stay at pogos/skips/broad jumps
- IF athlete in peak strength week → 1–2 short plyo/throw sets for sharpness only
- IF sport = rotational → prioritize rotational med ball work over linear jumps
- IF knee/foot pain → strip impact plyos; use med ball + seated rotational throws
- IF CNS fried → skip depth jump session; light pogos as priming only

---

## GPP Decision Rules and Routing Matrix

**PRINCIPLE:** GPP selection is a five-question filter; the priority quality gets the cleanest day; GPP supports it, never crowds it; when in doubt, do less. (Art. 52)

**Five-question filter (answer before assigning any GPP/conditioning):**
1. What is the priority quality for this block?
2. What is the limiting structure right now?
3. What is the fatigue budget left after priority work?
4. Which equipment and modality is pain tolerant?
5. What does the calendar require in the next 4 weeks?

**Quality-to-tool matrix:**
| Quality | Primary tools |
|---|---|
| Aerobic base | Bike, rower, ski erg, easy swim, sled walks, hills at easy pace |
| Tempo/extensive intervals | Bike, rower, ski erg, runs (tolerant athletes) |
| Alactic power | Short hill sprints, bike/ski erg sprints, broad jumps, throws |
| Alactic capacity | Short bike intervals, repeated short hills, battle ropes, sandbag bursts |
| Sport-specific intervals | Round-timed work (combat), event mimic (strongman) |
| Loaded GPP | Sled, prowler, yoke, carries, medleys |
| Plyometrics | Pogos, skips, broad/box jumps, bounds, depth jumps, throws |
| Restoration | Walks, easy bike, mobility, pool flush |

**Six mandatory decision rules:**
1. Priority quality gets cleanest day; GPP supports, never crowds
2. IF two GPP pieces compete for same tissue → drop one
3. Loaded GPP + heavy lower work do NOT share a day at full dose
4. Hard intervals + heavy lower work do NOT share a day at full dose
5. Skill + sport sessions come before GPP in day order
6. When in doubt, do less; capacity from repeatable weeks, not hero sessions

**Athlete-type GPP profiles:**
| Athlete type | GPP prescription |
|---|---|
| Advanced powerlifter | 2 zone-2 sessions + 1 short loaded carry tail + optional plyo priming + restoration |
| Strongman | Event mimic medleys + 1 zone-2 + 1 alactic capacity + restoration |
| BJJ competitor | 2 zone-2 + 1 sport-specific interval (co-scheduled with mat) + light plyo/throw + careful grip/neck management |
| MMA | Sport-specific round intervals + 2 zone-2 + light alactic + careful sparring count |
| Calisthenics/gymnastics | Scapular + trunk-biased carries + low-impact aerobic base + restorative pool + careful plyo dosing |
| Hybrid athlete | Priority quality drives calendar; other quality at maintenance |

**Pre-competition GPP taper:**
- 2–3 weeks out: cut interval volume; keep alactic taps + easy aerobic
- 1 week out: walks, very easy spins, sharp short throws/jumps, technique only
- Day before: movement and rest

**Goal-agnostic note:** The five-question filter and six decision rules apply universally across all goal classes. Athlete-type profiles are routing illustrations, not defaults.

---

*End of v10.9 Part 2 distillation (Articles 26–51)*

## PART C — GPP, Injury Management, Volume Thresholds & Nutrition (Articles 52–78)

## Articles 52–78 | Clusters E/F/G/H
### GPP Decision Rules · Combat Strength · Volume Thresholds · Nutrition

---

## 1. GPP Decision Rules

**PRINCIPLE:** GPP selection is routed through a five-question priority filter before any tool is added; GPP supports the priority quality and never competes with it. (Art. 52)

**Definitions (internal):** Priority quality = the target adaptation for the block. Limiting structure = the anatomical or physiological bottleneck currently constraining GPP selection. Fatigue budget = recoverable capacity remaining after priority work is accounted for.

**Rules:**
- IF two tools compete for the same tissue → drop one entirely.
- IF loaded GPP and heavy lower work are planned same day → drop one to zero; no full-dose stacking.
- IF hard intervals and heavy lower work are planned same day → same rule; not shareable at full dose.
- IF skill/sport sessions are in the day → GPP follows; never precedes.
- IF in doubt on dose → do less; repeatable weeks > hero sessions.
- IF priority = powerlifter → GPP = 2× Zone 2, 1× short loaded carry tail, optional plyo priming, restoration PRN.
- IF priority = strongman → GPP = event-mimic medleys + 1× Zone 2 + 1× alactic capacity + restoration.
- IF priority = BJJ competitor → GPP = 2× Zone 2 + 1× sport-specific interval co-scheduled with mat + light plyo/throw + careful grip/neck management.
- IF priority = MMA → GPP = sport-specific round intervals + 2× Zone 2 + light alactic + careful sparring count.
- IF priority = calisthenics/gymnastics → GPP = scapular/trunk-biased carries + low-impact aerobic base + restorative pool + careful plyo dosing.
- IF priority = hybrid athlete → priority quality drives calendar; secondary quality held at maintenance.
- IF bar speed drops on planned submax → pull GPP volume before SPP volume.
- IF resting HR climbing → cut intensity; keep easy aerobic.
- IF sleep disrupted after late conditioning → move sessions earlier.
- IF recurrent local pain at a site → pause that tool; switch modality; coach review; clinician review if not resolving.

**Tables / landmarks (GPP taper):**

| Weeks Out | Action |
|---|---|
| 2–3 | Cut interval volume; keep alactic taps + easy aerobic |
| 1 | Walks, easy spins, sharp short throws/jumps, technique only |
| Day before | Movement and rest |

**Tool × Quality matrix:**

| Quality | Tools |
|---|---|
| Aerobic base | Bike, rower, ski erg, easy swim, sled walks, hills at easy pace |
| Tempo/extensive intervals | Bike, rower, ski erg, runs (tolerant athletes) |
| Alactic power | Short hill sprints, bike/ski erg sprints, broad jumps, throws |
| Alactic capacity | Short bike intervals, repeated short hills, battle ropes, sandbag bursts |
| Sport-specific intervals | Round-timed work for combat; event-mimic for strongman |
| Loaded GPP | Sled, prowler, yoke, carries, medleys |
| Plyometrics | Pogos, skips, broad/box jumps, bounds, depth jumps, throws |
| Restoration | Walks, easy bike, mobility, pool flush |

**Limiting-structure routing:**

| Limiter | Bias |
|---|---|
| Trunk stiffness | Suitcase carries, sled push, slow yoke if tolerated |
| Scapular control | Unilateral carries, controlled rowing, throw progressions |
| Hip capacity | Sled push, low box step-ups, A/B skips |
| Knee tolerance | Backward sled drag, bike, pool, low box |
| Foot/ankle | Pool, bike, controlled pogos only when tolerated |
| Neck/grip (grapplers) | Bike or rower > rope and carry; reduce grip GPP |
| Aerobic base limited | Zone 2 across multiple modalities |
