| RSA limited | Short interval work matched to sport demand |

**Goal-agnostic note:** These routing rules apply regardless of goal class. The priority filter and limiting-structure selector govern every block type (strength, skill, hypertrophy, combat, hybrid). Examples above are format illustrations only.

---

## 2. Cluster F — Combat Athlete Stress-Cost Scoring Layer (Module 0)

**PRINCIPLE:** Strength work is the last claimant on a combat athlete's finite multi-channel recovery budget; select exercises by strength return per unit of total systemic cost, given what the mat already took this week. (Art. 53–60, Module 0)

**Definitions (internal):**
- **SD** (Spinal Debt) = running 7-day spinal-load ledger.
- **CFS** (CNS Fatigue Score) = running 7-day CNS-load ledger.
- **TSC** (Total Stress Cost) = sum of 9 exercise-scoring dimensions (0–27).
- **Day types:** High (CFS ≤14, SD ≤10 only) / Medium (RIR 1–3, no max intent) / Low/Restorative (CNS ≈ 0, usable even in Red weeks).

### 2a. Five Recovery Channels

| Channel | What It Is | Recovery Rate | Primary Sport Drain |
|---|---|---|---|
| Spinal | Cumulative compressive/shear/flexion-extension load | 48–96 h (slow) | Scrambles, takedown defense, guard, bridging, stacking |
| CNS | High-threshold motor output, maximal/near-max intent | 24–72 h (intent-dependent) | Hard sparring, explosive exchanges, max-effort scrambles |
| Peripheral (local) | Muscle/connective fatigue in a specific region | 24–96 h (region-dependent) | Grip, neck, forearms, hips, lower back |
| Skill/coordination | Motor-learning bandwidth, technique freshness | 12–48 h | Technical drilling, new positions |
| Tissue tolerance | Constraint (not a fuel tank) — capacity of region to accept load without symptom flare | Variable | Contact, repeated impact, end-range loading |

### 2b. Spinal Debt (SD) Formula

```
SD_week = Σ (SpinalLoad_i × Density_i × FatigueState_i)

  SpinalLoad_i   = Σ exercise spinal scores (0–3 each) + mat spinal load estimate
  Density_i      = 1.0 normal | 1.25 if two spinal-heavy sessions <24 h apart
  FatigueState_i = 1.0 fresh | 1.3 entering session with low-back soreness/stiffness
```

**Mat spinal load per session:**

| Session Type | Mat Spinal Load |
|---|---|
| Technical drilling, flow | 1 |
| Positional rounds, moderate | 3 |
| Hard sparring / live wrestling | 5 |
| Competition / hard takedown battles | 7 |

**SD Interpretation (rolling 7-day):**

| SD_week | State | Programming Response |
|---|---|---|
| 0–10 | Green | Normal spinal loading (deadlift variants, loaded carries, heavy hinge) |
| 11–18 | Amber | Cap axial loading; prefer supported/neutral-spine variants; no max hinge |
| 19–26 | Red | Remove spinal-compressive lifting; substitute to low-SD options |
| 27+ | Black | Strength session = restorative only; reassess weekly mat load |

### 2c. CNS Fatigue Score (CFS) Formula

```
CFS_session = Σ (Intent_i × Proximity_i × VolumeFactor_i)

  Intent_i      = 1 (controlled) | 2 (forceful) | 3 (maximal/ballistic)
  Proximity_i   = 1 (≤70% / RIR≥3) | 2 (70–85% / RIR 1–2) | 3 (>85% / RIR 0)
  VolumeFactor  = 1 (≤3 hard sets) | 1.5 (4–6 sets) | 2 (7+ sets)

Mat CNS add: +1 hard positional | +2 hard sparring | +3 competition
```

**CFS Interpretation (rolling 7-day):**

| CFS_week | State | Response |
|---|---|---|
| ≤14 | Recoverable | Plan a true High day this week |
| 15–24 | Loaded | One High day max; speed work crisp + low-volume |
| 25–32 | Saturated | No max-effort gym; convert to Medium; protect sparring quality |
| 33+ | Overdrawn | Maintenance dose only; flag deload candidate |

**Canary rule:** If bar speed AND sparring sharpness both drop → CNS overdrawn regardless of the score number.

### 2d. Peripheral (Local) Fatigue Recovery Table

| Region | Typical Recovery After Hard Load | Sport Reload Demand | Key Caution |
|---|---|---|---|
| Grip/forearms | 24–48 h (cumulative across week) | Every session (gi especially) | High-grip lifting day before gi sparring degrades grip endurance on mat |
| Neck | 48–72 h (connective-heavy, slow) | Constant in grappling | Never train neck to true failure within 72 h of hard sparring |
| Lower back (erectors/QL) | 48–96 h | Constant | Most over-drafted; governed by SD |
| Hips/adductors/glutes | 24–72 h | High (guard, shots) | Heavy adductor eccentrics degrade shot speed for 48 h |
| Shoulders (cuff/scapular) | 24–72 h | High (framing, posting, pressing) | Pressing volume + heavy posting stacks local cost |
| Lats/upper back | 24–48 h | Moderate | Fast recovery; good "safe" volume sink |
| Quads | 24–48 h | Moderate | Heavy eccentric squats sore for shots/sprawls |
| Hamstrings | 48–72 h | Moderate–high | Eccentric-biased work lingers before live |

### 2e. Exercise Stress-Cost Scoring Dimensions (TSC)

Each exercise scored 0–3 per dimension; sum = TSC (0–27). **The highest individual dimension governs day-type and placement, not the total.**

| Dimension | What It Captures |
|---|---|
| Spinal compression/shear | Axial load + shear on spine |
| Eccentric cost | Magnitude/duration of lengthening tension |
| Grip/forearm cost | Demand on grip and forearm flexors |
| Local tissue cost | Concentrated load on one region |
| Skill cost | Coordination/learning bandwidth used |
| CNS cost | Intent × proximity to max |
| Soreness risk | Likelihood of next-day soreness affecting mat |
| Sport interference | Direct conflict with imminent mat quality |
| Injury-constraint cost | How much it loads a currently sensitive/limited region |

**Rule:** A TSC-9 exercise scoring 3 on Spinal in a Red SD week is disallowed even though its total looks moderate.

### 2f. Low-Cost Substitution Library

| Pattern | Standard (Higher Cost) | Low-Spinal Sub | Low-CNS Sub | Low-Grip Sub |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Hinge | Conventional DL | Hip thrust, back-extension | RDL at tempo light | Machine ham, hip thrust |
| Squat | Back squat | Belt squat, hack | Tempo goblet | Belt squat, leg press |
| Pull | Heavy bent row | Chest-supported row | Light cable row | Straps / chest-supported |
| Press | Barbell OHP | Landmine, machine press | DB press at RIR 3 | Machine press |
| Carry | Heavy farmer | Front-rack carry (lighter) | Short distance | Yoke/zercher (less grip) |

### 2g. Day-Type Definitions

- **High day:** CFS ≤14 AND SD ≤10; placed 24–48 h before rest or light mat; never before hard sparring.
- **Medium day:** RIR 1–3, no max intent; default during camps.
- **Low/Restorative day:** Pumps, blood flow, positional isometrics, mobility-with-load; CNS ≈ 0; usable even in Red weeks.

**Cross-cluster channel gates (hard rules):** (Art. 53–60 summary)
- SD tier gates all spinal/hinge work.
- CFS tier gates max-intent/overcoming work.
- Grip cost ≤1 within 24 h of gi sparring.
- Eccentric cost ≤1 within 48 h of shooting-heavy sparring.
- Neck work blocked within 72 h of hard sparring (isometric maintenance only allowed).
- Pressing local cost ≤1 within 24 h of heavy-posting sparring.
- Pull:push ≥1.3:1 for all grappling profiles (auto-enforce).
- Density multipliers: 1.25 if spinal lift <24 h from mat spinal load ≥5; 1.3 if entering with low-back stiffness. **Both compound — re-check SD tier after applying both.**
- Deload triggers: Two channels simultaneously Red, OR sparring quality drops 2+ sessions, OR a constraint flag escalates.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The five-channel scoring framework applies to any concurrent athlete (not exclusively combat). Replace "mat spinal load" with the appropriate sport-load estimate for any high-CNS or spinal-demanding sport.

---

## 3. Strength Training Around Hard Sparring Weeks

**PRINCIPLE:** Hard sparring weeks cap the gym at Medium by default; one High day is unlocked only if CFS ≤14 and SD ≤10 after adding mat estimates. (Art. 53)

**Worked example — 2 hard-spar week (Tue + Thu live), mat-only baseline:**
- Mon drilling: SD +1, CFS 0
- Tue hard spar: SD +5, CFS +2
- Wed technical: SD +1, CFS 0
- Thu hard spar: SD +5, CFS +2
- Fri positional: SD +3, CFS +1
- **Mat-only totals: SD ≈15 (Amber), CFS ≈5.**

Adding naive Wednesday leg day (back squat 4×5 @82% + conventional DL 3×3 @85%) → SD into Red + Density 1.25 multiplier applies (Wed lift <24 h after Tue hard spar, spinal-heavy) → dumps CNS fatigue directly into Thu sparring.

**Repaired 2-spar week template:**

| Day | Mat | Gym Day-Type | Focus | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Mon | Drilling | Medium | Belt squat 4×6 @RIR 2, chest-supported row 3×10, front-rack carry | Spinal ≤1, full buffer to Tue |
| Tue | Hard spar | None / AM restorative | Neck isometric maintenance, light grip flush | Protect the spar |
| Wed | Technical | Low | Hip thrust 3×8, back-extension 3×12, sled, lat volume | Spinal 0–1, CNS ≈0 |
| Thu | Hard spar | None | — | Protect the spar |
| Fri | Positional | Medium | Landmine press 4×6, pull volume, hip/adductor low-cost | Upper bias, low spinal |
| Sat | Optional roll | High (CFS ≤14 only) | One heavy main lift, low-spinal | Max buffer to next hard spar |

**Rules:**
- IF 2+ hard spars scheduled AND CFS ≥15 → no High gym day; cap at Medium.
- IF SD Red → all hinge/squat axial work → belt squat + back-extension at low load.
- IF sparring sharpness drops 2 sessions running → cut gym to restorative regardless of calendar.
- IF heavy lift is desired → place it the day after the last hard spar, ≥36 h before the next.
- IF gi sparring next-day → grip cost ≤1 in the gym today.
- IF two spinal-heavy exposures <24 h apart → apply Density 1.25; re-check SD tier before finalizing.

**Substitution tradeoffs:**
- Belt squat vs back squat: Spinal 0–1 vs 2–3; acceptable trade of trunk-bracing stimulus (mat already over-supplies this).
- Hip thrust vs deadlift: Spinal 0–1 vs 3; acceptable mid-week.
- Chest-supported row vs heavy bent row: removes spinal cost AND grip-limiter problem.
- Sled vs eccentric leg work: Eccentric 0, Soreness 0–1; no next-day quad/ham soreness degrading shots.

**Goal-agnostic note:** "Hard sparring week" logic generalizes to any high-CNS sport week (competition week for strength athletes, game week in field sports). The principle is always: mat/sport is the priority stimulus; gym protects and maintains.

---

## 4. Strength Training During MMA/BJJ Competition Camp

**PRINCIPLE:** Camp is a taper of strength stress and a peak of sport stress; gym volume decreases across camp while intensity stays just high enough to maintain. (Art. 54)

**Key number:** Maintenance requires approximately **2 hard sets per major pattern at ≥80% or RIR ≤2, 1–2×/week** to retain strength across a standard 6–8 week camp.

**Camp Phase Template:**

| Camp Phase | Weeks Out | Gym Dose | Day Types | CNS Ceiling |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Early | 8–6 | Highest gym tolerance of camp | 2 Medium, occasional 1 High early-week | CFS ≤2 from gym |
| Mid | 5–3 | Maintenance, volume trimmed | 2 Medium | CFS ≤2 from gym |
| Late | 2 | Minimal dose | 1 Medium + 1 Low | CFS ≤1 from gym |
| Fight week | 1 | Movement only | 1–2 Low/restorative, sharp and brief | CFS ≤1; no soreness |

**Maintenance template (mid-camp, 2×/week):**
- **Day A (Medium):** Belt squat 2×3 @RIR 2 (Spinal ≤1) + horizontal pull 3×8 + front-rack carry + neck isometric maintenance. Placed ≥36 h before hard sparring.
- **Day B (Medium):** Hip thrust 3×6 + landmine press 3×6 @RIR 2 + low-cost hip/adductor + grip maintenance only. Placed on lighter mat day.

**Gym CFS contribution must fall across phases:** 12 → 8 → 5 → 2 CFS units as mat CFS climbs. If gym CFS is flat or rising across a camp, the plan is wrong.

**Rules:**
- IF weeks out ≤2 → no Eccentric cost ≥2.
- IF active weight cut → all gym TSC ceilings drop one tier (High→Medium, Medium→Low); disable jumps/throws.
- IF CFS Saturated for 2 consecutive weeks → drop to one gym session, maintenance only; flag head coach.
- IF flagged sensitive region → injury-constraint-cost = 0 on that region; substitute the pattern.
- IF fight week → crisp, sub-maximal, confidence-building movement only; nothing that can create soreness.
- IF new exercise requested in camp → deny by default (skill + soreness cost); keep patterns the athlete already owns.
- IF weight cut active → drop eccentric cost AND grip cost to ≤1; depleted athletes bruise/sore more easily.

**Goal-agnostic note:** This phased-reduction structure applies to any competition camp where sport stress peaks and gym work must taper. The "maintenance requires surprisingly little" rule (2 hard sets/pattern, 1–2×/week) applies across all goal classes.

---

## 5. Lower-Back Management for Guard Players and Wrestlers

**PRINCIPLE:** The lower back's gym budget is a remainder computed after mat spinal load; SD is the governing number; build trunk capacity primarily through lower-spinal-cost tools. (Art. 55)

**Trunk capacity menu by spinal cost:**

| Spinal Cost | Tools | Weekly Role |
|---|---|---|
| 0–1 | Loaded carries (suitcase/front-rack), dead-bug progressions, Pallof, reverse hyper light, bodyweight back-extension | Staple — most of the volume |
| 2 | RDL moderate, Zercher carry, moderate good morning, trap-bar (neutral) | Periodic, Green SD only |
| 3 | Heavy conventional/sumo DL, heavy good morning | Rare, Green SD, away from hard mat |

**Sample wrestler week (2 hard mat sessions):**
- Early week (Medium): front-rack carries + suitcase carries + Pallof anti-rotation + hip thrust 3×8. SD contribution ≈ 1–2.
- Mid-week (Low): back-extension (controlled) + reverse hyper light + dead-bug. SD ≈ 0–1.
- One moderate hinge (trap-bar or RDL, Spinal 2) only if SD ≤10 on a buffered day.

**Rules:**
- IF SD Amber → all hinging capped at Spinal ≤1 (hip thrust, back-extension); no barbell DL.
- IF SD Red → trunk work = carries + bracing only; remove all hinge load.
- IF athlete reports low-back stiffness entering session → apply FatigueState 1.3; downgrade one tier; avoid end-range loading.
- IF Green SD window appears (light mat week) → schedule the rare heavy hinge here.
- IF wrestler has heavy takedown sparring next day → no Spinal ≥2 today.
- IF Density AND FatigueState multipliers both apply → they compound; re-check SD tier after applying both.

**Goal-agnostic note:** SD-gated hinge selection applies to any athlete with high cumulative spinal load, not only grapplers. Replace "mat spinal load" with the appropriate sport estimate.

---

## 6. Neck Training for Grapplers

**PRINCIPLE:** Neck work is almost never trained to failure and almost never within 72 h of hard sparring; 2 small sub-maximal doses/week for months outperforms occasional hard sessions. (Art. 56)

**Progression ladder (conservative):**
1. Isometric holds — flexion, extension, both lateral sides: 3×10–20 s sub-maximal against hand/band.
2. Longer/loaded isometrics — light head-harness held statically or banded, longer durations.
3. Slow dynamic — controlled harness flexion/extension through comfortable range, light load, high control.
4. Contact-tolerance integration — bridging/wrestler's-bridge variations, progressed gradually only when prior tiers are comfortable.

**Dosing:** 2×/week, sub-maximal, placed away from hard sparring (ideally a clean 72 h window before next live session). 3–4 directions, low volume each. Progress one variable at a time.

**Rules:**
- IF hard sparring within 72 h → neck work = isometric maintenance only, sub-maximal, low volume; or skip.
- IF any neck stiffness/sensitivity reported → reduce to gentle isometrics in comfortable range only.
- IF new to neck training → isometrics for 2–3 weeks before any harness load.
- IF competition week → maintenance isometrics only; no novel load.
- IF bridging introduced → progress from supported/partial before full; never rush range.
- IF no clean 72 h window in the calendar → default to maintenance isometrics; never harness.

**Scoring note:** CNS cost for neck work = 0. Never schedule as a "hard" element or count toward a High day. Harness/dynamic neck work day-before-spar = Sport-interference 3; block it.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The "isometric-first, small-dose, high-frequency" structure applies to any slow-recovering connective-tissue-heavy region where contact/force tolerance is required.

---

## 7. Shoulder Durability for BJJ

**PRINCIPLE:** Pull volume ≥ push volume for grapplers; build the cuff and scapular stabilizers directly; choose pressing angles that allow free scapular movement. (Art. 57)

**Weekly shoulder structure:**

| Slot | Tool | Sets/Week | Cost Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| Primary pull | Row / pull-up variants, 8–15 reps | 6–10 | Low spinal if chest-supported |
| Primary press | Landmine / neutral DB / incline, RIR 1–2 | 4–6 | Moderate local |
| Cuff/scapular | External rotation, prone/wall scap, face pulls | 6–10 across week (2–3×/wk) | Very low cost |
| End-range capacity | Controlled overhead carries, light bottoms-up, gradual overhead loading | 3–6 | Low–moderate; progress slowly |

**Pull:push volume ratio target ≈ 1.5–2:1. Hard floor: ≥1.3:1.**

**Rules:**
- IF shoulder sensitivity reported in a position → reduce injury-constraint-cost in that range to 0; keep work in comfortable ranges; bias cuff/scapular.
- IF heavy posting / scramble sparring next day → cap pressing local cost ≤1 today.
- IF introducing overhead pressing → progress landmine → neutral DB → barbell over weeks.
- IF push volume has crept above pull volume → rebalance before adding any pressing intensity.
- IF pull:push < 1.3:1 → auto-trim pressing sets and add pulling before anything else.

**Generator rule:** Enforce pull:push ≥1.3:1 for grappling profiles; always include low-cost cuff/scapular work 2–3×/week regardless of phase.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The pull:push ratio and cuff/scapular maintenance frequency apply to any overhead athlete or anyone with significant pressing volume; the specific threshold of 1.3:1 is the hard floor for contact sports.

---

## 8. Hip Strength for Guard Retention, Passing, and Takedowns

**PRINCIPLE:** Train the hip in all sport vectors (extension, flexion, abduction/adduction, rotation, unilateral stability); bias toward low-spinal, low-eccentric tools so hip work doesn't degrade shot/sprawl speed. (Art. 58)

**Hip vector menu:**

| Vector | Lower-Cost Staples | Higher-Cost / Rationed |
|---|---|---|
| Extension | Hip thrust, back-extension, sled | Heavy RDL/DL (spinal) |
| Squat pattern | Belt squat, split squat, hack | Heavy back squat (spinal) |
| Abduction/adduction | Cable/band ab-adduction, Copenhagen progressions (controlled) | Heavy adductor eccentrics (soreness) |
| Flexion/control | Loaded hip flexion, knee-drive, dead-bug | — |
| Power | Sled, low-volume jumps, KB swing | Max jumps/throws (CNS) |

**Game-style vector emphasis:**
- Guard player → weight abduction, hip flexion control, unilateral end-range work.
- Wrestler → weight extension power and squat-pattern leg drive; respect adductor-soreness rule before live.

**Rules:**
- IF shooting-heavy sparring within 48 h → adductor/hamstring Eccentric cost ≤1; keep hip power crisp and low-volume.
- IF SD Amber/Red → squat/hinge slot = belt squat / hip thrust / split squat; no heavy back squat.
- IF introducing Copenhagen/adductor work → start short-lever, controlled; soreness risk is high early.
- IF CFS Saturated → cut jump/throw volume; keep extension strength via thrust/sled.
- IF guard-retention is priority quality → emphasize abduction, hip flexion control, unilateral end-range.
- IF heavy eccentric hip exercise falls before takedown sparring → move after the session or substitute.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Multi-vector hip coverage applies to any athlete with hip-dominant sport demands. The specific eccentric-soreness window (48 h) before explosive/cutting actions generalizes beyond grappling.

---

## 9. Isometric Strength for Grappling (Yielding)

**PRINCIPLE:** Yielding isometrics build position-holding endurance and tissue tolerance at length with very low spinal and soreness cost; they are the primary gym content during Amber/Red SD weeks. (Art. 59)

**Two isometric flavors:**
- **Yielding (resisting a load, holding a position):** builds position-holding endurance, tissue tolerance; low CNS cost; usable in Red weeks.
- **Overcoming (push/pull against immovable resistance):** high force expression, joint-angle strength; CNS-costed (see Art. 60).

**Strength carry-over:** ±15° around the trained joint angle; train the exact angles the sport demands.

**Position-matched isometric menu:**

| Grappling Demand | Isometric Tool | Type | Cost Profile |
|---|---|---|---|
| Pin / top pressure | Loaded position holds, prone press holds | Yielding | Low |
| Framing / posting | Bottoms-up holds, wall/rack press holds | Yielding | Low–moderate |
| Grip stalemate | Bar/towel hangs, plate pinches, gi grip holds | Yielding | High grip cost |
| Scramble joint angles | Split-stance holds, mid-range squat holds | Yielding | Low spinal |
| Force production | Overcoming pushes/pulls vs pins | Overcoming | CNS (Art. 60) |

**Dosing:** Yielding holds 20–45 s, 2–4 sets; grip holds spaced away from gi sparring; overcoming work brief and crisp.

**Rules:**
- IF SD/CFS Amber/Red → yielding isometrics become primary gym content.
- IF gi sparring within 24 h → grip isometric cost ≤1.
- IF building position-specific strength → pick the exact joint angle the position uses.
- IF overcoming isometrics are programmed → treat as High/Medium CNS element; not filler.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Angle-specific isometrics apply to any athlete who needs position-specific strength (post-rehab return, specific sport positions in any domain).

---

## 10. Overcoming Isometrics for Combat Athletes

**PRINCIPLE:** Overcoming isometrics concentrate cost almost entirely in the CNS channel (spinal ≈0–1, eccentric 0, soreness 0–1, but CNS 2–3); they are the escape hatch when SD is Amber/Red but CFS ≤14. (Art. 60)

**Cost profile:** Spinal ≈0–1, Eccentric 0, Soreness 0–1, CNS 2–3. This exact profile makes them the precision instrument: spare CNS capacity converted into a strength stimulus when the spine cannot pay for traditional lifting.

**Prescription:**
- Effort: ramp to ~90–100% perceived effort over the set; early sets sub-maximal to groove position.
- Duration: 3–6 s per maximal push (true overcoming intent).
- Volume: 3–5 hard efforts per angle.
- Angles: 1–2 angles per pattern per session.
- Frequency: 1–2×/week as a CNS-costed element; not daily.

**Sport-matched overcoming menu:**

| Pattern | Setup | Sport Relevance |
|---|---|---|
| Press | Pins in rack at framing/lockout angle | Framing, posting, stiff-arm |
| Pull | Bar/handle pinned, pull into immovable | Grip fights, breaking posture, pulling guard |
| Hinge/extension | Pins low, push into bar (low-spinal setup) | Bridging, hip-extension power |
| Squat/leg drive | Pins mid-range, drive up | Scramble leg drive, stand-ups |

**Rules:**
- IF SD Amber/Red AND CFS ≤14 → overcoming isometrics = ideal strength stimulus (low spinal, real CNS strength); promote as High-day tool.
- IF CFS Saturated/Overdrawn → treat as max-effort element; pull them like any heavy work.
- IF hard sparring within 24 h → no maximal overcoming work (CNS interference).
- IF athlete reports joint-angle sensitivity → do not load maximally into that angle; choose a comfortable angle.
- IF weight cut active → reduce to sub-maximal; max CNS efforts poorly tolerated depleted.

**Prescription integrity rule:** Enforce 3–6 s, 3–5 efforts; reject long-duration prescriptions as mislabeled yielding work.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Overcoming isometrics apply to any athlete in a CNS-available/spinal-limited state regardless of sport or goal.

---

## 11. Cluster G — Volume-Threshold and Adaptation-Scoring Layer (Module 0)

**PRINCIPLE:** Adaptation is dose-dependent and bounded on both ends; find the smallest dose that drives the desired adaptation, then add only as much as the athlete can recover from and still improve. (Art. 61–68, Module 0)

**Definitions (internal):**

| Landmark | Name | Definition |
|---|---|---|
| MEV | Minimum Effective Volume | Smallest weekly dose producing measurable progress in the target adaptation |
| MAD | Minimum Adaptive Dose | Per-session threshold — smallest single-session dose that counts as a real stimulus |
| MAV | Maximum Adaptive Volume | Dose that produces most adaptation per unit of fatigue — the efficient sweet spot |
| MRV | Maximum Recoverable Volume | Most the athlete can recover from across a microcycle and still adapt |
| AR | Adaptive Reserve | Unused gap between current working volume and MRV |

**Rule:** MEV ≤ MAV ≤ MRV always. The window narrows with: higher training age, more concurrent training, more sport-supplied load on the same channel. For a combat athlete in camp, MEV and MRV can sit almost on top of each other.

### Master Adaptation Threshold Table

| Adaptation | Unit | MEV | MAV (sweet spot) | MRV (ceiling) | Warning Signs |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Skill acquisition (planche, HSPU, OAP, lever) | Quality exposures/week | 2 | 3–5 | 5–6 | Form decays in-session; failed attempts rise |
| Maximal strength | Hard sets/week per main lift | 4–6 | 8–12 | 12–16 | Bar speed falls week-over-week; top-set grind with no PR |
| Hypertrophy | Hard sets/week per muscle/region | 8–10 | 12–18 | 18–22 (region-dependent) | Pump/connection fades; soreness >72 h |
| Endurance/density (pull-up family) | Total submax reps/week vs max-rep set | ~150–200% of max | ~250–400% of max | ~450–550% of max | Rep quality/ROM degrades; elbow/forearm nags |
| GPP/conditioning | Hard sessions/week | 1–2 | 2–3 | 3–4 | Flat sessions; resting HR creep; appetite/sleep disruption |
| Tissue tolerance/prehab | Loaded exposures/week to region | 2 | 3–4 | 4–5 | Target region stays irritated between exposures |

**Combat-athlete correction:** When the sport already loads a quality, sport volume counts toward the threshold. Gym fills the remainder between sport-supplied volume and MAV — never pushes combined total past MRV.

### Effective Volume Units (EVU)

```
EVU(set) = Proximity × LoadZone × ROMquality × (1 − Junk_penalty)

  Proximity    = 0.5 (RIR≥4) | 0.8 (RIR 3) | 1.0 (RIR 1–2) | 1.1 (RIR 0, true failure)
  LoadZone     = 1.0 (in adaptation's effective zone) | 0.6 (clearly off-zone)
  ROMquality   = 1.0 (full quality ROM) | 0.7 (partial/cut ROM, unless partials are intent)
  Junk_penalty = 0.2 (set is fatigue-only; no progression, no quality)

Weekly Effective Volume = Σ EVU across qualifying sets
```
Compare Weekly EVU (not raw set count) to MEV/MAV/MRV anchors.

### Volume Cost Score (VCS)

```
VCS(block) = Σ [EVU_i × FailureMult_i × EccentricMult_i × NoveltyMult_i] × ChannelWeight

  FailureMult    = 1.0 (RIR≥2) | 1.3 (RIR 1) | 1.6 (RIR 0)
  EccentricMult  = 1.0 (normal) | 1.4 (slow/loaded eccentric) | 1.6 (supramaximal eccentric)
  NoveltyMult    = 1.0 (familiar) | 1.3 (new exercise/first exposure in block)
  ChannelWeight  = 1.0 (local hypertrophy) | 1.3 (spinal/axial) | 1.4 (CNS-heavy) | 1.2 (connective-heavy)
```
VCS is the explicit handshake with Cluster F: converts planned volume into the same cost language as the stress-cost layer.

### Skill Quality Score (SQS)

```
SQS(exposure) = Quality_reps / (Quality_reps + Failed_or_degraded_reps)

  Quality rep/hold = full position, full intended duration, clean form, no grinding.
  Failed/degraded  = missed, collapsed, broke position early, or visibly fought.

Stop rule: end the skill exposure when SQS < 0.7, OR at the first true form failure on a high-skill static.
```
Only quality reps count toward weekly skill MEV/MAV. Failed attempts = VCS cost with zero stimulus.

### Local Tissue Overlap Score (LTOS)

```
LTOS(region) = Σ [EVU_exercise × RegionShare_exercise] + SportRegionLoad

  RegionShare    = fraction of an exercise's EVU that lands on the region
  SportRegionLoad = region's weekly load from the sport

Flag when LTOS(region) approaches that region's MRV from 0.3.
```

### Adaptive Reserve (AR) Tiers

```
AR(channel) = MRV(channel) − [current gym volume on channel + sport-supplied volume on channel]

  AR ≥ 30% of MRV → Green:  room to add stimulus / progress
  AR 10–30%       → Amber:  hold volume; progress via intensity or quality, not added sets
  AR 0–10%        → Red:    at ceiling; maintain only; any add risks overshoot
  AR < 0          → Black:  already over MRV; cut volume now
```
**Governing-channel rule:** Plan to the channel with the lowest AR, not the average.

**Volume dose language:**
- **Progression dose:** Working volume at/above MEV with AR Green — drives the adaptation.
- **Maintenance dose:** ~MEV (often one-third to one-half of MAV) — holds the quality with minimal cost.
- **Overreach dose:** Brief planned excursion toward/above MRV for 1–2 weeks; only when followed by a deload and only on a non-sport-priority channel.

**Goal-agnostic note:** MEV/MAV/MRV/AR are universal across goal classes. The unit changes (sets, exposures, reps as % of max, sessions); the bounded-dose logic does not.

---

## 12. Volume Landmarks for Advanced Athletes

**PRINCIPLE:** For advanced athletes, the MEV–MRV productive window narrows; plan to the lowest-AR channel; maintenance is a legitimate, valuable dose. (Art. 61)

**Key numbers (repeat of master table for emphasis):**

| Adaptation | MEV | MAV | MRV |
|---|---|---|---|
| Skill (high-static) | 2 exposures/wk | 3–5 exposures/wk | 5–6 exposures/wk |
| Max strength | 4–6 hard sets/wk/lift | 8–12 hard sets/wk/lift | 12–16 hard sets/wk/lift |
| Hypertrophy | 8–10 hard sets/wk/muscle | 12–18 hard sets/wk/muscle | 18–22 hard sets/wk/muscle |
| Endurance/density | 150–200% of max set/wk | 250–400% of max set/wk | 450–550% of max set/wk |
| GPP/conditioning | 1–2 sessions/wk | 2–3 sessions/wk | 3–4 sessions/wk |
| Tissue tolerance | 2 exposures/wk | 3–4 exposures/wk | 4–5 exposures/wk |

**Two failure modes that look identical:** Both stalling-below-MEV and stalling-above-MRV produce flat performance and no PRs. Distinguish by checking quality (bar speed, ROM, SQS): quality intact = below MEV (add); quality degrading = at/over MRV (cut).

**Rules:**
- IF stalled 2–3 weeks AND EVU < MAV AND quality intact → below productive volume; add EVU.
- IF stalled AND quality (bar speed, ROM, SQS) degrading → at/over MRV; cut, don't add.
- IF AR Amber on priority channel → progress via load/quality; not added sets.
- IF AR Red/Black on any priority channel → maintenance dose only; plan deload.
- IF concurrent (sport + lifting) → subtract sport-supplied volume from the channel's MRV before computing gym room.
- IF logged volume is high but progress flat → recompute in EVU before changing anything; nominal volume lies.
- Qualities hold for 2–3 weeks at approximately MEV.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The narrow window and "count EVU not sets" rules are especially critical for advanced athletes in any goal class, and for any concurrent training scenario.

---

## 13. Skill Acquisition Volume

**PRINCIPLE:** Quality reps are the only reps that count for skill; frequency beats density for motor learning; 3–4 short fresh exposures/week build skill faster than 2 long fatiguing ones. (Art. 62)

**Skill volume thresholds:**

| Skill | Frequency (exposures/wk) | Quality Reps/Holds per Exposure | Failed-Attempt Cap | Deload Rule |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Planche (straddle→full) | 3–5 | 4–6 quality holds | ≤1–2 per exposure | Every 4–6 wk drop to MEV (2 exposures) |
| HSPU (freestanding/deficit) | 2–4 | 5–10 quality reps total | ≤2 | Deload when balance/ROM decays |
| One-arm pull-up (OAP) | 2–3 | 3–6 quality reps/side | ≤1 grind/side | Every 3–4 wk; elbow is the governor |
| Front/back lever | 3–4 | 4–8 quality holds | ≤2 | Every 4–6 wk to MEV |
| Press-to-handstand | 3–5 | 5–8 quality reps | ≤2 | Balance-decay triggered |

**MEV = 2 exposures/wk; MAV = 3–5; MRV = 5–6.** Beyond MRV, quality reps fall and failed reps rise — SQS itself signals the overshoot.

**SQS worked example (planche):**
- 8 holds planned; holds 1–5 clean; hold 6 breaks early; hold 7 shaky; hold 8 collapses.
- Quality = 5, degraded/failed = 3 → SQS = 5/(5+3) = 0.625 (< 0.7 stop-rule threshold).
- Productive exposure ended at rep 5; reps 6–8 = VCS cost with zero skill stimulus and error rehearsal.

**Rules:**
- IF SQS < 0.7 in a session → end the skill exposure; log only quality reps.
- IF failed attempts exceed cap 2 sessions running → reduce difficulty or frequency; over MRV.
- IF elbow/wrist/anterior-shoulder irritation lingers between exposures → reduce loaded exposures to that region (LTOS); choose lower-leverage progression.
- IF athlete also trains heavy pulling/pressing → count that region's load toward the skill's connective LTOS before adding skill frequency.
- IF hard sport/CNS week scheduled → drop skill to MEV (2 exposures); skill quality requires CNS freshness.

**Connective tissue is the ceiling (slow channel):** Wrists, elbows, biceps tendon (OAP), anterior shoulder (planche) set the real MRV, not the muscles. Deload skill on a separate clock from strength.

**Goal-agnostic note:** SQS gating and frequency-beats-density rules apply to any high-skill movement across all goal classes (muscle-ups, L-sit progressions, handstands, barbell skill in powerlifting, etc.).

**PRIMARY-SKILL FREQUENCY FLOOR (enforcement):** When a calisthenics skill is a PRIMARY named goal (not a maintenance/secondary quality), it must be programmed at the MIDDLE-TO-UPPER end of its frequency band above, not at the minimum. A single weekly exposure for a primary skill goal is an UNDER-DOSE failure unless connective-tissue irritation, a hard sport/CNS week, or an explicit pain gate forces it to MEV (2). Concretely: a primary OAP goal should get at least 2–3 exposures/week (varied as eccentric / isometric / band-assisted across the week, not the same row repeated); a primary planche goal at least 3–4 quality-hold exposures; a primary HSPU goal at least 2–3. Frequency beats per-session volume for skill strength — distribute the exposures across non-consecutive days. Only drop to the bottom of the band (or to one exposure) when you name the specific recovery/pain/sport reason for that skill.

---

## 14. Strength Volume Thresholds

**PRINCIPLE:** Strength MRV is CNS-gated (neural readiness, bar speed) — not muscle-tolerance gated; the productive volume band is narrow (~4–12 hard sets/wk per lift); past MRV, the athlete is training fatigue management, not strength. (Art. 63)

**Strength volume thresholds:**

| Element | Unit | MEV | MAV | MRV | Warning Signs |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Top sets | Hard sets/wk | 1–2 | 2–4 | 4–5 | Grind with no PR; bar speed down |
| Back-off sets | Hard sets/wk | 2–3 | 4–8 | 8–10 | Form drifts late in sets |
| Heavy singles | Reps/wk | 1–2 | 3–6 | 6–8 | Misses; slow lockout |
| Heavy triples | Sets/wk | 1–2 | 2–4 | 4–5 | Rep 3 grinds; speed falls |
| Speed/dynamic | Sets/wk | 3–4 | 6–10 | 10–12 | Bar speed not actually fast |

**Key distinctions:**
- ME (max-effort heavy singles/doubles): buys neural drive at high VCS.
- RE (back-offs at RIR 1–2): buys technique and some hypertrophy at lower CNS cost.
- Speed work: cheap CNS deposit; maintain even in loaded weeks.
- Effective strength set = approximately ≥80% and RIR 0–2. A 70% "strength" set is off-zone.

**High-concurrent sport modification:** Drop ME first when sport supplies heavy CNS. Keep 1–2 crisp top-set primer reps (RIR 1); move accumulation to RE at submax. Strength is retained 2–3 weeks at maintenance — no urgency to push during hard sport weeks.

**Rules:**
- IF bar speed at fixed load falls 2+ sessions → over MRV on CNS; cut heavy exposures (not back-offs first).
- IF top sets grind with no PR but speed work is crisp → too much ME; reduce ME, keep speed.
- IF AR Green on CNS and quality intact → add a back-off set OR raise top-set load; not both simultaneously.
- IF athlete trains a sport with high CNS draw → 1 heavy exposure/lift/week max; bias to RE and speed.
- IF weight cut active → reduce ME; near-maximal work poorly tolerated depleted.
- IF two main lifts both want a heavy day → they share the CNS MRV; alternate which lift gets the true ME exposure.
- Max-effort exposures: cap at 1/lift/week for advanced athletes; auto-reduce on flagged hard-CNS or sport weeks.

**Goal-agnostic note:** These strength-specific thresholds apply to any goal class that includes a max-strength component. The CNS-gated MRV distinction is critical for any athlete also doing CNS-expensive conditioning or sport.

---

## 15. Hypertrophy Volume Thresholds

**PRINCIPLE:** Count effective sets per muscle (EVU), not nominal sets; MRV is local and region-specific (18–22 effective sets/wk, region-dependent); sport-supplied volume counts toward a muscle's MRV via LTOS. (Art. 64)

**Hypertrophy volume thresholds by region group:**

| Region Group | Recovery Speed | MEV | MAV | MRV | Combat/Concurrent Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Lats/upper back | Fast | 8–10 | 14–18 | 20–22 | Safe volume sink; minimal sport overlap |
| Delts (all heads) | Fast | 6–8 | 12–16 | 18–20 | Tolerates frequency; watch posting overlap in grapplers |
| Chest | Moderate | 8–10 | 12–16 | 16–18 | Pressing overlaps posting volume |
| Quads | Moderate | 8–10 | 12–16 | 16–18 | Heavy eccentrics sore shots/sprawls for 48 h |
| Hamstrings | Slow | 6–8 | 10–14 | 14–16 | Eccentric work lingers; respect before live |
| Lower back/erectors | Slow | 4–6 | 8–10 | 10–12 | Most over-drafted by sport; often zero gym room in camp |
| Elbow flexors (biceps) | Moderate | 6–8 | 12–16 | 16–18 | High gi-grip overlap → LTOS critical |
| Forearms/grip | Slow (cumulative) | 4–6 | 8–12 | 12–14 | Sport supplies most; gym only fills the gap |

**Eccentric cost multiplier:** Slow-eccentric sets cost VCS ×1.4–1.6. A few slow-eccentric sets can cost more local recovery than many concentric-biased sets.

**Rules:**
- IF sport-supplied volume fills a region to MEV → remove or minimize gym volume to that region.
- IF eccentric work is near hard sport sessions → cap Eccentric cost ≤1; eccentric soreness in quads/hams degrades shots and scrambles for 48 h.
- IF region's LTOS approaches its MRV → gate any additional gym volume behind that region's AR.
- IF in-season with sport overlap → default to maintenance dosing (~MEV) for sport-overlapping regions; bias progression to low-overlap regions (lats, delts, chest).
- IF training is a hypertrophy focus → bias to lats, delts, chest where AR is largest.
- Muscle is retained for 2–3 weeks at approximately MEV — hypertrophy can yield to sport without loss.

**Fast vs slow recoverers:** Fast-recovering muscles (delts, lats, calves, forearms-as-trained) tolerate more frequency; slow-recovering or large multi-joint muscles (hamstrings, lower back, large prime movers) cap lower and recover slower.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Region-specific MRV table and LTOS correction apply to any hypertrophy-focused program or any concurrent training scenario.

---

## 16. Pull-Up Endurance and Density Volume

**PRINCIPLE:** Dose density off the athlete's current max-rep set (the correct denominator), not a round number; the connective tissue (elbows, forearm flexors, biceps tendon) sets MRV, not the lungs. (Art. 65)

**Volume thresholds:**
- MEV ≈ 150–200% of max-rep set/week.
- MAV ≈ 250–400% of max-rep set/week.
- MRV ≈ 450–550% of max-rep set/week.

**Density methods and volume profiles:**

| Method | Per-Set Load vs Max | Typical Weekly Dose | Best Use |
|---|---|---|---|
| Straight sets | 35–50% of max set | 200–400% of max | Base endurance, pain-free high-rep capacity |
| Ladders | Ramps to ~60% of max | 250–450% of max | Volume accumulation with built-in submax cap |
| EMOMs | 30–50% of max, many sets | 250–400% of max | Density/work-capacity, easy autoregulation |
| Cluster sets | 50–70% of max | 200–350% of max | Quality reps at higher per-rep load without failure |

**Most density reps live at 40–70% of max-rep capacity, stopping ≥2–3 reps shy of failure.**

**Scaling rule:** Express every density prescription as a % of athlete's current clean max set; re-anchor whenever max set shifts by >15%.

**Worked example:** 28–30 rep athlete using 4×10–12 (≈33–40% of max set), pain-free = moderate density dose in MAV band. Appropriate and unremarkable.

**Rules:**
- IF athlete's max set is high and elbows/forearms pain-free → 4×10–12 is an appropriate submax density dose; progress reps/sets within MAV band.
- IF ROM or tempo degrades within a set → stop the set; only full-ROM reps count (EVU).
- IF elbow/forearm/biceps-tendon irritation lingers between sessions → reduce density volume or shift to lower-overlap pattern.
- IF athlete also does heavy weighted pulling or gi sport → run LTOS on elbow flexors/grip before adding density.
- IF density times/rep counts slow week over week → at/over MRV on connective channel; deload the density block.
- IF CNS/spinal channels taxed by sport → density is a good low-CNS volume sink, provided the local channel has reserve.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The "max-set percentage" denominator for dosing density work applies to any endurance/density pull or push pattern across goal classes. The connective-tissue ceiling logic applies to any high-frequency pulling or overhead work.

---

## 17. Combat-Sport Volume Management

**PRINCIPLE:** The gym question for a combat athlete is never "how much should we lift?" but "what volume budget did the mat leave, and how do we fill the remainder without crossing combined MRV?" (Art. 66)

**Weekly sport-context volume map:**

| Sport Week Type | Sport-Supplied Volume | Gym Strength Dose | Gym Hypertrophy Dose | Governing Channel |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Hard sparring week (2+ live) | Very high CNS + spinal | Maintenance (~MEV; 1 primer top set) | Maintenance, low-overlap regions only | CNS + spinal |
| Competition camp (peak) | Maximal, sport-specific | Maintenance only; no ME | Maintenance, low-eccentric | Freshness/sharpness |
| Technical/skill week | Low–moderate | Progression allowed (MAV) | Progression on low-overlap regions | None acute → use the reserve |
| Deload/recovery week | Low | Low (restorative) or 1 quality top set | Low | Systemic recovery |

**Day-placement rule:**
- Low sport day → gym High day (one real progression session, maximum buffer before next live).
- Medium sport day → gym Medium day (RIR 1–3, no max intent).
- Hard sport day → gym Low/none (restorative, blood flow, low-overlap maintenance; protect the mat).

**Rules:**
- IF 2+ hard live sessions this week → gym strength = maintenance (1 primer); hypertrophy on low-overlap regions only.
- IF competition camp / peak week → no ME gym work; maintenance dose; protect sharpness.
- IF technical/light sport week → use the reserve; run gym progression dose (MAV).
- IF combined sport + gym AR < 10% (Red) on any channel → cut gym volume; substitute, don't push.
- IF gi grip/elbow LTOS is high → no added grip/elbow gym volume; gi supplied it.
- IF sparring sharpness drops 2 sessions → treat as MRV reached regardless of printed gym numbers; deload.

**Goal-agnostic note:** This inverse-scaling principle (gym volume flexes inversely to sport volume) applies to any concurrent athlete. A fixed gym template during high sport-demand weeks is the universal concurrent-training error.

---

## 18. Volume Allocation in Concurrent Training

**PRINCIPLE:** One quality gets a progression dose at a time; the rest get maintenance. Concurrent training requires subtractive planning from a global budget, not additive planning to individual MAVs. (Art. 67)

**Core concurrent rule:** Fund the priority quality to MAV; fund the rest only to MEV with whatever reserve remains. You can hold 4 qualities at MEV while pushing 1 to MAV; you cannot push all 5.

**Concurrent allocation matrix:**

| Priority This Block | Strength | Skill | Hypertrophy | GPP/Cond. | Shared-Channel Watch |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Strength focus | MAV | MEV (CNS-fresh, pre-strength) | MEV | MEV (low-CNS only) | CNS: skill + strength collide → skill before strength |
| Skill focus | MEV (1 primer) | MAV | MEV | MEV | CNS + connective: keep strength low so skill stays fresh |
| Hypertrophy focus | MEV (heavy primer) | MEV | MAV | MEV | Local/connective: density + hypertrophy collide → LTOS |
| Conditioning/GPP focus | MEV | MEV | MEV | MAV | Systemic: protect skill freshness; keep strength as primer |
| In-season (sport priority) | MEV + primer | MEV | MEV low-overlap | Sport supplies | Every channel — plan to lowest AR |

**Sequencing within the day:** Skill → Strength → Hypertrophy → Conditioning. Hard conditioning off priority-quality days.

**Interference types:**
- CNS collisions (strength × skill × max conditioning): sequence skill first (fresh), strength second; keep conditioning low-CNS in strength blocks.
- Local collisions (hypertrophy × density): apply LTOS; alternate which shares a region; don't run both to MAV on the same tissue.
- Systemic collisions (hard conditioning × everything): place hard conditioning on its own day or after the day's priority quality; never before skill/strength.

**Rules:**
- IF more than one quality is at a progression dose → reduce all but the priority to maintenance; can't fund two.
- IF two qualities share a channel → only one runs high; the other is MEV.
- IF global AR (lowest channel) is Red → no quality progresses this week; hold and recover.
- IF skill quality (SQS) drops during a strength or conditioning block → CNS collision; pull strength/conditioning, protect skill freshness.
- IF conditioning is blunting strength → switch conditioning to low-CNS modalities or move off strength days.
- IF rotating into a new block → re-rank the priority quality; re-allocate from the channel budgets.

**Maintenance is protective:** ~MEV holds a quality for 2–3 weeks, enabling prioritization without loss.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The one-progression-dose-at-a-time rule and the concurrent allocation matrix apply to every goal class. The specific collision types (CNS for skill+strength, local for hypertrophy+density) generalize across all training contexts.

---

## 19. Volume Audits to Fix Overloaded Programs

**PRINCIPLE:** Most stalled/overtrained programs are un-audited exercise lists; the audit converts an exercise list into channel/region ledgers, finds where the program exceeds MRV, and prunes back to a recoverable microcycle. (Art. 68)

**Volume-audit procedure (step by step):**

| Step | Action | Tool |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | List every gym exercise + sport session with sets, RIR, ROM, eccentric, novelty | Raw input |
| 2 | Convert each set to EVU (discount RIR-high, cut-ROM, junk) | EVU formula (0.4) |
| 3 | Map EVU onto muscles/regions via region-share; add sport region load | LTOS (0.7) |
| 4 | Map EVU onto channels (CNS, local/connective, spinal, systemic) | VCS/AR (0.5/0.8) |
| 5 | Compute LTOS per region and AR per channel; flag any near/over MRV | 0.7, 0.8 |
| 6 | Price the week in VCS; check against stress-cost budget | 0.5 + Cluster F |
| 7 | Prune: cut redundancy on over-MRV regions; redistribute to high-AR regions/days | Allocation logic |
| 8 | Re-test: recompute AR/LTOS; confirm all priority channels ≤ MRV with reserve | 0.8 |

**Key insight:** The problem is usually un-audited overlap on one channel while another sits idle.

**Rules:**
- IF athlete reports stalled + nagging region → audit that region's LTOS first; usually over MRV from stacked sources.
- IF region is over MRV → cut the lowest-priority direct contributor (often isolation work); keep the priority pattern.
- IF a channel is over MRV but a region within it has reserve → redistribute, don't just delete.
- IF the audited week still exceeds global MRV → cut a whole secondary quality to maintenance (Art. 67); don't shave everything evenly.
- IF sport supplies a region's MEV already → remove redundant gym volume to that region.
- IF athlete resists cutting → frame it as maintenance (qualities hold 2–3 weeks); show LTOS/AR numbers.

**Generator audit mode:** Ingest exercise list + sport → output EVU, per-region LTOS, per-channel AR, VCS, with over-MRV flags → prune redundancy → re-test → output recoverable microcycle. Keep all scoring internal unless user asks.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The audit procedure is domain-agnostic; it applies to any training scenario. The most common finding is an over-loaded connective/local region from stacked exercises that look fine in isolation.

---

## 20. Nutrition Intake Triage

**PRINCIPLE:** Screen the athlete's nutritional situation before generating any nutrition output; assign a complexity tier and gate the depth of guidance accordingly. (Art. 69)

**Triage inputs required:**
- Body composition and weight trend (stable / gaining / losing / cutting; planned phase).
- Training schedule (sessions/wk, duration, type, same-day doubles, fasted vs fed).
- Nutrition basics (meals/day, timing, appetite, food restrictions, GI tolerance).
- Hydration (active vs thirst-only, sweat rate, cramping history, heat exposure).
- Supplement and stimulant use (current supplements, caffeine dose/timing, anti-doping status).
- Deadlines (competition date, weigh-in deadline, weight-class restriction).

**Nutrition complexity tiers:**

| Tier | Criteria | Engine Output |
|---|---|---|
| Tier 1 — Low | Stable BW or gradual change; ≥3 meals/day with reasonable protein distribution; no active cut within 4 wk; no significant GI issues; normal appetite; adequate hydration awareness; no comp deadline within 6 wk | Standard nutrition support notes, general hydration, optional supplement basics |
| Tier 2 — Moderate | Any of: actively losing/gaining with performance or recovery affected; training volume high enough that glycogen depletion is plausible; ≤2 meals/day or consistently low appetite; mild GI issues around training; comp/weigh-in within 6–12 wk; significant caffeine dependence or erratic use | Detailed nutrition notes, timed fueling guidance, hydration decision rules, supplement considerations, weight-class caution flags |
| Tier 3 — High | Any of: rapid unexplained weight loss or gain; signs consistent with disordered eating; severe/persistent GI distress; fainting/near-fainting; fatigue unresolved by rest or basic nutrition corrections; severe dehydration; suspected supplement/drug interaction; diabetes, kidney disease, cardiac conditions, eating disorder history | Flag for professional referral; do not generate aggressive nutrition protocols; reduce training volume recommendations; connect athlete with sports dietitian or physician |

**Refer-out triggers (always, regardless of athlete preference):**
- Signs of disordered eating.
- Rapid unexplained weight change.
- Persistent fainting/syncope.
- Severe GI bleeding, vomiting, or malabsorption history.
- Diabetes requiring medication management.
- Kidney disease or history of kidney stones.
- Eating disorder diagnosis or suspected active eating disorder.
- Extreme supplement stacking (hormonal products, thyroid agents, diuretics, stimulants beyond caffeine).
- Any athlete subject to WADA/USADA testing asking about aggressive supplement protocols.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The triage-tier framework applies across all goal classes and athlete types. The tier governs depth of guidance; goal-specific formulas are applied within the appropriate tier.

---

## 21. Calorie and Macro Targets

**PRINCIPLE:** Starting maintenance estimate = 35–45 kcal/kg/day; macros are set in order of protein → carbohydrate → fat; fat has a hard floor; carbohydrate is scaled to training demand, not only body composition goals. (Art. 70)

**Calorie target starting range:** 35–45 kcal/kg/day for moderate-to-high training frequency. Athletes with very high volumes, two-a-days, or heavy conditioning may be at the upper end or above.

**Goal-state calorie adjustments from maintenance:**

| Goal State | Calorie Adjustment | Key Conditions |
|---|---|---|
| Performance maintenance | ±0 | No BW change goal |
| Gradual fat loss | −300–500 kcal/day | Only if training performance and recovery remain intact |
| Aggressive fat loss | −500–750 kcal/day | Flag for Tier 2/3 monitoring; not compatible with high-intensity blocks |
| Muscle gain | +200–400 kcal/day | Use lower end to minimize excess fat gain |
| Recomposition | Maintenance or −100–200 kcal with high protein | Best for beginners or detrained athletes returning to training |
| Competition performance (peaking, not cutting) | Maintenance or slight surplus | Carbohydrate timing is primary lever |

**Calorie adjustment rules (at 1–2 week review):**
- IF losing weight faster than 0.5–1 kg/week AND training quality dropping → increase by 200–300 kcal; primarily from carbohydrate.
- IF gaining faster than 0.25–0.5 kg/week AND fat gain appears excessive → reduce by 200–300 kcal; primarily from the surplus.
- IF persistent fatigue, poor sleep, or reduced performance despite adequate rest → check calorie adequacy before reducing training; undereating is more commonly the cause.
- IF training performance stable and body composition moving toward goal → no adjustment.
- IF cutting to weight class and performance dropping sharply → reassess cut timeline and rate; slower cut preferred over sacrificing training quality.

**Macronutrient decision rules:**

**Protein:**
- Standard (moderate training volume): 1.6–2.0 g/kg/day.
- High volume or hard dieting phase: 2.0–2.4 g/kg/day.
- Athletes over 40: err toward upper end.
- Vegan athletes: add 10–15% above stated range.

**Carbohydrate (scaled to training demand):**
- Low activity day or deload: 3–4 g/kg/day.
- Moderate training day: 4–6 g/kg/day.
- Hard training day (heavy lifting, BJJ, conditioning, or two-a-days): 6–8 g/kg/day.
- Competition day or pre-competition: 7–10 g/kg/day.
- Low-carbohydrate approaches are **contraindicated** during: hard conditioning blocks; high-volume hypertrophy phases; repeated same-day training; weight-class competition close to competition.

**Fat:**
- Remaining calories after protein and carbohydrate are established.
- Hard floor: 0.8–1.0 g/kg/day (hormonal function). Do not reduce below this floor in any cutting phase.

**Calorie and macro template by phase:**

| Phase | Protein (g/kg) | Carbohydrate (g/kg) | Fat (g/kg) | Total kcal/kg |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Muscle gain | 2.0–2.2 | 5–7 | 1.0–1.2 | 38–45 |
| Performance maintenance | 1.8–2.0 | 5–6 | 1.0 | 36–42 |
| Gradual fat loss | 2.2–2.4 | 3–5 | 0.8–1.0 | 28–34 |
| Aggressive cut (caution) | 2.4 | 3–4 | 0.8 | 25–30 |
| Recomposition | 2.0–2.2 | 3–5 | 0.8–1.0 | 28–35 |
| Competition peak | 1.8–2.0 | 6–10 | 0.8–1.0 | 40–50+ |

**Goal-agnostic note:** These formulas apply across goal classes. Competition peak carbohydrate (6–10 g/kg) is the primary fueling lever regardless of sport.

---

## 22. Carbohydrate Periodization

**PRINCIPLE:** Muscle glycogen is the limiting substrate for high-intensity effort; 45-min heavy resistance session can deplete glycogen in type IIx fibers by 40–44%; chronically low carbohydrate availability is one of the most common and correctable causes of performance regression. (Art. 71)

**Session-type classification:**

**High carbohydrate demand:** Heavy compound strength (>75% 1RM, multiple heavy sets); high-volume hypertrophy; hard BJJ/wrestling/Muay Thai/boxing sparring or high-intensity drilling; competitive conditioning (HIIT, circuits, AMRAP); two-a-days; competition/testing day.

**Moderate carbohydrate demand:** Moderate-volume strength days (submax loading); technical drilling at low-to-moderate intensity; accessory/hypertrophy without heavy compound loading; single moderate-intensity conditioning session.

**Low carbohydrate demand:** Active recovery, mobility, light GPP; deload sessions; rest days; LISS below 60–65% max HR.

**Carbohydrate periodization framework:**

| Day Type | Target Carbohydrate | Practical Examples |
|---|---|---|
| High demand training day | 6–8 g/kg or higher | Heavy squat/DL day, hard BJJ, competitive conditioning, competition day |
| Moderate demand training day | 4–6 g/kg | Moderate upper body push-pull, technical drilling, single moderate conditioning session |
| Low demand or rest day | 2–4 g/kg | Active recovery, rest day, deload, mobility |
| Competition day or peak | 7–10 g/kg | Prioritize high-glycemic carbohydrate availability pre-event |

**Pre-session carbohydrate timing:**
- 2–4 hours before: full meal with 50–150 g carbohydrate, complete protein, low-to-moderate fat. Avoid very high fat or high fiber close to training.
- 1 hour before: smaller carbohydrate-focused snack, 25–50 g, lower fiber, if pre-session meal not possible.
- 30 minutes or less (emergency only): 20–30 g fast-digesting carbohydrate only. No protein or fat at this window.

**Fasted training rules:**
- Low-to-moderate intensity, under 60 minutes: generally tolerable fasted for most athletes.
- High intensity, combat sport, or over 60–75 minutes: fasted = clear performance compromise. Chronic fasted hard training is a performance and recovery liability.

**Intra-session carbohydrate:**
- Under 60 minutes, moderate intensity: water alone sufficient.
- Over 60 minutes OR high-intensity combat sport or conditioning: 25–60 g fast-digesting carbohydrate per hour.
- Two-a-days or back-to-back sessions same day: intra-session carbohydrate becomes critical; begin earlier in session and continue into recovery window.

**Post-session carbohydrate:**
- Glycogen resynthesis fastest in first 30–60 minutes post-training.
- Optimal window: 0.8–1.2 g/kg carbohydrate + 0.3–0.4 g/kg protein.
- If two sessions on same day with fewer than 4 hours between: aggressive post-session carbohydrate replenishment is critical for maintaining quality in the second session.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The session-type classification and daily carbohydrate targets apply regardless of goal class. The 40–44% glycogen depletion figure underscores why carbohydrate adequacy is non-negotiable for any athlete doing high-intensity work.

---

## 23. Protein Rules, Meal Distribution, and Recovery Support

**PRINCIPLE:** Protein requirements are anchored to training volume and goal state; muscle protein synthesis requires a per-meal leucine threshold; distribute protein across 3–5 meals of 30–50 g each. (Art. 72)

**Protein targets by goal and athlete state:**

| Athlete State | Protein Target (g/kg/day) |
|---|---|
| Standard strength or hypertrophy | 1.6–2.2 |
| High-volume training or dieting phase | 2.0–2.4 |
| Combat sport athletes (BJJ, wrestling, Muay Thai, boxing) | 1.8–2.2 |
| Older athletes (40+) | 2.0–2.4 |
| Vegetarian athletes | Add 10–15% to stated target (leucine-rich plant sources: soy, legumes, edamame) |
| Vegan athletes | Add 15–20% to stated target; strategic pairing of complementary plant proteins |

**Leucine threshold:** Muscle protein synthesis requires ~2.5–3 g leucine per meal. This corresponds to ~30–40 g of high-quality animal protein per meal (chicken, beef, fish, eggs, dairy) or higher amounts from plant sources (lower leucine density).

**Meal distribution decision rules:**
- Target: 3–5 protein-containing meals/day, each with 30–50 g protein.
- IF athlete eating fewer than 3 meals/day → first priority is increasing meal frequency and protein distribution (before manipulating macro ratios).
- Pre-sleep protein: 30–40 g (casein, cottage cheese, or casein-containing shake) may support overnight MPS, particularly in hypertrophy phases or during hard training blocks with high soreness.

**Protein in dieting phases:**
- Apply upper range of protein targets (2.2–2.4 g/kg) during any fat loss phase.
- Higher protein in deficit supports lean mass retention, increases satiety, and has higher thermogenic effect than carbohydrate or fat.

**Goal-agnostic note:** The leucine threshold and per-meal protein floor (30–40 g) apply across all goal classes. The elevated protein target during dieting applies regardless of sport.

---

## 24. Hydration and Electrolyte Decision Rules

**PRINCIPLE:** Fluid loss of 1% BW meaningfully reduces performance; at 2% strength/power decline; at 3–4% cognitive function and reaction time compromised; at 4%+ cramping and heat exhaustion risk elevated. Proactive drinking always beats reactive. (Art. 73)

**Hydration assessment — urine color field marker:**
- Pale straw yellow = well hydrated (target).
- Dark yellow = mild dehydration.
- Amber or darker = significant dehydration.
- Clear = potentially over-hydrated (dilutional hyponatremia risk in prolonged exercise).

**Pre-session hydration protocol:**
- 2–3 hours before: 500–600 mL fluid.
- 20–30 minutes before: 200–250 mL fluid.

**Intra-session hydration:**
- Under 60 min, mild conditions: water ad libitum.
- 60–90 min, moderate conditions: 400–600 mL/hour (water or low-concentration electrolyte drink).
- Over 90 min OR high-intensity OR hot/humid: 400–800 mL/hour; add sodium 300–700 mg/liter.

**Post-session rehydration:**
- Replace 1.25–1.5 liters of fluid per kg of bodyweight lost.
- Include sodium 300–700 mg/liter to promote fluid retention.

**Electrolyte decision rules:**
- Sodium: primary electrolyte lost in sweat; average sweat sodium concentration ≈ 1.0–1.5 g/liter.
- Potassium: important for muscle contractility; athletes with high sweat rates or heat training should ensure adequate dietary intake.
- Magnesium: lost in sweat; commonly under-consumed in athletes with restricted diets or high training loads; deficiency → cramping, poor sleep, impaired neuromuscular function.

**Cramping decision tree:**
- Cramping during/immediately after hard training in heat → likely sodium and fluid deficits (increase pre-session sodium, intra-session sodium-containing fluid, post-session rehydration).
- Cramping at rest or at night, not heat/session related → may involve magnesium, potassium, or total dietary deficiency.
- Cramping with severe dehydration signs → medical attention; do not train.

**Hyponatremia caution:** Over-consumption of plain water during prolonged sessions dilutes blood sodium. Risk factors: very large volumes of plain water during prolonged sessions, no sodium in fluids during prolonged events, salty sweaters, endurance-type events. Prevention: include sodium in hydration during prolonged events.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Hydration thresholds apply regardless of goal class. The 1%/2%/3–4%/4%+ performance impact framework is universal.

---

## 25. Pre/Intra/Post-Workout Fueling

**PRINCIPLE:** Pre-session fueling timing gates nutrient composition; intra-session fueling threshold is 60 minutes or session intensity; post-session window is 30–60 minutes for maximal glycogen resynthesis. (Art. 74)

**Pre-workout fueling by timing:**

| Timing | Carbohydrate | Protein | Fat | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 2–3 hours before | 50–100+ g | 30–50 g | 15–30 g (moderate) | Full meal; moderate fiber acceptable |
| 1 hour before | 30–60 g (lower fiber) | 20–30 g (lean source) | Minimal | Smaller, simpler; lower fiber |
| 30 min or less (emergency) | 20–30 g fast-digesting only | None | None | Avoid protein and fat at this window |

**Fasted training rules:**
- Low-intensity, under 60 min: tolerable fasted for most athletes.
- Moderate-to-high intensity: recommend minimum 20–30 g fast-digesting carbohydrate 15–30 min pre-session if athlete cannot tolerate a full meal.
- Hard BJJ, wrestling, sparring, or competitive conditioning fasted = clear performance compromise.
- Chronic fasted hard training: consistently recommend against in athletes with performance or muscle gain goals.

**Intra-workout fueling:**

| Session Duration/Intensity | Carbohydrate |
|---|---|
| Under 60 min, single session | Water only sufficient for most athletes |
| 60–90 min, moderate-to-high intensity | 25–40 g carbohydrate/hour |
| Over 90 min OR two sessions in one day | 40–60 g carbohydrate/hour |

**Post-workout fueling (within 30–60 minutes):**
- Carbohydrate: 0.8–1.2 g/kg BW.
- Protein: 0.3–0.4 g/kg BW (minimum 30–40 g).
- Fat: minimal in the immediate recovery window.

**Practical options:** Whey protein + banana + water or milk; chocolate milk; rice with chicken or fish; Greek yogurt with fruit.

**Two-a-day fueling requirements:**
- Session 1 pre-training: full pre-session meal or minimum carbohydrate-protein snack.
- Between sessions: 0.8–1.2 g/kg carbohydrate + 30–40 g protein immediately after session 1; plus active rehydration.
- Session 2 pre-training: small top-up snack 30–60 min before session 2 if full recovery window has elapsed.
- Post-session 2: full recovery meal.
- IF athlete cannot meet these fueling requirements → reduce two-a-day frequency or reduce intensity of one session until fueling can support both.

**Goal-agnostic note:** These peri-workout windows apply across all goal classes. The two-a-day requirements are non-negotiable regardless of sport or goal.

---

## 26. Supplements

**PRINCIPLE:** Apply the 7-step hierarchy before any supplement is considered; supplements at the bottom of the hierarchy are the last increment, not the foundation. (Art. 75)

**Supplement hierarchy (address in order):**
1. Total calorie adequacy.
2. Protein targets consistently met.
3. Carbohydrate adequacy for training demands.
4. Hydration and electrolyte management.
5. Sleep quantity and quality.
6. Training consistency and progressive overload.
7. Supplements.

**Evidence-based supplement reference:**

| Supplement | Evidence Level | Dose | Timing / Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| Creatine monohydrate | Strong | Loading (optional): 20 g/day in 4 divided doses for 5–7 days, then maintenance. Maintenance: 3–5 g/day | Timing not critical; BW gain 0.5–2 kg (intramuscular water) in first week; third-party verification for tested athletes; not recommended for kidney disease |
| Caffeine | Strong | 3–6 mg/kg BW | 30–45 min before training; tolerance develops with regular use; avoid afternoon/evening for sleep quality; caution with anxiety, panic disorder, cardiac arrhythmias |
| Beta-alanine | Moderate (specific use) | 3.2–6.4 g/day in divided doses | Best for efforts of 60–240 s sustained high intensity; paresthesia common and harmless; take with food or split doses |
| Protein powder | Practical tool | 20–40 g/serving | Whey = post-training; casein = pre-sleep; plant-based (pea/rice/soy blend) for vegan athletes; third-party certified |
| Omega-3 (EPA + DHA) | Broad health support | 2–3 g combined EPA + DHA/day | High doses >3–4 g/day may increase bleeding time |
| Vitamin D | Condition-relevant | 1000–3000 IU/day | Baseline for strength/combat athletes, especially limited sun exposure or indoor training; pair with vitamin K2 at higher doses |
| Magnesium | Practical (high-sweat athletes) | 200–400 mg elemental/day | Glycinate, malate, or citrate forms; take in evening; contraindicated in renal disease without physician oversight |
| Dietary nitrates / beetroot | Emerging evidence | 300–600 mg dietary nitrate ~2–3 h before training | Avoid mouthwash around supplementation (kills oral bacteria needed for nitrate-to-nitric-oxide conversion) |
| Collagen/gelatin + Vitamin C | Emerging (connective tissue) | 15–20 g gelatin/collagen + 50–200 mg Vitamin C | ~60 min before a connective tissue loading activity; not established therapy; does not replace medical guidance |

**Pre-workout blends:** Approach with caution; high variability in quality and risk. Do not recommend named products. Choose third-party certified. Red flags: proprietary blends without individual ingredient doses; stimulants beyond caffeine; no third-party certification.

**Banned substance / anti-doping flag:** Flag for any athlete competing in a tested sport. Third-party testing reduces but does not eliminate risk. Only fully safe approach for tested athletes: avoid all supplements not third-party certified.

**Do-not-recommend list:**

| Category | Reason |
|---|---|
| Diuretics/water pills (non-medical) | Dehydration and electrolyte risks; banned in many sports |
| Testosterone boosters and hormone precursors | Inadequate evidence; potential hormonal disruption; banned substance risk |
| Stimulant fat burners (DMAA, DMHA, ephedrine) | Cardiovascular risk; banned in tested sport |
| Growth hormone secretagogues | Banned; outside coaching scope |
| HCG, peptides, SARMs | Banned substances; outside coaching scope |
| Weight-loss products with undisclosed stimulants | Contamination risk; cardiovascular risk |
| Detox cleanses and liver flush products | No meaningful evidence |
| Yohimbine at high doses | Cardiovascular and psychiatric risk |

**Goal-agnostic note:** The 7-step hierarchy applies regardless of goal class. No supplement compensates for inadequate calories, protein, carbohydrate, hydration, or sleep.

---

## 27. Weight-Class, Cutting, Refeed, and Competition-Week Nutrition

**PRINCIPLE:** Gradual cut at 0.5–1% BW/week is the conservative default; maintain protein at 2.0–2.4 g/kg during any cut; fat not below 0.8 g/kg; acute water manipulation is not recommended. (Art. 76)

**Weight-class risk classification:**

| Risk Level | Criteria |
|---|---|
| Routine (low risk) | Within 2–3% of competition weight year-round; no extreme acute manipulation planned; gradual fat loss 0.3–0.5 kg/week in weeks before comp |
| Moderate risk | 4–6% above competition weight within 8–12 weeks of competition |
| High risk (flag for referral/professional consultation) | More than 6–8% above competition weight within 6 weeks; rapid weight cutting (water/food restriction 24–48 h before weigh-in) planned; athlete under 18 |

**Gradual cut decision rules:**
- Default rate: 0.5–1% BW/week.
- If training is hard and competition approaching → target slower end: 0.3–0.5 kg/week.
- If larger cut needed → add 2–4 weeks to timeline rather than increasing weekly deficit.
- During any cut: protein = 2.0–2.4 g/kg; reduce carbohydrate first; fat ≥ 0.8 g/kg.

**Refeed protocol:**
- Insert a refeed day every 7–14 days for athletes in a gradual cut lasting more than 3 weeks.
- On a refeed day: increase carbohydrate to maintenance-level intake or higher (5–7 g/kg); protein stays constant.
- A refeed day is structured and intentional — not a "cheat day."

**Competition-week nutrition:**

| Days Out | Guidance |
|---|---|
| 7–3 before comp | Maintain training nutrition habits; slightly reduce training volume (taper); carbohydrate intake similar or slightly increased as volume drops |
| 2–1 before comp | Emphasize carbohydrate availability; reduce dietary fiber; avoid high-fat, high-fiber, or unfamiliar foods; maintain hydration |

**Acute water weight cutting — do not recommend without professional oversight:**
Aggressive acute dehydration (sauna, heavy sweating, fluid restriction, diuretics) in 24–48 h before weigh-in is associated with: impaired strength, power, and reaction time; cognitive and coordination deficits; cardiovascular stress; kidney stress; dangerous electrolyte imbalances; and death in extreme cases. **The engine does not generate protocols for acute water manipulation.**

**Goal-agnostic note:** Gradual cut rates and refeed timing apply regardless of sport or goal class. Competition-week carbohydrate loading is relevant to any athlete with a performance event.

---

## 28. Nutrition Readiness and Recovery Scoring Layer

**PRINCIPLE:** A 7-variable, 0–14 point nutrition readiness score gates session prescription; scores below 8 reduce volume and intensity; persistent low scores trigger escalation. (Art. 77)

**Nutrition readiness scoring variables:**

| Variable | 0 (Poor) | 1 (Moderate) | 2 (Good) |
|---|---|---|---|
| Morning BW trend | Down >1 kg from 3-day average (unexplained) or up >1 kg rapidly | Stable ±0.5 kg | Stable and consistent with goal |
| Appetite | Suppressed or absent | Somewhat reduced | Normal or appropriately elevated |
| Pre-session fueling | Fasted >5 hours or skipped meal | Small snack only | Appropriate pre-session meal |
| Hydration status | Dark urine or morning weight drop | Mild signs | Pale urine; BW stable |
| GI comfort | Active symptoms (cramping, nausea, bloating) | Mild discomfort | No GI issues |
| Energy level | Subjectively low; fatigue before session begins | Moderate, manageable | Normal or good |
| Recovery between sessions | Soreness or fatigue persisting from prior session | Moderate residual fatigue | Adequately recovered |

**Total score: 0–14**

**Score interpretation and engine response:**

| Score | Readiness Level | Engine Modification |
|---|---|---|
| 12–14 | Green — high nutrition readiness | Full session as programmed |
| 8–11 | Yellow — moderate nutrition readiness | Reduce volume by 10–20%; maintain intensity; apply fueling guidance |
| 4–7 | Orange — low nutrition readiness | Reduce volume by 20–30%; reduce intensity to submaximal; flag for nutrition correction |
| 0–3 | Red — compromised nutrition readiness | Do not prescribe high-intensity session; active recovery or rest; investigate nutrition deficit |

**Persistent low readiness escalation:**
- IF nutrition readiness averages below 8 for more than 5 consecutive sessions without clear explanation → flag for nutrition review conversation with coach; check total daily calorie intake vs training demands; check protein distribution; evaluate sleep quality independently.
- IF no clear explanation found → Tier 3 escalation (refer out) is appropriate.

**Goal-agnostic note:** This 7-variable readiness scoring framework gates session prescriptions regardless of sport or goal class. The volume-reduction tiers (10–20%, 20–30%, rest) are universal override rules.

---

## 29. Nutrition Troubleshooting

**PRINCIPLE:** Address nutrition deficits in a structured check sequence before attributing performance problems to overtraining or programming errors. (Art. 78)

### Low Energy and Fatigue — Check Sequence:
1. Total caloric intake sufficient for training demands? Check for undereating or poor meal planning.
2. Carbohydrate availability adequate on hard training days? Carbohydrate-depleted athletes feel flat; increase pre- and intra-session carbohydrate before attributing fatigue to other causes.
3. Protein adequately distributed? Low protein per meal reduces recovery quality even if daily total is met.
4. Iron deficiency possible? Elevated risk: female athletes; vegetarian/vegan; calorie-restricted athletes.
5. Vitamin D deficiency possible? Elevated risk: indoor athletes; darker skin tones; winter months.
6. Sleep independently adequate?

### Muscle Cramping — Check Sequence:
1. Training-related cramping with heat/sweat/prolonged sessions → primary suspects: sodium depletion and fluid deficit. Increase pre-session sodium, intra-session sodium-containing fluid, and post-session rehydration.
2. Cramping at rest or at night → consider dietary magnesium. Supplemental magnesium glycinate or citrate (200–400 mg elemental) in the evening is the practical first intervention.
3. Active weight cutting → weight cutting involving fluid restriction can cause severe electrolyte imbalances; refer to Art. 76 cautions.
4. Severe cramping with dark urine or signs of kidney stress → refer to a physician.

### GI Issues Around Training — Check Sequence:
1. Pre-training meal timing: meal consumed within 30–60 min of training causes GI distress → move meal earlier; reduce fat and fiber closer to training.
2. Intra-session nutrition: concentrated carbohydrate solutions slow gastric emptying → dilute sports drinks or gels with extra water.
3. New supplements/ingredients: any new supplement recently introduced may be the cause → remove and reassess.
4. Lactose or whey sensitivity: if GI issues follow protein shakes → switch to whey isolate or plant-based protein.
5. Persistent GI symptoms unrelated to training or nutrition changes → refer to physician.

### Poor Sleep from Nutrition — Check Sequence:
1. Caffeine timing: limit caffeine to before noon or early afternoon.
2. Pre-sleep nutrition: large high-carbohydrate meal immediately before sleep may impair sleep quality in some individuals.
3. Alcohol: impairs sleep architecture, reducing slow-wave and REM sleep.
4. Magnesium deficiency: associated with sleep disruption.
5. High stimulant supplement use late in the day: a common and easily correctable cause.

### Bodyweight Drift — Decision Trees:

**Unexpected weight gain:**
- Creatine loading phase? (Expected BW gain 0.5–2 kg from intramuscular water.)
- New hypertrophy phase with increased caloric intake?
- Gain disproportionate to calorie intake?
- Unexplained rapid weight gain with swelling, breathlessness, or other systemic symptoms → refer to physician.

**Unexpected weight loss:**
- Weight loss intentional and at appropriate rate?
- Athlete in hard training and losing weight faster than expected? (Check calorie adequacy.)
- Weight loss unexplained with fatigue, low appetite, and poor performance? → refer to physician.

**Goal-agnostic note:** These troubleshooting check sequences apply across all goal classes. The principle is always: address nutrition deficits systematically before attributing problems to training programming.

---

## Cluster-Level Cross-Reference Summary

**Cluster F → G handshake:** VCS (from Cluster G) converts planned volume into the same cost language as Cluster F stress-cost scoring. Run volume thresholds first (target dose), then filter through stress-cost (what the week affords).

**Cluster G → H handshake:** Nutrition readiness score (Art. 77) is an override layer on top of all volume prescriptions from Cluster G. A Red nutrition readiness score converts any High day to active recovery/rest regardless of what the volume layer prescribes.

**Universal deload triggers (apply across Clusters F, G, H):**
- Two recovery channels simultaneously Red (Cluster F).
- AR < 0 on any priority channel (Cluster G).
- Quality (bar speed, SQS, ROM, sport sharpness) down 2+ sessions (both clusters).
- Constraint flag escalates (Cluster F).
- Nutrition readiness averages below 8 for 5+ consecutive sessions (Cluster H).
- CFS Saturated for 2 consecutive weeks (Cluster F).

**Language discipline (hard rule across all three clusters):** No medical claims; no injury-prevention guarantees; no diagnoses; no named conditions. Use: capacity, tolerance, load-management, freshness, quality, recovery, reserve language only.

## PART D — Stateful Coaching, Sport Adjustments, Competition Prep & Recovery Routing (Articles 79–102)

## Clusters J / K / L / M — Articles 79–102
## Ongoing Coaching, Sport-Specific Adjustment, Competition Cycle, Data Interpretation

---

## 1. Stateful Coaching Mode — Program Generator → Ongoing Coach

**PRINCIPLE:** Once a program is delivered, the engine enters a persistent coaching-agent state whose sole job is to carry the client through the end of the current block. (Art. 79)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Active Program State Object: {current_block, current_week, session_sequence, load_params, disruption_log, substitution_log, check-in_log}
- Five message categories: (a) check-in, (b) disruption, (c) substitution, (d) clarification, (e) general feedback
- Escalation triggers: structural mismatch, Level 4 fatigue, 2× consecutive holds unresolved, end-of-block handoff complete

**Rules:**
- IF client sends any message → classify into categories (a)–(e) BEFORE any response or program change.
- IF no disruption signal → affirm adherence, prompt next session.
- IF disruption signal → route to Art. 81 (schedule) or Art. 82 (fatigue).
- IF substitution request → route to Art. 83.
- IF end-of-week update → route to Art. 84 check-in protocol.
- IF "I want a new program" → acknowledge, confirm block-end status, initiate new intake.
- IF ambiguous message → ask exactly ONE clarifying question; do not assume and route.
- IF 1 disruption in block → noise; do not restructure.
- IF 2+ disruptions in block → pattern; flag.
- IF 3+ disruptions in block → coaching problem; structural fix required.
- NEVER revert to intake behavior mid-block unless explicitly triggered.
