- NEVER treat every message as a program-generation trigger.
- NEVER over-adjust for single-session complaints.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Applies identically regardless of athlete goal (strength, BJJ, running, hypertrophy). The block structure being protected is whatever was generated for that client's stated objective.

---

## 2. Follow-Up Question Triage — Message Classification Without Program Rebuild

**PRINCIPLE:** Every incoming client message in coaching mode must pass through a triage decision tree before any protocol is activated; response depth matches message depth. (Art. 80)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Category 1: Adherence check-in (no action to program)
- Category 2: Disruption report → Art. 81/82
- Category 3: Substitution request → Art. 83
- Category 4: Clarification question (no program change)
- Category 5: General feedback/emotion (acknowledge + probe)

**Rules (Triage Decision Tree):**
```
INCOMING MESSAGE
     │
     ▼
Disruption signal present? ─ YES ──► Cat 2 → Art. 81/82
     │ NO
     ▼
Substitution request? ────── YES ──► Cat 3 → Art. 83
     │ NO
     ▼
Direct question? ──────────── YES ──► Cat 4 → Answer directly; do NOT alter program
     │ NO
     ▼
Log / completion signal? ─── YES ──► Cat 1 → Affirm briefly
     │ NO
     ▼
General statement/emotion ──────────► Cat 5 → Acknowledge + one probe question
```
- IF Cat 1 or Cat 4 → no program change.
- IF Cat 4 (curiosity) → NEVER treat as Cat 2 (resistance).
- IF Cat 2 confirmed → Cat 1–5 status overridden; route immediately.
- One-sentence check-in → 2–3 sentence acknowledgment maximum.
- Ambiguity → ask ONE targeted question; not two.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Triage logic is goal-independent; the same five categories and tree apply whether the program is a 10K plan, powerlifting cycle, or BJJ camp prep.

---

## 3. Missed Session & Schedule Disruption Protocols

**PRINCIPLE:** Make the smallest schedule adjustment that preserves training productivity; never catch up missed strength work on back-to-back days; skip before compress for primary sessions. (Art. 81)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Type A: Single missed session (isolated week)
- Type B: 2+ sessions missed in one week
- Type C: Entire week missed
- Type D: Recurring pattern across 2+ weeks (structural mismatch)

**Rules:**
- IF Type A, primary lift day → attempt to move session within 48 h; if not possible, skip; do NOT add make-up sets to next session.
- IF Type A, accessory/conditioning day → fold key accessory into next session as secondary if feasible; otherwise skip entirely.
- IF Type B → identify 2 highest-priority sessions; protect them; drop lowest-priority session(s).
- IF Type C, Week 1 → repeat the week.
- IF Type C, Week 2 → judgment call; lean toward repeating.
- IF Type C, Week 3–4 → skip; move to next block or planned deload.
- IF Type C due to illness → add 1 deload week regardless of block position before resuming.
- IF Type D (2+ weeks) → explicitly flag pattern; ask ONE diagnostic question about actual schedule; prepare schedule adjustment for next block.
- NEVER restructure block mid-block for a single disruption event.
- Week 1–2 missed session = lower consequence than Week 3–4 missed session.

**Goal-agnostic note:** Block-position weighting applies across all goal types. An early-block miss in a hypertrophy program or a marathon plan is lower-consequence than a late-block miss.

---

## 4. Fatigue, Soreness & Readiness-Based Weekly Adjustments

**PRINCIPLE:** Volume is the first adjustment lever (reduce sets before reducing weight); Level 4 fatigue is a deload trigger, not an adjustment trigger. (Art. 82)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Level 1: Normal DOMS; muscle-specific; resolves 48–72 h; joint integrity intact.
- Level 2: Elevated but manageable; above baseline but not limiting; movement quality intact.
- Level 3: Multiple concurrent signals — poor sleep ≥ 3 nights, persistent soreness not resolving, mood drop, performance decline ≥ 2 sessions.
- Level 4: Overreached/non-functional — meaningful performance decline, joint soreness, gym avoidance/dread.

**Rules:**
- Ask 2 questions before adjusting: (1) Is sleep disrupted? (2) Is performance declining or only perception declining?
- IF Level 1 → no change; optional: remind recovery basics. Do NOT reduce load.
- IF Level 2 → cut 1–2 working sets; optionally reduce top-set intensity 5–10%. Do NOT eliminate sessions.
- IF Level 3 → reduce volume 30–40%; keep intensity; consider session consolidation. Do NOT skip block-critical lifts.
- IF Level 4 → full deload week; evaluate next-block entry. Do NOT continue normal training. Deload cannot be substituted with light sessions.
- IF fatigue signals appear in last week of block → expected; no adjustment required unless Level 4.
- NEVER distinguish soreness from pain by RPE alone: soreness = diffuse, 24–48 h delayed, resolves; pain = sharp, joint-associated, acute-onset, non-resolving.

**Adjustment Toolkit (compact table):**
| Level | Primary Tool | Secondary Tool | Prohibited |
|-------|-------------|----------------|------------|
| 1 | No change | Remind recovery basics | Reduce load |
| 2 | Cut 1–2 working sets | Reduce top-set intensity 5–10% | Eliminate sessions |
| 3 | Reduce volume 30–40%, keep intensity | Session consolidation | Skip block-critical lifts |
| 4 | Full deload week | Assess next-block entry | Continue normal training |

**Goal-agnostic note:** Thresholds apply identically across goal types. A BJJ athlete at Level 3 and a powerlifter at Level 3 receive the same volume-reduction logic; the pattern of disruption (mat sessions vs. gym sessions) differs but the classification does not.

---

## 5. Substitution Requests — Equipment / Time / Pain / Preference Routing

**PRINCIPLE:** Identify the substitution driver before selecting a substitute; the substitute must replicate the original's primary training intent. (Art. 83)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Driver 1: Equipment unavailability (loading pattern match required)
- Driver 2: Time constraint (primary lifts preserved; accessories cut first)
- Driver 3: Pain signal (movement-based substitution removing aggravating element)
- Driver 4: Preference/boredom (lowest priority; requires confirmation of same training intent)

**Rules:**
- IF Driver 3 → ask ONE pain probe: "Is it sharp pain during movement, or a dull ache afterward?" before routing.
- IF sharp pain during movement → treat as Orange/Red pain flag (see Art. 101); do not just substitute.
- IF Driver 2 → preserve primary strength work; accessory work is first to cut.
- IF Driver 4 → confirm substitute serves same training intent before accepting.
- Priority order when multiple drivers present: Pain > Equipment > Time > Preference.

**Movement Pattern Substitution Map:**
| Pattern | Substitution Chain |
|---------|-------------------|
| Hip Hinge | RDL → stiff-leg DL → good morning → cable pull-through → single-leg RDL |
| Squat | Back squat → front squat → goblet squat → safety bar squat → leg press (last resort; non-equivalent) |
| Horizontal Push | BB bench → DB bench → cable press → loaded push-up → landmine press |
| Horizontal Pull | BB row → DB row → cable row → chest-supported row → seal row |
| Vertical Pull | Pull-up → lat pulldown → assisted pull-up → single-arm cable pulldown |
| Vertical Push | OHP → seated DB press → landmine press → cable overhead press |
| Knee Flexion | Leg curl → Nordic curl → Swiss ball curl → single-leg curl → GHR |

**Goal-agnostic note:** The substitution chain is pattern-based, not goal-based. A grappler needing to swap the RDL follows the same chain as a powerlifter; the selected variant may differ based on context (e.g., grip fatigue → leg press over RDL), but the decision logic is identical.

---

## 6. Progress Check-In Protocols — Weekly Updates, Load Decisions, Next-Block Handoffs

**PRINCIPLE:** Every weekly check-in produces one of four explicit load decisions (Progress/Hold/Reduce/Deload) based on five data inputs; block handoff follows a five-step protocol. (Art. 84)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Five check-in data points: (1) adherence, (2) performance feel (Easy/On target/Hard/Failed), (3) fatigue 1–10, (4) disruptions, (5) flags.
- Decision 1 (Progress): ≥80% adherence, performance on target or easy, fatigue manageable, no major disruptions → increase load per program's progression scheme.
- Decision 2 (Hold): most sessions completed, performance hard but not failed, some fatigue → keep load identical.
- Decision 3 (Reduce): multiple sessions missed OR performance declining OR fatigue ≥ Level 3 → reduce volume 20–30%, maintain intensity.
- Decision 4 (Deload): Level 4 fatigue OR consistent decline ≥ 2 check-ins OR end-of-block deload week.

**Rules:**
- Progress requires ≥ 80% adherence (hard threshold).
- Hold is an active strategic choice; frame explicitly to client, not as failure.
- IF 2 consecutive holds on same lift → diagnostic: recovery vs. technique breakdown vs. starting-load miscalibration?
- Reduce before deloading in ambiguous cases.
- Log every load decision with rationale.

**Next-Block Handoff — 5-Step Protocol:**
1. Block Summary: compile adherence rate, load progression, disruptions, fatigue patterns, substitutions.
2. Performance Assessment: identify progressed/held/stalled/disrupted lifts.
3. Client Input: 3 questions — "Most productive this block?" / "Most limiting?" / "More or less of what?"
4. Next-Block Parameters: volume adjustment, intensity trajectory, schedule changes, permanent substitutions.
5. New Program Generation Trigger: only after Steps 1–4 complete.

**Escalation Triggers (legitimate exits from stateful coaching mode):**
- Type D recurring disruption (structural schedule mismatch)
- Level 4 fatigue → deload → reassessment
- 2 consecutive holds same primary lift, unresolved
- End-of-block handoff Steps 1–4 complete

**Goal-agnostic note:** Load decision logic and handoff protocol are goal-agnostic. The same five-step handoff applies whether transitioning from a hypertrophy block, a running meso, or a BJJ camp cycle.

---

## 7. BJJ & Grappling Adjustment Rules

**PRINCIPLE:** Mat load is the primary constraint variable; pulling volume and grip-intensive work are the first levers cut; competition prep routing activates at T-4 weeks. (Art. 85)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Mat Load: mat hours/week × live rolling intensity + drilling volume
- Key stressor channels: grip fatigue, neck/upper-back stress, spinal compression load, competition proximity
- Grip fatigue rating ≥ 7/10 → activates ≥10 mat hours protocol regardless of actual mat hours

**Rules (If/Then):**
- IF mat hours ≥ 10/week → cut gym pulling volume 50%; remove all grip-intensive accessory; replace bilateral squats with split squats/step-ups; reduce axial loading sessions 2x→1x/week; upper body focus = pressing + overhead stability only.
- IF mat hours 6–9/week → maintain primary strength lifts at base volume; reduce pulling accessory 25%; monitor grip RPE — if ≥7/10 → apply ≥10 protocol immediately; no neck-loaded accessory.
- IF mat hours ≤ 5/week → standard gym template; light grip-specific prehab permitted; neck isometrics safe.
- IF competition within 4 weeks → reduce total gym sets 35%; keep 1 heavy lower + 1 heavy upper/week for neural maintenance; eliminate all new exercises.
- IF neck pain ≥ 3/10 → remove all axial loading immediately; horizontal pulling at submaximal loads only; flag for sports medicine before returning to axial loading.
- IF weight cut active (within 10 days of weigh-in) → maintenance only; no loading increases; cut all high-RPE sessions; volume reduced 40–50% of base.

**Generator Hard Rules:**
1. Mat hours input required before generating weekly plan.
2. Mat hours ≥ 10 → total weekly pulling sets hard-capped at 6 working sets.
3. Grip fatigue ≥ 7 → apply ≥10 protocol regardless of reported mat hours.
4. Competition week (T-0) → activation only; no strength work above 70% 1RM.
5. Neck pain ≥ 3/10 → all axial loading locked out until cleared.
6. Weight cut flag → override all progressive loading rules; maintenance-only mode.

**Red/Yellow/Green Flags:**
- **Red (stop/reroute):** neck pain ≥ 4/10 axial loading; grip failure in gym; acute cervical stiffness limiting ROM; weight cut + high mat + heavy gym simultaneously.
- **Yellow (modify):** grip fatigue 6–7/10; mat hours ≥ 25% above prior week; skipping food between mat and gym; main lifts down ≥ 2 consecutive weeks during high mat phase.
- **Green (proceed):** mat hours ≤ 5/week, no grip complaints; sleep ≥ 7 h, appetite normal, mood positive; no competition within 6 weeks; lifts stable or improving.

---

## 8. Boxing & Striking Adjustment Rules

**PRINCIPLE:** Sparring is a binary flag that immediately caps pressing volume; the gym corrects the internal-rotation imbalance from boxing—never compounds it. (Art. 86)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Sparring sessions/week: categorical variable; any sparring = sparring flag ON
- High conditioning density: ≥ 5 bag/pad sessions/week
- Footwork sessions: ≥ 4/week triggers plyometric lockout

**Rules (If/Then):**
- IF sparring scheduled any amount this week → cut pressing volume 40%; remove all overhead pressing; maintain external rotation + shoulder stability at full volume; reduce plyometric lower body 50%; keep 1 primary lower session.
- IF sparring ≥ 3 sessions this week → gym max 2 sessions; primary lifts only; no accessory volume; no new loading (maintain current intensities only).
- IF conditioning density ≥ 5 bag/pad sessions → gym 2 sessions; lower volume 30% all categories.
- IF footwork sessions ≥ 4/week → remove all plyometric lower body from gym; replace with slow eccentrics + single-leg stability; add calf/Achilles prehab.
- IF competition within 3 weeks → pressing at 50% of base; shoulder stability at full volume; all sessions maintenance; no progressive overload.

**Generator Hard Rules:**
1. Sparring flag is binary; overrides all volume rules immediately.
2. Active boxing phases → pressing never exceeds 60% of base. Sparring weeks → pressing never exceeds 35%.
3. External rotation + face pulls + scapular work are non-negotiable in every session.
4. Footwork ≥ 4/week → all plyometric lower body blocked.
5. Any concussion/acute head impact → zero gym work that week; medical clearance required.
6. Overhead pressing eliminated entirely from T-3 weeks to fight week.

---

## 9. MMA Hybrid Adjustment Rules

**PRINCIPLE:** Apply the more restrictive of grappling and striking constraints when both are active; weight-cut protocol overrides all sport-specific rules and then halves the resulting output. (Art. 87)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Fight camp phases: General Prep (10–12 weeks out), Specific Prep (6–9 weeks out), Peak/Taper (1–5 weeks out)
- Wrestling adder: each wrestling/clinch session = +1 lower-back fatigue unit
- Weight-cut override: activates within 14 days of weigh-in

**Rules (If/Then):**
- IF grappling ≥ 3/week AND striking ≥ 3/week → apply both rule sets; resolve all conflicts by taking more restrictive; gym max 2 sessions/week; 1 primary lift per session; remove all accessory, plyometrics, grip-intensive, overhead pressing.
- IF weight cut active (within 14 days) → override all sport-specific rules; gym volume at 50% of sport-adjusted template; intensity capped at 80% 1RM; session duration capped at 45 min.
- IF weight cut + high mat + high striking all active → 1 gym session/week maximum; maintenance only; flag coach that athlete is at maximum tolerable stress.
- IF fight camp General Prep (10–12 wks out) → gym at 80–90% of base; strength development priority.
- IF fight camp Specific Prep (6–9 wks out) → gym at 60–70% of base; no new exercises introduced.
- IF fight camp Peak/Taper (1–5 wks out) → gym at 30–45% of base; 1–2 sessions/week; primary lifts only; T-1 week: activation only, no heavy loading.
- IF wrestling/clinch ≥ 3 sessions → lower-back load reduction protocol activates.

**Generator Hard Rules:**
1. Dual-sport conflict → always take the more restrictive constraint; never average.
2. Wrestling adder: each wrestling/clinch session +1 lower-back fatigue unit; ≥ 3 units → lower-back load reduction.
3. Weight-cut override replaces sport-rule output, then cuts result by 50%.
4. Engine must detect or prompt for fight camp phase before generating.
5. Weight-cut sessions: 45-min duration cap hard-coded.
6. PRs blocked when weight-cut flag active.

---

## 10. Running & Field-Sport Adjustment Rules

**PRINCIPLE:** The gym's primary role for running/field athletes is tendon health, force production maintenance, and speed enhancement—not additional fatigue; heavy lower body and speed sessions must be ≥ 48 h apart. (Art. 88)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Mileage tiers: <40 km/week (standard gym), 40–69 km/week (reduced lower body), ≥70 km/week (maintenance gym only)
- Speed sessions: sprint/interval sessions; ≥ 2/week triggers plyometric restriction
- In-season: competition game/race scheduled that week

**Rules (If/Then):**
- IF running ≥ 70 km/week → gym lower body 1 session/week; no plyometrics; eccentric-focused lower body max 1 set/session; priority: tendon prehab (calf raise, tibialis, hip stability).
- IF running 40–69 km/week → 2 lower body gym sessions/week; plyometrics: 1 low-intensity session permitted if not within 48 h of tempo or speed.
- IF speed sessions ≥ 2/week → heavy gym lower body on non-sprint days or ≥ 48 h after sprint sessions; no plyometrics same day or day after speed; hamstring eccentric volume halved.
- IF in-season, competition game this week → 1 gym session at maintenance load (75–80% 1RM, reduced volume); no new exercises, plyometrics, or intensity PRs.
- IF tendon pain reported (Achilles, patellar, hamstring origin) → remove all plyometrics; remove eccentric-focused exercises for affected tendon; substitute heavy isometric protocols; flag for physio if pain ≥ 3/10 under load.

**Generator Hard Rules:**
1. 48-hour separation rule: heavy gym lower body ≥ 48 h from sport speed/sprint sessions; gym moves, not sport session.
2. In-season vs. off-season required input → sets development vs. maintenance mode.
3. Speed sessions ≥ 2/week → plyometric gym volume automatically reduced/eliminated.
4. Tendon pain ≥ 3/10 → eccentric + plyometric work removed; isometric protocols substituted.
5. Mileage tier system: <40 / 40–69 / ≥70 km/week determines base template.

---

## 11. Hybrid Athlete Adjustment Rules

**PRINCIPLE:** Establish a primary goal hierarchy before generating; strength and endurance same-day adds +15% fatigue multiplier to next-day recovery; minimum 2 complete recovery days/week hard-coded. (Art. 89)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Primary goals: strength-primary, endurance-primary, or body-composition-primary
- Modalities: strength, endurance, skill, body composition
- Concurrent session penalty: +15% fatigue multiplier when strength + endurance same day

**Rules (If/Then):**
- IF primary goal = strength → 3–4 strength sessions/week with progressive overload; endurance 2/week low–moderate intensity; skill on non-heavy days or morning sessions.
- IF primary goal = endurance → endurance at full volume (apply Art. 88 rules); strength 2/week maintenance mode.
- IF primary goal = body composition → strength 3/week moderate volume 8–12 rep ranges; endurance 2–3/week moderate intensity; caloric deficit 400–600 kcal/day.
- IF all four modalities at high volume → flag as unsustainable; apply 4-week rotation: strength emphasis → endurance emphasis → skill emphasis → recovery week.
- IF skill performance declining despite training → move skill sessions to first of day; fatigue-generating sessions to afternoon/evening; IF skill decline persists ≥ 2 weeks → reduce total training volume 20%.
- Separate strength and endurance by ≥ 6 h minimum; ≥ 24 h preferred.
- Skill sessions always placed before fatigue-generating sessions.
- Body composition caloric deficit capped at 300–500 kcal/day when all modalities active.
- IF caloric deficit >500 kcal/day and high training load → generate warning; reduce volume recommendations.

**Generator Hard Rules:**
1. Primary goal declaration required before generating hybrid program.
2. Skill sessions always generated first in day sequence.
3. Same-day strength + endurance → apply +15% fatigue multiplier to next-day recovery.
4. Deficit >500 kcal + high load → auto-warning + volume reduction.
5. 2 complete recovery days per 7-day microcycle hard-coded minimum.
6. All four modalities at high volume → auto-suggest 4-week block periodization.

---

## 12. Sport-Interference Decision Matrix — Push / Maintain / Reduce / Deload

**PRINCIPLE:** Generate exactly one of four gym states per week per athlete; the most conservative state always wins when multiple inputs conflict; Deload > Reduce > Maintain > Push. (Art. 90)

**Definitions (internal):**
- PUSH: progressive overload appropriate; all conditions support loading increases.
- MAINTAIN: current loads/volumes held constant; default during high sport-load weeks.
- REDUCE: specific percentage volume pullback; magnitude depends on trigger count.
- DELOAD: 40–50% volume of base; 60–70% intensity of working weights; 2 sessions max; primary lifts only; accessories removed; 30–45 min sessions.

**Route to PUSH (ALL must be true):**
- Sport sessions ≤ 5/week; none classified high-intensity sparring or competition
- Sleep ≥ 7 h average
- RPE on primary lifts at or below expected
- Gym performance stable or improving
- Competition ≥ 8 weeks out
- No active injury or pain flags
- No weight cut active
- Currently in accumulation or early intensification block

**Route to MAINTAIN (ANY, with no red flags):**
- Sport sessions 5–8/week, moderate intensity
- Sleep averaging 6.5–7 h
- RPE at expected level (not below)
- Gym performance stable
- Competition 4–8 weeks out
- No active injury; minor soreness only
- No weight cut active

**Route to REDUCE (ANY):**
- Sport sessions ≥ 8/week OR ≥ 3 high-intensity sport sessions
- Sleep averaging < 6.5 h for 3+ consecutive days
- RPE on primary lifts trending up ≥ 1.5 points above expected for 2+ weeks
- Gym performance declining ≥ 2 consecutive sessions
- Competition 2–4 weeks out
- Weight cut initiated
- Minor injury/tendon complaint (pain 1–3/10)

**Reduce magnitude:**
- 1 trigger → reduce volume 20%
- 2 triggers → reduce volume 30%
- 3+ triggers → reduce volume 40%; apply Deload at next check-in

**Route to DELOAD (ANY immediately triggers):**
- 3+ Reduce triggers active simultaneously
- Performance declining all gym sessions for 3+ consecutive weeks
- Active injury (pain ≥ 3/10 on any loaded movement)
- Weight cut within 7 days of weigh-in
- Competition within 1 week
- Athlete cannot complete sport sessions due to gym fatigue
- 6+ weeks of prior training without a deload

**Integrated Sport-Specific State Override Table:**
| Sport Context | Default State | Override Condition | Override State |
|---------------|--------------|-------------------|----------------|
| BJJ, mat ≥ 10 h/week | MAINTAIN | + comp < 4 wks | DELOAD |
| BJJ, neck pain active | REDUCE | Pain ≥ 4/10 | DELOAD |
| Boxing, sparring ≥ 3/week | REDUCE | + pressing complaint | DELOAD |
| Boxing, no sparring, cond ≤ 3 | MAINTAIN or PUSH | Performance improving | PUSH |
| MMA, weight cut active | REDUCE | Cut within 7 days | DELOAD |
| MMA, fight camp General Prep | MAINTAIN or PUSH | Performance trending up | PUSH |
| MMA, fight camp Peak | REDUCE | T-1 week | DELOAD |
| Running, mileage ≥ 70 km/week | REDUCE | Tendon pain active | DELOAD |
| Running, mileage < 40 km, off-season | MAINTAIN or PUSH | Strength developing | PUSH |
| Field sport, in-season game week | MAINTAIN | 2+ games/week | REDUCE |
| Hybrid, all modalities high | REDUCE | Sleep < 6 h + decline | DELOAD |
| Hybrid, primary goal aligned, good recovery | MAINTAIN or PUSH | All green flags | PUSH |

**Escalation Protocol:**
- MAINTAIN for ≥ 4 consecutive weeks without gym improvement → flag to coach; reassess.
- REDUCE with 3+ triggers simultaneously → escalate directly to DELOAD (do not apply another REDUCE week).
- Post-DELOAD → mandatory return to MAINTAIN first; no athlete goes DELOAD → PUSH directly.
- PUSH → high sport-load week → drops to MAINTAIN or REDUCE depending on load severity.

**Generator Hard Rules:**
1. One state per week; exactly one.
2. State hierarchy: Deload > Reduce > Maintain > Push.
3. Mandatory deload triggers are hard-coded; cannot be overridden without clinical documentation logged.
4. Post-deload lock: engine locked to MAINTAIN for following week.
5. MAINTAIN time cap: ≥ 4 consecutive weeks → mandatory flag + reassessment.
6. Sport load = primary input; always takes precedence over gym performance data.

---

## 13. Taper Decision Rules — Fatigue Reduction Without Fitness Loss

**PRINCIPLE:** The taper strips accumulated fatigue while preserving neuromuscular drive; intensity is preserved; volume is what falls; final heavy session ≥ day –5 for strength, ≥ day –3 for skill/speed athletes. (Art. 91)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Exponential taper: steep volume drop early in window, flattens near competition; default for 10–14-day tapers; most evidence-supported for strength-power athletes.
- Linear taper: consistent % reduction each day/week; simple; works for predictable fatigue responders.
- Step taper: large single volume drop at start, then holds steady; for athletes responding poorly to gradual reductions.
- Readiness prime: for undertrained/injury-managed athletes entering final block.

**Taper Initiation Decision (Step 1):**
- IF high volume (≥ 8 training units/week) → full structured taper 10–14 days.
- IF moderate volume (5–7 units/week near baseline) → short taper 7–10 days.
- IF undertrained or managing injury entering final block → use "readiness prime" protocol; skip standard taper.

**Primary Demand Determines Taper Structure (Step 2):**
- Max strength (powerlifting, weightlifting, strongman): keep 70–90% of peak intensity; cut volume to 40–60% of peak by competition week.
- Power-endurance / sport-skill (combat sport, CrossFit, team): intensity near competition speed; volume cuts 50–70%.
- Both strength + skill: two-phase taper — days 10–5 out: reduce volume, preserve intensity; days 4–1 out: reduce intensity load, preserve movement quality and speed.

**Taper Timing Table:**
| Competition Type | Taper Start | Intensity Preservation | Volume by Day –1 |
|-----------------|-------------|----------------------|-------------------|
| Powerlifting / Olympic WL | 14 days out | 90–95% of peak | 30–40% of peak |
| Strongman / Highland Games | 10–12 days out | 85–90% of peak | 40–50% of peak |
| Combat sport (strength camp) | 10 days out | 80% of peak | 50–60% of peak |
| CrossFit / Hybrid | 7–10 days out | 75–85% | 40–55% of peak |
| Team sport competition week | 5–7 days out | 70–80% | 50–70% of peak |

**Non-Negotiable Timing Rules:**
- No new movements or loading patterns within 10 days of competition.
- No DOMS-inducing work within 7 days of competition.
- Final heavy stimulus: ≤ day –5 (strength athletes); ≤ day –3 (skill/speed-dominant).
- Day –1: activation only.

**Readiness Extension Rules (Step 3):**
- SRS < 6 for 3+ consecutive days → extend taper 2–3 days.
- HRV declining trend → reduce volume further.
- Bar speed/jump performance at RPE 7 drops >10% below baseline → fatigue not yet cleared; extend taper.
- Sleep quality consistently 4–5 → prioritize sleep intervention before training manipulation.

**What to Remove During Taper:**
- Hypertrophy-only accessory volume
- High-fatigue conditioning methods
- Technical drilling of new/corrected patterns
- Recreational activity with significant musculoskeletal loading
- Hard sparring competition week

**What to Keep:**
- Competition-specific movements at competition intensity
- Submaximal motor pattern reinforcement
- Sport-skill rehearsal at speed
- Low-intensity aerobic work (10–20 min easy bike/walk)
- Competition-day warm-up sequence rehearsed ≥ 2× during taper

**Common Errors (internal flags):**
- Cutting volume only 20–30% (athletes arrive fatigued)
- Removing intensity with volume (intensity stays; volume falls)
- Adding new recovery modalities week before competition
- Adding volume back mid-taper because athlete "feels great" (recovered feeling = taper working, not green light to add volume)

---

## 14. Competition Week Microcycles

**PRINCIPLE:** Competition week goal is controlled expression of accumulated fitness at the correct moment—not training; build backward from Day 0. (Art. 92)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Day 0: competition day
- Day –1: activation only (CNS primer, psychological routine)
- Day –2: last technical session (submaximal quality, no fatigue)
- Day –3: optional light conditioning or skill maintenance; no strength training (pure strength athletes)
- Day –4: last near-maximal session (1–3 reps at 90–93% for strength athletes); last heavy session for skill athletes if slow recovery profile shifts to day –6/–7
- Day –5 to –7: reduced volume, preserved intensity, no new demands

**Type A — Absolute Strength (powerlifting, weightlifting, strongman):**
| Day | Session |
|-----|---------|
| –7 | Moderate volume strength (60–70% peak vol, 85–90% intensity) |
| –6 | Rest or light aerobic/recovery |
| –5 | Light technical — pattern rehearsal, no fatigue |
| –4 | Last heavy: low vol, high intensity (1–3 sets × 1–3 reps @ 90–95%) |
| –3 | Full rest or light movement only |
| –2 | Activation + technical cue rehearsal |
| –1 | Activation only |
| 0 | Compete |

**Type B — Skill + Strength (combat sport, functional fitness):**
| Day | Session |
|-----|---------|
| –7 | Skill-speed + strength component |
| –6 | Strength maintenance |
| –5 | Skill-only; no heavy loading |
| –4 | Light conditioning + movement quality |
| –3 | Rest or active recovery only |
| –2 | Light skill rehearsal; no fatigue |
| –1 | Activation + routine walkthrough |
| 0 | Compete |

**Type C — Endurance-Strength Hybrid:**
| Day | Session |
|-----|---------|
| –7 | Moderate conditioning |
| –6 | Strength maintenance (moderate load) |
| –5 | Short skill + active recovery |
| –4 | Rest or light aerobic only |
| –3 | Short activation + movement quality |
| –2 | Rest |
| –1 | Activation walkthrough |
| 0 | Compete |

**Conditioning Placement Rules:**
- Never high-intensity conditioning within 72 h of competition.
- Never conditioning + near-maximal strength in same session during competition week.
- Low-intensity aerobic on rest days: maintains metabolic function, reduces "flat" feeling.
- Combat sport: technical-only by day –4; contact ends day –5 minimum.

**Strength Placement Rules:**
- Last heavy stimulus: day –5 to –4 (standard recovery); –6 to –7 (slow recovery profile).
- No eccentric-dominant training in competition week.
- No DOMS-inducing volume in competition week.

---

## 15. Travel Week & Low-Equipment Competition Prep

**PRINCIPLE:** Travel week sessions are activation + pattern maintenance only—not training; never convert hotel gym access into a training session; nutrition and sleep are prioritized over training optimization. (Art. 93)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Scenario A: same-day travel (<4 h transit, no overnight) → minimal impact.
- Scenario B: overnight domestic (1–2 nights, no time-zone change) → moderate impact; sleep drops 15–30%.
- Scenario C: international (3+ h time-zone change) → high impact; strength expression reduced 5–10% for 1–3 days.

**Jet Lag Decision Rules:**
- Eastbound (losing hours; harder) → arrive ≥ 3–4 days before competition; morning light exposure immediately on arrival.
- Westbound (gaining hours; easier) → arrive ≥ 2–3 days before competition; stay awake until local target sleep time on arrival night.
- Short trip ≤ 48 h with large time-zone change → do NOT attempt circadian shift; maintain home schedule as much as possible.

**Travel Session Structure (20–30 min):**
1. Soft tissue + mobility (5 min): thoracic rotation, hip flexor, ankle mobility
2. Activation sequence (10 min): glute bridges, banded clamshells, face pulls, scapular retractions
3. Movement pattern rehearsal (10–15 min): squat, hinge, push, pull at low load
4. Breathing/arousal regulation (5 min): box breathing or HRV protocol

**What can be maintained with minimal equipment:**
- Lower body: BW squat, single-leg work, band hip hinge
- Upper body: push-up variations, banded pressing, face pulls with band
- Core: anti-rotation or anti-extension

**What cannot be meaningfully maintained:**
- Absolute strength at competition-specific loads
- Sport-specific skill at full speed without appropriate equipment
- High-intensity glycolytic conditioning

**Nutrition rules during travel:**
- Maintain protein intake as close to normal as possible.
- No novel foods within 48 h of competition.
- Extra hydration: +0.5 L per 3 h of flight time.
- Alcohol: zero during competition travel week (non-negotiable).

---

## 16. Testing Decisions — When to Test, Estimate, or Avoid Max Attempts

**PRINCIPLE:** Test for programming calibration at block completion or competition; estimate between; never test when fatigued, within 3 weeks of competition, or when the purpose is coach curiosity. (Art. 94)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Purpose categories: programming calibration, competition performance, psychological milestone, coach curiosity.
- Mock session: 90–93% singles used in lieu of true max test within 4–6 weeks of competition.

**Testing Decision Tree:**
- Purpose = programming calibration → Step 2 (timing check).
- Purpose = competition performance → Step 3 (mock session rules).
- Purpose = psychological milestone → Step 4 (confidence check).
- Purpose = coach curiosity → DO NOT TEST; estimate.

**Appropriate to Test (programming calibration):**
- Completed full training block (8–12 weeks) since last test
- Working weights reached or exceeded projected training max
- Velocity/RPE data no longer matches projected maxes
- New training phase beginning

**Not Appropriate to Test (programming calibration):**
- Within 3 weeks of competition
- In deload or recovery week
- Managing active injury
- Training inconsistent for prior 4+ weeks

**Competition Testing Rules:**
- Strength sport (powerlifting/weightlifting/strongman): test no later than 3–4 weeks out; within 2 weeks is contraindicated; use mock session (90–93% singles) not true max.
- Combat sport: true max tests rarely meaningful; test sport-relevant qualities (force output at moderate fatigue, loaded carry, repeated power) rather than isolated 1RM.

**Psychological Milestone Authorization:**
- Physical readiness high
- Attempt at 90–95% confidence single
- ≥ 3 weeks adequate recovery time before next block/competition
- Athlete understands this is expression session, not all-out effort

**Estimation Over Testing — Use when:**
- Training proceeding normally, weights moving well (RPE estimation at submaximal loads provides accurate 1RM without fatigue/injury risk)
- Within 4–6 weeks of competition (use mock sessions)
- Returning from injury/illness (wait ≥ 3–4 weeks post-return)
- Environment cannot support safe missed attempts

**Avoid Max Attempts When:**
- Readiness < 7/10
- Poor sleep ≥ 2 consecutive nights
- Acute soft tissue injury, active joint inflammation, or unresolved pain
- Within 3 weeks of competition that matters
- Testing environment cannot ensure safe missed attempt
- Athlete emotionally dysregulated
- Technique degraded under recent loading

**Attempt Selection Rules (powerlifting/strength sport):**
- Opener: 92–95% of estimated max (can make on worst day of their life).
- Second: if opener moved at expected bar speed → 97–100% of estimated max; if heavy/technique degraded → cap at 97%.
- Third: record attempts or specific milestones only; requires pre-set green-light criteria.
- Rule: load for each attempt determined by prior attempt performance, not emotion.

---

## 17. Peaking Models — Strength, Multi-Quality, Combat Sport, Hybrid Conditioning

**PRINCIPLE:** The taper reduces fatigue; the peak is the intentional 8–16 week architectural design ensuring fitness, technique, and competitive readiness converge at a single target date; different competitive demands require different peak architectures. (Art. 95)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Model 1: Strength Peak (powerlifting/Olympic WL) — 12–16 weeks
- Model 2: Multi-Quality Peak (strongman/highland games/hybrid strength sport) — 10–14 weeks
- Model 3: Combat Sport Peak (fight camp) — 8–12 weeks
- Model 4: Hybrid Conditioning Peak (CrossFit/functional fitness) — 8–10 weeks

**Peak Model Decision (primary competitive demand):**
- Single-event maximal force output → Model 1
- Multi-event strength + power + skill → Model 2
- Strength + skill under accumulated physiological stress, weight management concurrent → Model 3
- Cyclic repeated-power output + strength maintenance → Model 4

**Model 1: Strength Peak (Powerlifting / Olympic WL) — 12–16 weeks:**
- Wks 1–4 (Accumulation): volume at/above baseline; intensity 70–82%; maximize adaptation, maintain technique under moderate load.
- Wks 5–8 (Intensification): volume decreasing; intensity 80–90%; technical mastery under heavier loads; introduce competition-specific singles and doubles.
- Wks 9–12 (Competition Prep/Realization): volume 50–65% of accumulation peak; intensity 90–97%; all work competition-movement focused; singles 90–95% with technical assessment.
- Wks 13–14: apply Art. 91 taper rules.
- Key indicators: bar speed at 85% measurably faster in wk 10 vs. wk 4; RPE at 90% drops from ~9 (wk 6) to ~8 (wk 11); technique at near-max cleaner in wk 11 than wk 7.

**Model 2: Multi-Quality Peak (Strongman / Highland Games) — 10–14 weeks:**
- Wks 1–3 (General Prep): mixed quality work — strength, power, conditioning, event training all present.
- Wks 4–7 (Specialization): prioritize competition events; reduce non-event work; strength becomes event-specific; conditioning matches event demands.
- Wks 8–10 (Competition Realization): events at near-competition loading + sequencing; simulate competition-day event order; high intensity, controlled volume.
- Wks 11–12 (Taper): reduce event volume 50%; maintain event speed and technical quality.

**Model 3: Combat Sport Peak — 8–12 weeks:**
- Wks 1–4 (Volume Base): high training volume all qualities; work density priority.
- Wks 5–8 (Intensification): volume drops; strength intensifies; sparring quality increases.
- Wks 9–10 (Competition Sharpening): volume drops significantly; strength sessions 2×/week maintenance loading only; sparring technical + controlled.
- Wks 11–12: apply Art. 92 competition week microcycle.
- Note: strength supports skill; technical/tactical sharpness = primary performance determinant.

**Model 4: Hybrid Conditioning Peak (CrossFit / Functional Fitness) — 8–10 weeks:**
- Wks 1–3 (Broad Base): high variety, all energy systems, strength maintained.
- Wks 4–6 (Event Specificity): training narrows toward likely competition demands.
- Wks 7–8 (Realization): near-competition rehearsals; full-effort simulated workouts.
- Wks 9–10 (Taper): reduce volume 40–50%; maintain competition-specific movement speed.

**Peaking Timing Table:**
| Competition | Peak Block Length | Taper Starts | Final Heavy Session |
|-------------|------------------|-------------|---------------------|
| Powerlifting | 12–16 weeks | 14 days out | Day –5 |
| Olympic Weightlifting | 10–14 weeks | 10 days out | Day –5 |
| Strongman | 10–12 weeks | 10 days out | Day –4 |
| Combat Sport | 8–12 weeks | 10 days out | Day –4 to –5 |
| CrossFit / Hybrid | 8–10 weeks | 7 days out | Day –3 to –4 |

---

## 18. Post-Competition Transition — Restoration, Rebuild, Next-Block Selection

**PRINCIPLE:** Post-competition transition is a distinct programming phase (not rest and not return-to-training); classify recovery need within 48 h; restoration before rebuild before next block selection. (Art. 96)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Category 1: Physically intact, psychologically satisfied → 7–10 day restoration.
- Category 2: Physically intact, psychologically disappointed → same physical restoration + psychological reset (goal clarity session, performance debrief, re-established buy-in).
- Category 3: Physical stress present → ≥ 14 days restoration; physical assessment before training resumption.
- Category 4: Major injury → full medical assessment; training timeline determined by injury management.

**Restoration Phase:**
- Days 1–3: no structured training; light movement only (walking, swimming, mobility); prioritize sleep, hydration, caloric restoration.
- Days 4–7: 2–3 light sessions, movement quality only, no loading; Zone 2 aerobic ≤ 20–30 min.
- Days 8–14 (rebuild entry evaluation): SRS back to ≥ 7 for 3 consecutive days; movement quality at baseline; sleep quality restored. IF any marker below threshold → extend restoration.

**Rebuild Phase (Weeks 2–4):**
- Begin at 50–60% of pre-taper volume.
- Intensity: 70–80% of pre-competition working loads.
- No max-effort work until week 3 of rebuild minimum.
- Week 1: ≤ 3–4 sessions.
- Week 2: 4–5 sessions; introduce secondary movements.
- Week 3: return to pre-competition session frequency if all markers clear.

**Next-Block Selection Logic (3 Questions):**
Q1: What did competition reveal?
- Strength limitation → next block emphasizes strength accumulation.
- Conditioning/work capacity limitation → energy system development block.
- Technical failure under fatigue/pressure → structured skill blocks under fatigue conditions.
- Psychological limitation → performance coaching + graduated competition exposure.

Q2: What is the next competition timeline?
- ≤ 6 weeks → compressed peak block immediately after rebuild.
- 8–12 weeks → short accumulation (4 weeks) → intensification → competition prep.
- 12–20 weeks → full program cycle.
- No upcoming competition → GPP block.

Q3: What is athlete's recovery and motivation state?
- Full recovery, high motivation → normal accumulation on schedule.
- Full recovery, low motivation → 2-week novelty block before structured accumulation.
- Incomplete recovery, high motivation → enforce extended restoration (high-motivation athletes = highest premature-return risk).
- Incomplete recovery, low motivation → extend restoration + address motivational factors before programmatic intervention.

**Common Errors (internal flags):**
- Returning to training within 3–5 days of competition.
- Treating post-competition as free training period.
- Selecting next block based on what coach wants vs. what competition revealed.
- Ignoring psychological component.
- Beginning next block without scheduling next competition (no target date = no peak structure).

---

## 19. Readiness Signal Hierarchy

**PRINCIPLE:** Signals are not equal; acute physiological signals outweigh self-report when conflicting in same direction; 5–7-day objective trends outweigh single-session snapshots; performance output is ground truth. (Art. 97)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Tier 1 (primary): HRV (rMSSD, 7-day rolling average), Subjective Readiness Score (SRS 1–10)
- Tier 2 (modifier): Resting Heart Rate (RHR), Sleep Quality Score, Perceived Stress Score
- Tier 3 (contextual/background): Bodyweight trend (5-day rolling), Nutrition compliance

**Tier 1 — HRV Rules:**
- Use 7-day rolling average as baseline; use rMSSD (preferred over SDNN).
- Single-day drop 10–15% with all other signals normal → monitor only; no adjustment.
- ≥ 2 consecutive mornings >10% below rolling average → concern threshold.
- Consecutive drops + confirmed poor sleep → reduce session load 15–20%.

**Tier 1 — SRS Rules:**
- SRS 8–10 → proceed as programmed.
- SRS 6–7 → proceed; monitor bar speed; apply +5% RPE ceiling.
- SRS 4–5 → reduce working set volume 20–25%; keep intensity; cut sets.
- SRS 1–3 → recovery-tier session: no top sets; technique work + submaximal volume at non-failure only.
- SRS administered pre-warm-up, before coach feedback or external cues.

**Tier 2 — RHR Rules:**
- >5 BPM above 30-day baseline → mild suppression flag.
- >10 BPM above baseline → confirming fatigue signal; downregulate volume.
- RHR alone without HRV or SRS confirmation → no program adjustment; flag for monitoring.

**Tier 2 — Sleep Quality Rules:**
- 1 poor night → no adjustment unless SRS also <6.
- 2 consecutive nights → reduce session complexity; drop accessory; keep primary movement.
- 3 consecutive nights → reduce working intensity 10%; reduce volume 20%; flag recovery week trigger.

**Tier 2 — Perceived Stress Rules:**
- Stress 6+ → no new PRs or max-arousal top sets.
- Stress 8–10 → treat as SRS 4–5 equivalent for volume/intensity modification.

**Signal Hierarchy Decision Tree:**
```
Both Tier 1 normal (HRV within 10%, SRS ≥ 8) → Proceed as programmed
One Tier 1 flagged:
  └─ Tier 2 confirms → reduce volume 15–20%
  └─ Tier 2 normal → monitor with RPE ceiling; do NOT cut volume preemptively
Both Tier 1 flagged → Move to modified session immediately (no Tier 2 wait)
Tier 1 normal, Tier 2 flagged only → No volume adjustment; remove PR attempts; post-session wellbeing check
```

**False Positive Guards:**
- HRV outside consistent conditions (post-alcohol, shift work, different time, fever) → unreliable; discard reading.
- Single bad HRV morning → do NOT adjust full training week.
- Athlete under-reporting SRS to avoid heavy sessions → cross-reference with HRV + actual bar speed during warm-up.

---

## 20. Performance Drop Interpretation — 4-Cause Classification

**PRINCIPLE:** Performance drops have exactly four possible root causes; each requires a different fix; misdiagnosis leads to wrong intervention. (Art. 98)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Cause 1: Acute dip (bad day)
- Cause 2: Accumulated fatigue
- Cause 3: Skill/technical regression
- Cause 4: Program error

**Cause 1: Acute Dip — Identification & Response:**
- Drop in one session only; prior 3–5 sessions at/above expected; HRV + SRS + sleep normal or mildly flagged; no exceptional stressor reported.
- → Interpretation: noise. No adjustment. Log and re-test at next scheduled heavy session.

**Cause 2: Accumulated Fatigue — Identification & Response:**
- Performance declined/stalled 2–4 sessions in a row; HRV sustained depression (below rolling average 3+ consecutive readings); RPE higher at same loads vs. 2–3 weeks ago; motivation declining.
- Confirmed threshold: 3+ consecutive sessions at ≤92% expected output AND HRV depressed ≥10% for 4+ days → confirmed overreaching → deload immediately.
- Adjustment: reduce volume 40–50% for 5–7 days; maintain intensity 70–80% of recent working loads; keep frequency (removing training days extends the hole); re-test at days 7–10.
- **False positive guard:** caloric deficit mimics accumulated fatigue almost perfectly → verify nutrition compliance + caloric intake prior 7–10 days before prescribing deload.

**Cause 3: Skill / Technical Regression — Identification & Response:**
- Movement quality visibly degraded at same or lower loads; cannot maintain bar path/depth/brace/position previously owned; drop specific to one lift, not supplementary movements for same muscle groups; no HRV/sleep/stress flags.
- Confirmed threshold: 2 sessions with clear technical breakdown at previously clean weight.
- Adjustment: reduce load to where technique is fully intact; use positional work, paused reps, or tempo variations to re-groove pattern.

**Cause 4: Program Error — Identification & Response:**
- Stagnant or declining since block start (not mid-block); no lifestyle/nutrition/stress cause; HRV + SRS suggest athlete is recovered; other lifts progressing while this variable is not.
- Confirmed threshold: 3+ weeks with no adaptation on a given variable despite appropriate readiness.
- Adjustment: change the primary stimulus (shift rep range, change movement variation, adjust load zone); review frequency; audit total weekly volume for target quality.

**Diagnostic Table:**
| Signal Pattern | Most Likely Cause | First Action |
|---------------|-------------------|--------------|
| One bad session, all signals normal | Acute dip | Log and continue |
| 3+ sessions declining, HRV depressed | Accumulated fatigue | Immediate deload |
| Technical breakdown, no physiological flags | Skill regression | Load reduction + technique work |
| No adaptation ≥ 3 weeks, athlete feels ready | Program error | Block redesign |

---

## 21. Bodyweight & Body Composition Trend Interpretation

**PRINCIPLE:** Bodyweight is a performance variable in strength programming; use 5–7-day rolling averages exclusively; single readings are noise; never adjust training or nutrition from a single weigh-in. (Art. 99)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Weigh-in protocol: morning, post-void, pre-food, same scale, same conditions.
- Frequency: daily optimal; minimum 3×/week.
- Rolling average: 5-day or 7-day; required for all trend decisions.

**Mass Gain Phase Targets:**
- Target rate: 0.25–0.5% bodyweight/week.
- IF >0.5%/week for >3 consecutive weeks → likely fat gain acceleration; review caloric surplus.
- IF <0.25%/week for 3+ weeks despite reported compliance → re-audit intake.

**Stable Bodyweight:**
- Stable BW + declining strength → caloric deficit OR recovery failure; investigate both.
- Stable BW + improving strength → appropriate; continue.

**Cut Phase Targets:**
- Intended cut target: 0.5–1.0% bodyweight/week.
- >1.0%/week → aggressive; expect some strength loss; reduce volume to preserve intensity.
- >1.5%/week → unacceptable for performance preservation.
- Unintended drops >0.5%/week for 2+ weeks → treat as fueling emergency regardless of athlete intent.

**Training Adjustments from BW Trends:**
- Aggressive deficit (>1.0%/week drop) → reduce accessory volume 25–30%; maintain primary lift frequency + intensity; verify protein intake.
- Stalled mass gain (surplus confirmed, weight not rising) → add 100–200 kcal/day from carbohydrate; reassess 7-day rolling average after 10 days.

**False Positive Guards:**
- 1–2 kg swing in 24 h = normal; no training implication.
- Female athletes: 1–3 kg cycle-phase variation; track cycle phase alongside BW data.
- High-carb refeed: 0.5–1.5 kg BW increase expected; do NOT flag as fat gain.

---

## 22. Sleep, Stress & Recovery Signal Routing

**PRINCIPLE:** Sleep and psychological stress are the two primary inputs determining nervous system readiness; treating them as secondary is a coaching error with direct performance and injury-risk consequences. (Art. 100)

**Definitions (internal):**
- Sleep categories: A (adequate), B (mildly compromised), C (significantly compromised), D (severe disruption)
- Stress levels: Low (1–4), Moderate (5–7), High (8–10)

**Sleep Category Thresholds:**
- **Category A (No Action):** total sleep ≥ 7 h; self-reported quality ≥ 3/5 → proceed as programmed.
- **Category B (Monitor):** total sleep 5.5–7 h OR quality 2/5 with adequate duration (single night) → cap RPE ceiling +5%; no new PRs/maximal efforts.
- **Category C (Modify Session):** total sleep <5.5 h OR quality 1/5 OR two consecutive Category B nights → reduce working set volume 20–25%; replace top sets with submaximal 70–75% of planned intensity; keep all movements.
- **Category D (Recovery Session):** total sleep <4 h OR ≥ 3 consecutive nights <6 h → shift to recovery session: technique work only; no loads above 70% 1RM; no compound movements to failure. IF also HRV >15% below baseline → consider rest day with active recovery only.

**Consecutive Night Rules:**
- 2 consecutive Category B nights → treat as Category C.
- 3 consecutive Category C nights → treat as Category D.

**Stress Level Routing:**
- Low (1–4): normal session; no modification.
- Moderate (5–7): avoid maximal efforts requiring complete attentional focus; maintain working sets but shift top sets 5–10% below planned max.
- High (8–10): treat as equivalent to poor sleep Category C for volume + intensity modification; no technical skill acquisition; keep session with familiar loading + controlled environment.

**Combined Routing Matrix:**
| Sleep Category | Stress Level | Session Protocol |
|----------------|-------------|-----------------|
| A (adequate) | Low | Proceed as programmed |
| A (adequate) | Moderate | Proceed; cap max effort |
| A (adequate) | High | Reduce intensity 5–10%; no max effort |
| B (mild) | Low | Monitor; apply RPE ceiling |
| B (mild) | Moderate | Reduce volume 15%; no PRs |
| B (mild) | High | Reduce volume 20–25%; no top sets |
| C (significant) | Any | Modified session; 20–25% volume cut |
| D (severe) | Any | Recovery session protocol |
| Any | 8–10 + HRV drop | Recovery session protocol |

**Additional Recovery Markers:**
- Appetite drop in athlete in caloric surplus → underrated early recovery signal (often precedes HRV drop by 24–48 h).
- Consistent motivation decline over 7–14 days → systemic recovery signal; if combined with HRV depression + performance drop → confirms accumulated fatigue.
- Recovery time between sessions extended (>72 h where previously 48 h) → direct volume or frequency adjustment signal.

---

## 23. Pain, Soreness & Local Tissue Feedback Scoring

**PRINCIPLE:** Soreness and pain are categorically different phenomena; soreness is a training signal; pain is a tissue integrity signal requiring assessment before next loading decision; never test a pain signal with a heavy set. (Art. 101)

**Definitions (internal):**

**Soreness vs. Pain Differential:**
| Feature | Soreness (DOMS) | Pain (Tissue Signal) |
|---------|----------------|---------------------|
| Onset | 12–48 h post-session | During or immediately after session |
| Location | Muscle belly, diffuse | Joint, tendon, or localized spot |
| Bilateral? | Often bilateral | Usually unilateral |
| Worsens with load? | Warm-up reduces it | Worsens or does not improve |
| Resolves in 48–72 h? | Yes, without intervention | Not on DOMS timeline |
| Radiates? | No | Possible (especially if neural) |

**Soreness Scoring System:**
- **Score 1 (Minimal):** no soreness at rest; slight awareness during warm-up that clears in 5–10 min. → Train as programmed.
- **Score 2 (Mild):** soreness at rest/everyday movement; clears during warm-up; some initial performance decrement normalizing by working sets. → No modification needed unless combined with other flags.
- **Score 3 (Moderate):** soreness present throughout session, does not fully clear in warm-up; performance at target muscle group 5–10% below expected. → Reduce working sets by 1; maintain intensity.
- **Score 4 (Significant):** soreness limiting full ROM or >10% performance reduction. → Reduce volume 30–40% at affected region; do not add new soreness stimulus to same area; allow 24–48 additional hours before re-testing.
- **Score 5 (Severe):** cannot perform target movements at reasonable load without significant discomfort. → Remove affected movement pattern from session; reassess within 24 h; if not significantly resolved, treat as pain signal.

**Pain Scoring (Traffic Light):**
- **Green (Train Through):** familiar ache, assessed + cleared; no worsening with warm-up; full ROM without guarding; no radiation. → Train as programmed; monitor.
- **Yellow (Modify + Monitor):** pain 2–3/10 VAS; does not worsen with controlled loading; localized, no radiation; previously assessed + classified manageable. → Remove specific aggravating loading pattern; find substitution; reassess next session.
- **Orange (Assess Before Training):** pain 4–5/10 OR present at rest OR worsening under load OR new onset within 24–48 h OR joint-based OR audible event. → Do not load region; train around it; refer for physio/medical before full loading resumes.
- **Red (Stop + Refer):** pain ≥ 6/10 OR radiating/neurological symptoms (numbness, tingling, weakness distally) OR sharp pain forcing stop mid-set OR swelling/bruising/instability at joint. → End session for affected region; refer for medical evaluation; do not resume loading until clinician-cleared.

**Soreness-Adjusted Training Rules (compact):**
- Score 1–2 → no modification.
- Score 3 → reduce sets by 1, maintain intensity.
- Score 4 → reduce volume 30–40%.
- Score 5 with no resolution during warm-up → remove movement; reassess 24 h.

**Critical Rule:** Any pain above Yellow classification = remove the aggravating pattern. Never test pain with a heavy set.

---

## 24. Coach Dashboard Logic — Weekly Data → Program Decisions

**PRINCIPLE:** The dashboard is a decision engine, not a reporting tool; every data point must connect to a decision; weekly review (15–30 min) ends with a written program adjustment record or explicit written confirmation of no adjustment. (Art. 102)

**Dashboard Input Categories (Weekly Review Checklist):**

*Performance Metrics (Primary):*
- Working set completion rate
- Top set output vs. target
- Bar speed / velocity data (if available)
- Volume completed vs. prescribed

*Readiness Metrics:*
- HRV: daily readings, 7-day average vs. 30-day baseline, trend direction
- SRS: average across training days, any days below 5
- Sleep: average duration, any nights <6 h, consecutive flag count
- Stress: daily ratings, any days above 7 or 9

*Body Metrics:*
- BW 7-day rolling average vs. prior week
- Rate of change (%/week)
- Body composition update if measurement week

*Pain + Soreness:*
- Any Orange or Red pain flags
- Soreness scores by region
- Movement modifications applied + rationale

*Compliance:*
- Session attendance
- Nutrition log compliance
- Significant life events reported

**5-Step Review Sequence:**

**Step 1 — Red Flag Scan:**
Check for: any Red pain flag; any session missed due to illness/injury/crisis; HRV sustained <85% of baseline for 5+ days; SRS average <5 across training days. → If any TRUE → program response is predetermined.

**Step 2 — Performance Trend Assessment:**
- Athlete completed >90% of prescribed volume?
- Top sets at/above target?
- Performance trending up / flat / down vs. prior 3-week window?
- IF downward → apply 4-cause classification (Art. 98).

**Step 3 — Readiness Trend Assessment:**
- HRV direction this week?
- High-stress days affecting session quality?
- Sleep a limiting variable?
- Assign readiness status for next week: Green (full program) / Yellow (monitor, no advancement) / Red (load reduction or deload).

**Step 4 — Body Metrics Integration:**
- BW trend aligned with stated phase goal?
- Flag discrepancies between weight trend and performance trend.

**Step 5 — Decision Synthesis + Record:**
Write one decision from A–F:

| Decision | Condition | Action |
|----------|-----------|--------|
| A — Continue as Programmed | All signals normal, performance progressing, readiness adequate | No change |
| B — Load Advancement | Performance above target ≥ 2 weeks; readiness Green | Apply planned progression |
| C — Load Hold | Performance flat with adequate readiness | Maintain current Rx 1 more week; add diagnostic session if needed |
| D — Volume/Intensity Reduction | Readiness flagged by Tier 1 or confirmed Tier 2 | Apply relevant reduction; document trigger + reduction applied |
| E — Deload | Accumulated fatigue confirmed, performance declining, HRV suppressed | Apply formal deload protocol |
| F — Block Redesign | Program error confirmed or goals shifted | Rebuild block from training hypothesis; document what prior block achieved + new hypothesis |

**Weekly Review Record Format (required fields):**
Week ending date | Athlete | Review status (Green/Yellow/Red) | Performance summary | Readiness summary | Body metrics | Pain/soreness flags | Decision type (A–F) | Specific action | Next week prescription | Follow-up items

**Automation Alerts (threshold-based):**
- HRV <88% of rolling average for 3+ consecutive days
- SRS ≤ 4 on any session day
- BW change >1.5% in either direction in one week
- Session completion <80%
- Any Orange or Red pain flag
- No data entry for 48+ h on a scheduled session day

**Rule:** Alerts surface exceptions. The coach provides interpretation and decision. Alerts do not make decisions.

---

## Cross-Cluster Integration Notes (Art. 79–102)

**Cluster J (Art. 79–84) feeds:**
- Cluster M (Art. 102): check-in data from Art. 84 = primary input to weekly dashboard review.
- Cluster L (Art. 91–96): block handoff (Art. 84 Step 5) = transition into competition-cycle logic.

**Cluster K (Art. 85–90) — state assignments feed:**
- Cluster L: competition proximity is a primary input to Art. 90 state matrix; Cluster K manages sport-gym interference leading into Cluster L taper.
- Cluster H: weight-cut override + caloric deficit cap interact with weight-class management.

**Cluster L (Art. 91–96) feeds:**
- Cluster J: post-competition transition (Art. 96) re-enters stateful coaching mode; next-block selection triggers new program generation.
- Cluster M: readiness signals during taper/competition week interpreted through Cluster M hierarchy.

**Cluster M (Art. 97–102) — modifier of all upstream prescriptions:**
- Cluster M does not generate prescriptions from scratch; it modifies output from all upstream clusters based on incoming athlete data.
- Four-cause performance drop (Art. 98) maps to Cluster G's failure-mode framework (below MEV / above MRV / skill ceiling / program error).
- Art. 90 Push/Maintain/Reduce/Deload states = sport-contextualized expression of Cluster G's AR tier system (Green/Amber/Red/Black).

**Five Integration Principles (governing whole system):**
1. Sport load counted toward every shared threshold (mat hours, sparring, conditioning density all added to gym ledger before prescribing gym volume).
2. The most constrained channel governs — never plan to average reserve while one channel is overdrawn.
3. Maintenance is a legitimate strategic dose (qualities hold 2–3 weeks at ~MEV; holding is not failure).
4. Substitution before cancellation — substitute to lower-cost variant; do not cancel session.
5. Language discipline: all guidance is load management, capacity building, tolerance development — no medical claims, no injury-prevention guarantees.
